THE YELLOW FAIRY BOOK THE CAT AND THE MOUSE IN PARTNERSHIP A cat have make acquaintance with a mouse , and have speak so much of the great love and friendship she felt for her , that at last the Mouse consent to live in the same house with her , and to go share in the housekeeping .
` But we must provide for the winter or else we shall suffer hunger , ' say the Cat .
` You , little Mouse , can not venture everywhere in case you run at last into a trap . '
This good counsel be follow , and a little pot of fat be buy .
But they do not know where to put it .
At length , after long consultation , the Cat say , ' I know of no place where it could be good put than in the church .
No one will trouble to take it away from there .
We will hide it in a corner , and we wo n't touch it till we be in want . '
So the little pot be place in safety ; but it be not long before the Cat have a great longing for it , and say to the Mouse , ' I want to tell you , little Mouse , that my cousin have a little son , white with brown spot , and she want me to be godmother to it .
Let me go out to-day , and do you take care of the house alone . '
` Yes , go certainly , ' reply the Mouse , ` and when you eat anything good , think of me ; I should very much like a drop of the red christening wine . '
But it be all untrue .
The Cat have no cousin , and have not be ask to be godmother .
She go straight to the church , slunk to the little pot of fat , begin to lick it , and lick the top off .
Then she take a walk on the roof of the town , look at the view , stretch herself out in the sun , and lick her lip whenever she think of the little pot of fat .
As soon a it be even she go home again .
` Ah , here you be again ! '
say the Mouse ; ` you must certainly have have an enjoyable day . '
` It go off very well , ' answer the Cat .
` What be the child 's name ? '
ask the Mouse .
` Top Off , ' say the Cat drily .
` Topoff ! '
echo the Mouse , ` it be indeed a wonderful and curious name .
Is it in your family ? '
` What be there odd about it ? '
say the Cat .
` It be not bad than Breadthief , a your godchild be call . '
Not long after this another great longing come over the Cat .
She say to the Mouse , ` You must again be kind enough to look after the house alone , for I have be ask a second time to stand godmother , and a this child have a white ring round it neck , I can not refuse . '
The kind Mouse agree , but the Cat slunk under the town wall to the church , and eat up half of the pot of fat .
` Nothing taste well , ' say she , ` than what one eats by oneself , ' and she be very much pleased with her day 's work .
When she come home the Mouse ask , ` What be this child call ? '
` Half Gone , ' answer the Cat .
` Halfgone !
what a name !
I have never hear it in my life .
I do n't believe it be in the calendar . '
Soon the Cat 's mouth begin to water once more after her licking business .
` All good thing in three , ' she say to the Mouse ; ' I have again to stand godmother .
The child be quite black , and have very white paw , but not a single white hair on it body .
This only happen once in two year , so you will let me go out ? '
` Topoff !
Halfgone ! '
repeat the Mouse , ` they be such curious name ; they make me very thoughtful . '
` Oh , you sit at home in your dark grey coat and your long tail , ' say the Cat , ` and you get fanciful .
That come of not go out in the day . '
The Mouse have a good cleaning out while the Cat be go , and make the house tidy ; but the greedy Cat eat the fat every bit up .
` When it be all go one can be at rest , ' she say to herself , and at night she come home sleek and satisfy .
The Mouse ask at once after the third child 's name .
` It wo n't please you any good , ' say the Cat , ` he be call Clean Gone . '
` Cleangone ! '
repeat the Mouse . '
I do not believe that name have be print any more than the others .
Cleangone !
What can it mean ? '
She shake her head , curl herself up , and go to sleep .
From this time on no one ask the Cat to stand godmother ; but when the winter come and there be nothing to be get outside , the Mouse remember their provision and say , ` Come , Cat , we will go to our pot of fat which we have store away ; it will taste very good . '
` Yes , indeed , ' answer the Cat ; ` it will taste as good to you a if you stretch your thin tongue out of the window . '
They start off , and when they reach it they find the pot in it place , but quite empty !
` Ah , ' say the Mouse , ' ` now I know what have happen !
It have all come out !
You be a true friend to me !
You have eat it all when you stand godmother ; first the top off , then half of it go , then -- ' ` Will you be quiet ! '
scream the Cat .
` Another word and I will eat you up . '
` Clean-gone ' be already on the poor Mouse 's tongue , and scarcely be it out than the Cat make a spring at her , seize and swallow her .
You see that be the way of the world .
THE SIX SWANS A king be once hunt in a great wood , and he hunt the game so eagerly that none of his courtier could follow him .
When even come on he stand still and look round him , and he saw that he have quite lose himself .
He seek a way out , but could find none .
Then he saw an old woman with a shake head come towards him ; but she be a witch .
` Good woman , ' he say to her , ` can you not show me the way out of the wood ? '
` Oh , certainly , Sir King , ' she reply , ' I can quite well do that , but on one condition , which if you do not fulfil you will never get out of the wood , and will die of hunger . '
` What be the condition ? '
ask the King . '
I have a daughter , ' say the old woman , ` who be so beautiful that she have not her equal in the world , and be well fit to be your wife ; if you will make her lady-queen I will show you the way out of the wood . '
The King in his anguish of mind consent , and the old woman lead him to her little house where her daughter be sit by the fire .
She receive the King a if she be expect him , and he saw that she be certainly very beautiful ; but she do not please him , and he could not look at her without a secret feeling of horror .
As soon a he have lift the maiden on to his horse the old woman show him the way , and the King reach his palace , where the wedding be celebrate .
The King have already be marry once , and have by his first wife seven child , six boy and one girl , whom he love more than anything in the world .
And now , because he be afraid that their stepmother might not treat them well and might do them harm , he put them in a lonely castle that stand in the middle of a wood .
It lay so hidden , and the way to it be so hard to find , that he himself could not have find it out have not a wise-woman give him a reel of thread which possess a marvellous property : when he throw it before him it unwind itself and show him the way .
But the King go so often to his dear child that the Queen be offend at his absence .
She grow curious , and want to know what he have to do quite alone in the wood .
She give his servant a great deal of money , and they betray the secret to her , and also tell her of the reel which alone could point out the way .
She have no rest now till she have find out where the King guard the reel , and then she make some little white shirt , and , a she have learnt from her witch-mother , sew an enchantment in each of them .
And when the King have ride off she take the little shirt and go into the wood , and the reel show her the way .
The child , who saw someone come in the distance , think it be their dear father come to them , and sprang to meet him very joyfully .
Then she throw over each one a little shirt , which when it have touch their body change them into swan , and they fly away over the forest .
The Queen go home quite satisfied , and think she have get rid of her step-children ; but the girl have not run to meet her with her brother , and she know nothing of her .
The next day the King come to visit his child , but he find no one but the girl .
` Where be your brother ? '
ask the King .
` Alas !
dear father , ' she answer , ` they have go away and leave me all alone . '
And she tell him that look out of her little window she have see her brother fly over the wood in the shape of swan , and she show him the feather which they have let fall in the yard , and which she have collect .
The King mourn , but he do not think that the Queen have do the wicked deed , and a he be afraid the maiden would also be take from him , he want to take her with him .
But she be afraid of the stepmother , and beg the King to let her stay just one night more in the castle in the wood .
The poor maiden thought , ` My home be no longer here ; I will go and seek my brother . '
And when night come she flee away into the forest .
She run all through the night and the next day , till she could go no farther for weariness .
Then she saw a little hut , go in , and find a room with six little bed .
She be afraid to lie down on one , so she creep under one of them , lay on the hard floor , and be go to spend the night there .
But when the sun have set she hear a noise , and saw six swan fly in at the window .
They stand on the floor and blew at one another , and blow all their feather off , and their swan-skin come off like a shirt .
Then the maiden recognise her brother , and overjoy she creep out from under the bed .
Her brother be not less delighted than she to see their little sister again , but their joy do not last long .
` You can not stay here , ' they say to her .
` This be a den of robber ; if they be to come here and find you they would kill you . '
` Could you not protect me ? '
ask the little sister .
` No , ' they answer , ` for we can only lay aside our swan skin for a quarter of an hour every evening .
For this time we regain our human form , but then we be change into swan again . '
Then the little sister cry and say , ` Can you not be free ? '
` Oh , no , ' they say , ` the condition be too hard .
You must not speak or laugh for six year , and must make in that time six shirt for u out of star-flowers .
If a single word come out of your mouth , all your labour be vain . '
And when the brother have say this the quarter of an hour come to an end , and they fly away out of the window a swan .
But the maiden have determine to free her brother even if it should cost her her life .
She leave the hut , go into the forest , climb a tree , and spend the night there .
The next morning she go out , collect star-flowers , and begin to sew .
She could speak to no one , and she have no wish to laugh , so she sit there , look only at her work .
When she have live there some time , it happen that the King of the country be hunt in the forest , and his hunter come to the tree on which the maiden sat .
They call to her and say ` Who be you ? '
But she give no answer .
` Come down to u , ' they say , ` we will do you no harm . '
But she shake her head silently .
As they press her further with question , she throw them the golden chain from her neck .
But they do not leave off , and she throw them her girdle , and when this be no use , her garter , and then her dress .
The huntsman would not leave her alone , but climb the tree , lift the maiden down , and lead her to the King .
The King ask , ` Who be you ?
What be you do up that tree ? '
But she answer nothing .
He ask her in all the language he know , but she remain as dumb a a fish .
Because she be so beautiful , however , the King 's heart be touch , and he be seize with a great love for her .
He wrap her up in his cloak , place her before him on his horse , and bring her to his castle .
There he have her dress in rich clothes , and her beauty shone out as bright a day , but not a word could be draw from her .
He set her at table by his side , and her modest way and behaviour please him so much that he say , ' I will marry this maiden and none other in the world , ' and after some day he marry her .
But the King have a wicked mother who be displease with the marriage , and say wicked thing of the young Queen .
` Who know who this girl be ? '
she say ; ` she can not speak , and be not worthy of a king . '
After a year , when the Queen have her first child , the old mother take it away from her .
Then she go to the King and say that the Queen have kill it .
The King would not believe it , and would not allow any harm to be do her .
But she sit quietly sew at the shirt and trouble herself about nothing .
The next time she have a child the wicked mother do the same thing , but the King could not make up his mind to believe her .
He say , ` She be too sweet and good to do such a thing a that .
If she be not dumb and could defend herself , her innocence would be prove . '
But when the third child be take away , and the Queen be again accuse , and could not utter a word in her own defence , the King be oblige to give her over to the law , which decree that she must be burn to death .
When the day come on which the sentence be to be execute , it be the last day of the six year in which she must not speak or laugh , and now she have free her dear brother from the power of the enchantment .
The six shirt be do ; there be only the left sleeve want to the last .
When she be lead to the stake , she lay the shirt on her arm , and a she stand on the pile and the fire be about to be light , she look around her and saw six swan fly through the air .
Then she know that her release be at hand and her heart dance for joy .
The swan flutter round her , and hover low so that she could throw the shirt over them .
When they have touch them the swan-skins fell off , and her brother stand before her living , well and beautiful .
Only the young have a swan 's wing instead of his left arm .
They embrace and kiss each other , and the Queen go to the King , who be stand by in great astonishment , and begin to speak to him , say , ` Dearest husband , now I can speak and tell you openly that I be innocent and have be falsely accuse . '
She tell him of the old woman 's deceit , and how she have take the three child away and hide them .
Then they be fetch , to the great joy of the King , and the wicked mother come to no good end .
But the King and the Queen with their six brother live many year in happiness and peace .
THE DRAGON OF THE NORTH -LRB- 2 -RRB- -LRB- 2 -RRB- ` Der Norlands Drache , ' from Esthnische Mahrchen .
Kreutzwald .
Very long ago , a old people have tell me , there live a terrible monster , who come out of the North , and lay waste whole tract of country , devour both men and beast ; and this monster be so destructive that it be fear that unless help come no living creature would be leave on the face of the earth .
It have a body like an ox , and leg like a frog , two short fore-legs , and two long one behind , and besides that it have a tail like a serpent , ten fathom in length .
When it move it jump like a frog , and with every spring it cover half a mile of ground .
Fortunately it habit , be to remain for several year in the same place , and not to move on till the whole neighbourhood be eat up .
Nothing could hunt it , because it whole body be cover with scale , which be hard than stone or metal ; it two great eye shone by night , and even by day , like the bright lamp , and anyone who have the ill luck to look into those eye become a it be bewitch , and be oblige to rush of his own accord into the monster 's jaw .
In this way the Dragon be able to fee upon both men and beast without the least trouble to itself , a it need not to move from the spot where it be lie .
All the neighbouring king have offer rich reward to anyone who should be able to destroy the monster , either by force or enchantment , and many have try their luck , but all have miserably fail .
Once a great forest in which the Dragon lay have be set on fire ; the forest be burnt down , but the fire do not do the monster the least harm .
However , there be a tradition amongst the wise men of the country that the Dragon might be overcome by one who possess King Solomon 's signet-ring , upon which a secret writing be engrave .
This inscription would enable anyone who be wise enough to interpret it to find out how the Dragon could be destroy .
Only no one know where the ring be hide , nor be there any sorcerer or learn man to be find who would be able to explain the inscription .
At last a young man , with a good heart and plenty of courage , set out to search for the ring .
He take his way towards the sunrising , because he know that all the wisdom of old time come from the East .
After some year he meet with a famous Eastern magician , and ask for his advice in the matter .
The magician answered : ` Mortal men have but little wisdom , and can give you no help , but the bird of the air would be good guide to you if you could learn their language .
I can help you to understand it if you will stay with me a few day . '
The youth thankfully accept the magician 's offer , and say , ' I can not now offer you any reward for your kindness , but should my undertake succeed your trouble shall be richly repay . '
Then the magician brew a powerful potion out of nine sort of herb which he have gather himself all alone by moonlight , and he give the youth nine spoonful of it daily for three day , which make him able to understand the language of bird .
At part the magician say to him .
` If you ever find Solomon 's ring and get possession of it , then come back to me , that I may explain the inscription on the ring to you , for there be no one else in the world who can do this . '
From that time the youth never felt lonely a he walk along ; he always have company , because he understand the language of bird ; and in this way he learn many thing which mere human knowledge could never have teach him .
But time go on , and he hear nothing about the ring .
It happen one evening , when he be hot and tired with walking , and have sit down under a tree in a forest to eat his supper , that he saw two gaily-plumaged bird , that be strange to him , sit at the top of the tree talk to one another about him .
The first bird say : ' I know that wander fool under the tree there , who have come so far without find what he seek .
He be try to find King Solomon 's lose ring . '
The other bird answer , ` He will have to seek help from the Witch-maiden , -LRB- 3 -RRB- who will doubtless be able to put him on the right track .
If she have not get the ring herself , she know well enough who have it . '
-LRB- 3 -RRB- Hollenmadchen .
` But where be he to find the Witch-maiden ? '
say the first bird .
` She have no settle dwelling , but be here to-day and go to-morrow .
He might as well try to catch the wind . '
The other reply , ' I do not know , certainly , where she be at present , but in three night from now she will come to the spring to wash her face , a she do every month when the moon be full , in order that she may never grow old nor wrinkled , but may always keep the bloom of youth . '
` Well , ' say the first bird , ` the spring be not far from here .
Shall we go and see how it be she do it ? '
` Willingly , if you like , ' say the other .
The youth immediately resolve to follow the bird to the spring , only two thing make him uneasy : first , l he might be asleep when the bird go , and secondly , l he might lose sight of them , since he have not wing to carry him along so swiftly .
He be too tired to keep awake all night , yet his anxiety prevent him from sleep soundly , and when with the early dawn he look up to the tree-top , he be glad to see his feathered companion still asleep with their head under their wing .
He eat his breakfast , and wait until the bird should start , but they do not leave the place all day .
They hop about from one tree to another look for food , all day long until the evening , when they go back to their old perch to sleep .
The next day the same thing happen , but on the third morning one bird say to the other , ` To-day we must go to the spring to see the Witch-maiden wash her face . '
They remain on the tree till noon ; then they fly away and go towards the south .
The young man 's heart beat with anxiety lest he should lose sight of his guide , but he manage to keep the bird in view until they again perch upon a tree .
The young man run after them until he be quite exhaust and out of breath , and after three short rest the bird at length reach a small open space in the forest , on the edge of which they place themselves on the top of a high tree .
When the youth have overtake them , he saw that there be a clear spring in the middle of the space .
He sit down at the foot of the tree upon which the bird be perch , and listen attentively to what they be say to each other .
` The sun be not down yet , ' say the first bird ; ` we must wait yet awhile till the moon rise and the maiden come to the spring .
Do you think she will see that young man sit under the tree ? '
` Nothing be likely to escape her eye , certainly not a young man , say the other bird .
` Will the youth have the sense not to let himself be catch in her toil ? '
` We will wait , ' say the first bird , ` and see how they get on together . '
The evening light have quite fade , and the full moon be already shin down upon the forest , when the young man hear a slight rustling sound .
After a few moment there come out of the forest a maiden , glide over the grass so lightly that her foot seem scarcely to touch the ground , and stand beside the spring .
The youth could not turn away his eye from the maiden , for he have never in his life see a woman so beautiful .
Without seem to notice anything , she go to the spring , look up to the full moon , then kneel down and bath her face nine time , then look up to the moon again and walk nine time round the well , and a she walk she sing this song : ` Full-faced moon with light unshaded , Let my beauty ne'er be fade .
Never let my cheek grow pale !
While the moon be wan nightly , May the maiden bloom more brightly , May her freshness never fail ! '
Then she dry her face with her long hair , and be about to go away , when her eye suddenly fell upon the spot where the young man be sit , and she turn towards the tree .
The youth rise and stand wait .
Then the maiden say , ` You ought to have a heavy punishment because you have presume to watch my secret doings in the moonlight .
But I will forgive you this time , because you be a stranger and know no good .
But you must tell me truly who you be and how you come to this place , where no mortal have ever set foot before . '
The youth answer humbly : ` Forgive me , beautiful maiden , if I have unintentionally offend you .
I chance to come here after long wandering , and find a good place to sleep under this tree .
At your come I do not know what to do , but stay where I be , because I think my silent watching could not offend you . '
The maiden answer kindly , ` Come and spend this night with u .
You will sleep good on a pillow than on damp moss . '
The youth hesitate for a little , but presently he hear the bird say from the top of the tree , ` Go where she call you , but take care to give no blood , or you will sell your soul . '
So the youth go with her , and soon they reach a beautiful garden , where stand a splendid house , which glitter in the moonlight a if it be all build out of gold and silver .
When the youth enter he find many splendid chamber , each one fine than the last .
Hundreds of taper burn upon golden candlestick , and shed a light like the bright day .
At length they reach a chamber where a table be spread with the most costly dish .
At the table be place two chair , one of silver , the other of gold .
The maiden seat herself upon the golden chair , and offer the silver one to her companion .
They be serve by maiden dress in white , whose foot make no sound a they move about , and not a word be speak during the meal .
Afterwards the youth and the Witch-maiden converse pleasantly together , until a woman , dress in red , come in to remind them that it be bedtime .
The youth be now show into another room , contain a silken bed with down cushion , where he sleep delightfully , yet he seem to hear a voice near his bed which repeat to him , ` Remember to give no blood ! '
The next morning the maiden ask him whether he would not like to stay with her always in this beautiful place , and a he do not answer immediately , she continue : ` You see how I always remain young and beautiful , and I be under no one 's order , but can do just what I like , so that I have never think of marry before .
But from the moment I saw you I take a fancy to you , so if you agree , we might be marry and might live together like prince , because I have great rich . '
The youth could not but be tempt with the beautiful maiden 's offer , but he remember how the bird have call her the witch , and their warning always sound in his ear .
Therefore he answer cautiously , ` Do not be angry , dear maiden , if I do not decide immediately on this important matter .
Give me a few day to consider before we come to an understanding . '
` Why not ? '
answer the maiden .
` Take some week to consider if you like , and take counsel with your own heart . '
And to make the time pas pleasantly , she take the youth over every part of her beautiful dwelling , and show him all her splendid treasure .
But these treasure be all produce by enchantment , for the maiden could make anything she wish appear by the help of King Solomon 's signet ring ; only none of these thing remain fix ; they pass away like the wind without leave a trace behind .
But the youth do not know this ; he think they be all real .
One day the maiden take him into a secret chamber , where a little gold box be stand on a silver table .
Pointing to the box , she say , ` Here be my great treasure , whose like be not to be find in the whole world .
It be a precious gold ring .
When you marry me , I will give you this ring a a marriage gift , and it will make you the happy of mortal men .
But in order that our love may last for ever , you must give me for the ring three drop of blood from the little finger of your left hand . '
When the youth heard these word a cold shudder run over him , for he remember that his soul be at stake .
He be cunning enough , however , to conceal his feeling and to make no direct answer , but he only ask the maiden , a if carelessly , what be remarkable about the ring ?
She answer , ` No mortal be able entirely to understand the power of this ring , because no one thoroughly understand the secret sign engrave upon it .
But even with my half-knowledge I can work great wonder .
If I put the ring upon the little finger of my left hand , then I can fly like a bird through the air wherever I wish to go .
If I put it on the third finger of my left hand I be invisible , and I can see everything that pass around me , though no one can see me .
If I put the ring upon the middle finger of my left hand , then neither fire nor water nor any sharp weapon can hurt me .
If I put it on the forefinger of my left hand , then I can with it help produce whatever I wish .
I can in a single moment build house or anything I desire .
Finally , as long a I wear the ring on the thumb of my left hand , that hand be so strong that it can break down rock and wall .
Besides these , the ring have other secret sign which , a I say , no one can understand .
No doubt it contain secret of great importance .
The ring formerly belong to King Solomon , the wise of king , during whose reign the wise men live .
But it be not know whether this ring be ever make by mortal hand : it be suppose that an angel give it to the wise King . '
When the youth heard all this he determine to try and get possession of the ring , though he do not quite believe in all it wonderful gift .
He wish the maiden would let him have it in his hand , but he do not quite like to ask her to do so , and after a while she put it back into the box .
A few day after they be again speak of the magic ring , and the youth say , ' I do not think it possible that the ring can have all the power you say it have . '
Then the maiden open the box and take the ring out , and it glitter a she hold it like the clear sunbeam .
She put it on the middle finger of her left hand , and tell the youth to take a knife and try as hard a he could to cut her with it , for he would not be able to hurt her .
He be unwilling at first , but the maiden insist .
Then he try , at first only in play , and then seriously , to strike her with the knife , but an invisible wall of iron seem to be between them , and the maiden stood before him laugh and unhurt .
Then she put the ring on her third finger , and in an instant she have vanish from his eye .
Presently she be beside him again laughing , and hold the ring between her finger .
` Do let me try , ' say the youth , ` whether I can do these wonderful thing . '
The maiden , suspect no treachery , give him the magic ring .
The youth pretend to have forget what to do , and ask what finger he must put the ring on so that no sharp weapon could hurt him ? '
` Oh , the middle finger of your left hand , ' the maiden answer , laugh .
She take the knife and try to strike the youth , and he even try to cut himself with it , but find it impossible .
Then he ask the maiden to show him how to split stone and rock with the help of the ring .
So she lead him into a courtyard where stand a great boulder-stone .
` Now , ' she say , ` put the ring upon the thumb of your left hand , and you will see how strong that hand have become .
The youth do so , and find to his astonishment that with a single blow of his fist the stone fly into a thousand piece .
Then the youth bethink him that he who do not use his luck when he have it be a fool , and that this be a chance which once lose might never return .
So while they stand laugh at the shattered stone he place the ring , a if in play , upon the third finger of his left hand .
` Now , ' say the maiden , ` you be invisible to me until you take the ring off again . '
But the youth have no mind to do that ; on the contrary , he go far off , then put the ring on the little finger of his left hand , and soar into the air like a bird .
When the maiden saw him fly away she think at first that he be still in play , and cry , ` Come back , friend , for now you see I have tell you the truth . '
But the young man never come back .
Then the maiden saw she be deceive , and bitterly repent that she have ever trust him with the ring .
The young man never halt in his flight until he reach the dwelling of the wise magician who have teach him the speech of bird .
The magician be delight to find that his search have be successful , and at once set to work to interpret the secret sign engrave upon the ring , but it take him seven week to make them out clearly .
Then he give the youth the following instruction how to overcome the Dragon of the North : ` You must have an iron horse cast , which must have little wheel under each foot .
You must also be arm with a spear two fathom long , which you will be able to wield by mean of the magic ring upon your left thumb .
The spear must be a thick in the middle a a large tree , and both it end must be sharp .
In the middle of the spear you must have two strong chain ten fathom in length .
As soon a the Dragon have make himself fast to the spear , which you must thrust through his jaw , you must spring quickly from the iron horse and fasten the end of the chain firmly to the ground with iron stake , so that he can not get away from them .
After two or three day the monster 's strength will be so far exhaust that you will be able to come near him .
Then you can put Solomon 's ring upon your left thumb and give him the finishing stroke , but keep the ring on your third finger until you have come close to him , so that the monster can not see you , else he might strike you dead with his long tail .
But when all be do , take care you do not lose the ring , and that no one take it from you by cunning . '
The young man thank the magician for his direction , and promise , should they succeed , to reward him .
But the magician answer , ' I have profit so much by the wisdom the ring have teach me that I desire no other reward . '
Then they part , and the youth quickly fly home through the air .
After remain in his own home for some week , he hear people say that the terrible Dragon of the North be not far off , and might shortly be expect in the country .
The King announce publicly that he would give his daughter in marriage , as well a a large part of his kingdom , to whosoever should free the country from the monster .
The youth then go to the King and tell him that he have good hope of subdue the Dragon , if the King would grant him all he desire for the purpose .
The King willingly agree , and the iron horse , the great spear , and the chain be all prepare a the youth request .
When all be ready , it be find that the iron horse be so heavy that a hundred men could not move it from the spot , so the youth find there be nothing for it but to move it with his own strength by mean of the magic ring .
The Dragon be now so near that in a couple of spring he would be over the frontier .
The youth now begin to consider how he should act , for if he have to push the iron horse from behind he could not ride upon it a the sorcerer have say he must .
But a raven unexpectedly give him this advice : ` Ride upon the horse , and push the spear against the ground , a if you be push off a boat from the land . '
The youth do so , and find that in this way he could easily move forward .
The Dragon have his monstrous jaw wide open , all ready for his expect prey .
A few pace nearer , and man and horse would have be swallow up by them !
The youth tremble with horror , and his blood run cold , yet he do not lose his courage ; but , hold the iron spear upright in his hand , he bring it down with all his might right through the monster 's low jaw .
Then quick a lightning he spring from his horse before the Dragon have time to shut his mouth .
A fearful clap like thunder , which could be hear for mile around , now warn him that the Dragon 's jaw have close upon the spear .
When the youth turn round he saw the point of the spear stick up high above the Dragon 's upper jaw , and know that the other end must be fasten firmly to the ground ; but the Dragon have get his teeth fix in the iron horse , which be now useless .
The youth now hasten to fasten down the chain to the ground by mean of the enormous iron peg which he have provide .
The death struggle of the monster last three day and three night ; in his writhing he beat his tail so violently against the ground , that at ten mile ' distance the earth tremble a if with an earthquake .
When he at length lose power to move his tail , the youth with the help of the ring take up a stone which twenty ordinary men could not have move , and beat the Dragon so hard about the head with it that very soon the monster lay lifeless before him .
You can fancy how great be the rejoicing when the news be spread abroad that the terrible monster be dead .
His conqueror be receive into the city with as much pomp a if he have be the mighty of king .
The old King do not need to urge his daughter to marry the slayer of the Dragon ; he find her already willing to bestow her hand upon this hero , who have do all alone what whole army have try in vain to do .
In a few day a magnificent wedding be celebrate , at which the rejoicing last four whole week , for all the neighbouring king have meet together to thank the man who have free the world from their common enemy .
But everyone forget amid the general joy that they ought to have bury the Dragon 's monstrous body , for it begin now to have such a bad smell that no one could live in the neighbourhood , and before long the whole air be poison , and a pestilence break out which destroy many hundred of people .
In this distress , the King 's son-in-law resolve to seek help once more from the Eastern magician , to whom he at once travel through the air like a bird by the help of the ring .
But there be a proverb which say that ill-gotten gain never prosper , and the Prince find that the steal ring bring him ill-luck after all .
The Witch-maiden have never rest night nor day until she have find out where the ring be .
As soon a she have discover by mean of magical art that the Prince in the form of a bird be on his way to the Eastern magician , she change herself into an eagle and watch in the air until the bird she be wait for come in sight , for she know him at once by the ring which be hung round his neck by a ribbon .
Then the eagle pounce upon the bird , and the moment she seize him in her talon she tear the ring from his neck before the man in bird 's shape have time to prevent her .
Then the eagle fly down to the earth with her prey , and the two stand face to face once more in human form .
` Now , villain , you be in my power ! '
cry the Witch-maiden . '
I favour you with my love , and you repay me with treachery and theft .
You steal my most precious jewel from me , and do you expect to live happily a the King 's son-in-law ?
Now the table be turn ; you be in my power , and I will be revenge on you for your crime . '
` Forgive me !
forgive me ! '
cry the Prince ; ' I know too well how deeply I have wrong you , and most heartily do I repent it . '
The maiden answer , ` Your prayer and your repentance come too late , and if I be to spare you everyone would think me a fool .
You have doubly wrong me ; first you scorn my love , and then you steal my ring , and you must bear the punishment . '
With these word she put the ring upon her left thumb , lift the young man with one hand , and walk away with him under her arm .
This time she do not take him to a splendid palace , but to a deep cave in a rock , where there be chain hang from the wall .
The maiden now chain the young man 's hand and foot so that he could not escape ; then she say in an angry voice , ` Here you shall remain chain up until you die .
I will bring you every day enough food to prevent you die of hunger , but you need never hope for freedom any more . '
With these word she leave him .
The old King and his daughter wait anxiously for many week for the Prince 's return , but no news of him arrive .
The King 's daughter often dream that her husband be go through some great suffering : she therefore beg her father to summon all the enchanter and magician , that they might try to find out where the Prince be and how he could be set free .
But the magician , with all their art , could find out nothing , except that he be still live and undergoing great suffering ; but none could tell where he be to be find .
At last a celebrated magician from Finland be bring before the King , who have find out that the King 's son-in-law be imprison in the East , not by men , but by some more powerful be .
The King now send messenger to the East to look for his son-in-law , and they by good luck meet with the old magician who have interpret the sign on King Solomon 's ring , and thus be possess of more wisdom than anyone else in the world .
The magician soon find out what he wish to know , and point out the place where the Prince be imprison , but say : ` He be keep there by enchantment , and can not be set free without my help .
I will therefore go with you myself . '
So they all set out , guide by bird , and after some day come to the cave where the unfortunate Prince have be chain up for nearly seven year .
He recognise the magician immediately , but the old man do not know him , he have grow so thin .
However , he undo the chain by the help of magic , and take care of the Prince until he recover and become strong enough to travel .
When he reach home he find that the old King have die that morning , so that he be now raise to the throne .
And now after his long suffering come prosperity , which last to the end of his life ; but he never get back the magic ring , nor have it ever again be see by mortal eye .
Now , if YOU have be the Prince , would you not rather have stay with the pretty witch-maiden ?
STORY OF THE EMPEROR 'S NEW CLOTHES -LRB- 4 -RRB- -LRB- 4 -RRB- Andersen .
Many year ago there live an Emperor who be so fond of new clothes that he spend all his money on them in order to be beautifully dress .
He do not care about his soldier , he do not care about the theatre ; he only like to go out walk to show off his new clothes .
He have a coat for every hour of the day ; and just a they say of a king , ` He be in the council-chamber , ' they always say here , ` The Emperor be in the wardrobe . '
In the great city in which he live there be always something go on ; every day many stranger come there .
One day two impostor arrive who give themselves out a weaver , and say that they know how to manufacture the most beautiful cloth imaginable .
Not only be the texture and pattern uncommonly beautiful , but the clothes which be make of the stuff possess this wonderful property that they be invisible to anyone who be not fit for his office , or who be unpardonably stupid .
` Those must indeed be splendid clothes , ' think the Emperor .
` If I have them on I could find out which men in my kingdom be unfit for the office they hold ; I could distinguish the wise from the stupid !
Yes , this cloth must be weave for me at once . '
And he give both the impostor much money , so that they might begin their work .
They place two weaving-looms , and begin to do a if they be work , but they have not the least thing on the loom .
They also demand the fine silk and the best gold , which they put in their pocket , and work at the empty loom till late into the night . '
I should like very much to know how far they have get on with the cloth , ' think the Emperor .
But he remember when he think about it that whoever be stupid or not fit for his office would not be able to see it .
Now he certainly believe that he have nothing to fear for himself , but he want first to send somebody else in order to see how he stand with regard to his office .
Everybody in the whole town know what a wonderful power the cloth have , and they be all curious to see how bad or how stupid their neighbour be . '
I will send my old and honoured minister to the weaver , ' think the Emperor .
` He can judge best what the cloth be like , for he have intellect , and no one understand his office well than he . '
Now the good old minister go into the hall where the two impostor sit work at the empty weaving-looms .
` Dear me ! '
think the old minister , open his eye wide , ' I can see nothing ! '
But he do not say so .
Both the impostor beg him to be so kind a to step close , and ask him if it be not a beautiful texture and lovely colour .
They point to the empty loom , and the poor old minister go forward rub his eye ; but he could see nothing , for there be nothing there .
` Dear , dear ! '
thought he , ` can I be stupid ?
I have never think that , and nobody must know it !
Can I be not fit for my office ?
No , I must certainly not say that I can not see the cloth ! '
` Have you nothing to say about it ? '
ask one of the men who be weave .
` Oh , it be lovely , most lovely ! '
answer the old minister , look through his spectacle .
` What a texture !
What colour !
Yes , I will tell the Emperor that it please me very much . '
` Now we be delight at that , ' say both the weaver , and thereupon they name the colour and explain the make of the texture .
The old minister pay great attention , so that he could tell the same to the Emperor when he come back to him , which he do .
The impostor now want more money , more silk , and more gold to use in their weaving .
They put it all in their own pocket , and there come no thread on the loom , but they go on a they have do before , work at the empty loom .
The Emperor soon send another worthy statesman to see how the weaving be get on , and whether the cloth would soon be finish .
It be the same with him a the first one ; he look and look , but because there be nothing on the empty loom he could see nothing .
` Is it not a beautiful piece of cloth ? '
ask the two impostor , and they point to and describe the splendid material which be not there .
` Stupid I be not ! '
think the man , ` so it must be my good office for which I be not fit .
It be strange , certainly , but no one must be allow to notice it . '
And so he praise the cloth which he do not see , and express to them his delight at the beautiful colour and the splendid texture .
` Yes , it be quite beautiful , ' he say to the Emperor .
Everybody in the town be talk of the magnificent cloth .
Now the Emperor want to see it himself while it be still on the loom .
With a great crowd of select follower , amongst whom be both the worthy statesman who have already be there before , he go to the cunning impostor , who be now weave with all their might , but without fibre or thread .
` Is it not splendid ! '
say both the old statesman who have already be there .
` See , your Majesty , what a texture !
What colour ! '
And then they point to the empty loom , for they believe that the others could see the cloth quite well .
` What ! '
think the Emperor , ' I can see nothing !
This be indeed horrible !
Am I stupid ?
Am I not fit to be Emperor ?
That be the most dreadful thing that could happen to me .
Oh , it be very beautiful , ' he say .
` It have my gracious approval . '
And then he nod pleasantly , and examine the empty loom , for he would not say that he could see nothing .
His whole Court round him look and look , and saw no more than the others ; but they say like the Emperor , ` Oh !
it be beautiful ! '
And they advise him to wear these new and magnificent clothes for the first time at the great procession which be soon to take place .
` Splendid !
Lovely !
Most beautiful ! '
go from mouth to mouth ; everyone seem delighted over them , and the Emperor give to the impostor the title of Court weaver to the Emperor .
Throughout the whole of the night before the morning on which the procession be to take place , the impostor be up and be work by the light of over sixteen candle .
The people could see that they be very busy make the Emperor 's new clothes ready .
They pretend they be take the cloth from the loom , cut with huge scissors in the air , sew with needle without thread , and then say at last , ` Now the clothes be finish ! '
The Emperor come himself with his most distinguished knight , and each impostor hold up his arm just a if he be hold something , and say , ` See !
here be the breech !
Here be the coat !
Here the cloak ! '
and so on .
` Spun clothes be so comfortable that one would imagine one have nothing on at all ; but that be the beauty of it ! '
` Yes , ' say all the knight , but they could see nothing , for there be nothing there .
` Will it please your Majesty graciously to take off your clothes , ' say the impostor , ` then we will put on the new clothes , here before the mirror . '
The Emperor take off all his clothes , and the impostor place themselves before him a if they be put on each part of his new clothes which be ready , and the Emperor turn and bent himself in front of the mirror .
` How beautifully they fit !
How well they sit ! '
say everybody .
` What material !
What colour !
It be a gorgeous suit ! '
` They be wait outside with the canopy which your Majesty be wont to have bear over you in the procession , ' announce the Master of the Ceremonies .
` Look , I be ready , ' say the Emperor .
` Does n't it sit well ! '
And he turn himself again to the mirror to see if his finery be on all right .
The chamberlain who be use to carry the train put their hand near the floor a if they be lift up the train ; then they do a if they be hold something in the air .
They would not have it notice that they could see nothing .
So the Emperor go along in the procession under the splendid canopy , and all the people in the street and at the window say , ` How matchless be the Emperor 's new clothes !
That train fasten to his dress , how beautifully it hang ! '
No one wish it to be notice that he could see nothing , for then he would have be unfit for his office , or else very stupid .
None of the Emperor 's clothes have meet with such approval a these have .
` But he have nothing on ! '
say a little child at last .
` Just listen to the innocent child ! '
say the father , and each one whisper to his neighbour what the child have say .
` But he have nothing on ! '
the whole of the people call out at last .
This strike the Emperor , for it seem to him a if they be right ; but he think to himself , ' I must go on with the procession now .
And the chamberlain walk along still more uprightly , hold up the train which be not there at all .
THE GOLDEN CRAB -LRB- 5 -RRB- -LRB- 5 -RRB- ` Prinz Krebs , ' from Griechische Mahrchen .
Schmidt .
Once upon a time there be a fisherman who have a wife and three child .
Every morning he use to go out fishing , and whatever fish he catch he sell to the King .
One day , among the other fish , he catch a golden crab .
When he come home he put all the fish together into a great dish , but he keep the Crab separate because it shine so beautifully , and place it upon a high shelf in the cupboard .
Now while the old woman , his wife , be clean the fish , and have tuck up her gown so that her foot be visible , she suddenly hear a voice , which say : ` Let down , let down thy petticoat That let thy foot be see . '
She turn round in surprise , and then she saw the little creature , the Golden Crab .
` What !
You can speak , can you , you ridiculous crab ? '
she say , for she be not quite pleased at the Crab 's remark .
Then she take him up and place him on a dish .
When her husband come home and they sit down to dinner , they presently hear the Crab 's little voice say , ` Give me some too . '
They be all very much surprise , but they give him something to eat .
When the old man come to take away the plate which have contain the Crab 's dinner , he find it full of gold , and a the same thing happen every day he soon become very fond of the Crab .
One day the Crab say to the fisherman 's wife , ` Go to the King and tell him I wish to marry his young daughter . '
The old woman go accordingly , and lay the matter before the King , who laugh a little at the notion of his daughter marry a crab , but do not decline the proposal altogether , because he be a prudent monarch , and know that the Crab be likely to be a prince in disguise .
He say , therefore , to the fisherman 's wife , ` Go , old woman , and tell the Crab I will give him my daughter if by to-morrow morning he can build a wall in front of my castle much high than my tower , upon which all the flower of the world must grow and bloom . '
The fisherman 's wife go home and give this message .
Then the Crab give her a golden rod , and say , ` Go and strike with this rod three time upon the ground on the place which the King show you , and to-morrow morning the wall will be there . '
The old woman do so and go away again .
The next morning , when the King awoke , what do you think he saw ?
The wall stand there before his eye , exactly a he have bespeak it !
Then the old woman go back to the King and say to him , ` Your Majesty 's order have be fulfil . '
` That be all very well , ' say the King , ` but I can not give away my daughter until there stand in front of my palace a garden in which there be three fountain , of which the first must play gold , the second diamond , and the third brilliants . '
So the old woman have to strike again three time upon the ground with the rod , and the next morning the garden be there .
The King now give his consent , and the wedding be fix for the very next day .
Then the Crab say to the old fisherman , ` Now take this rod ; go and knock with it on a certain mountain ; then a black man -LRB- 6 -RRB- will come out and ask you what you wish for .
Answer him thus : '' Your master , the King , have send me to tell you that you must send him his golden garment that be like the sun . ''
Make him give you , besides , the queenly robe of gold and precious stone which be like the flowery meadows , and bring them both to me .
And bring me also the golden cushion . '
-LRB- 6 -RRB- Ein Mohr .
The old man go and do his errand .
When he have bring the precious robe , the Crab put on the golden garment and then creep upon the golden cushion , and in this way the fisherman carry him to the castle , where the Crab present the other garment to his bride .
Now the ceremony take place , and when the marry pair be alone together the Crab make himself know to his young wife , and tell her how he be the son of the great king in the world , and how he be enchant , so that he become a crab by day and be a man only at night ; and he could also change himself into an eagle as often a he wish .
No sooner have he say this than he shake himself , and immediately become a handsome youth , but the next morning he be force to creep back again into his crab-shell .
And the same thing happen every day .
But the Princess 's affection for the Crab , and the polite attention with which she behave to him , surprise the royal family very much .
They suspect some secret , but though they spy and spy , they could not discover it .
Thus a year pass away , and the Princess have a son , whom she call Benjamin .
But her mother still think the whole matter very strange .
At last she say to the King that he ought to ask his daughter whether she would not like to have another husband instead of the Crab ?
But when the daughter be question she only answer : ' I be marry to the Crab , and him only will I have . '
Then the King say to her , ' I will appoint a tournament in your honour , and I will invite all the prince in the world to it , and if any one of them please you , you shall marry him . '
In the even the Princess tell this to the Crab , who say to her , ` Take this rod , go to the garden gate and knock with it , then a black man will come out and say to you , '' Why have you call me , and what do you require of me ? ''
Answer him thus : ` Your master the King have send me hither to tell you to send him his golden armour and his steed and the silver apple . ''
And bring them to me . '
The Princess do so , and bring him what he desire .
The follow even the Prince dress himself for the tournament .
Before he go he say to his wife , ` Now mind you do not say when you see me that I be the Crab .
For if you do this evil will come of it .
Place yourself at the window with your sister ; I will ride by and throw you the silver apple .
Take it in your hand , but if they ask you who I be , say that you do not know . '
So say , he kiss her , repeat his warn once more , and go away .
The Princess go with her sister to the window and look on at the tournament .
Presently her husband rode by and throw the apple up to her .
She catch it in her hand and go with it to her room , and by-and-by her husband come back to her .
But her father be much surprise that she do not seem to care about any of the Princes ; he therefore appoint a second tournament .
The Crab then give his wife the same direction a before , only this time the apple which she receive from the black man be of gold .
But before the Prince go to the tournament he say to his wife , ` Now I know you will betray me to-day . '
But she swear to him that she would not tell who he be .
He then repeat his warning and go away .
In the evening , while the Princess , with her mother and sister , be stand at the window , the Prince suddenly gallop past on his steed and throw her the golden apple .
Then her mother fly into a passion , give her a box on the ear , and cry out , ` Does not even that prince please you , you fool ? '
The Princess in her fright exclaim , ` That be the Crab himself ! '
Her mother be still more angry because she have not be told sooner , run into her daughter 's room where the crab-shell be still lie , take it up and throw it into the fire .
Then the poor Princess cry bitterly , but it be of no use ; her husband do not come back .
Now we must leave the Princess and turn to the other person in the story .
One day an old man go to a stream to dip in a crust of bread which he be go to eat , when a dog come out of the water , snatch the bread from his hand , and run away .
The old man run after him , but the dog reach a door , push it open , and ran in , the old man follow him .
He do not overtake the dog , but find himself above a staircase , which he descend .
Then he saw before him a stately palace , and , enter , he find in a large hall a table set for twelve person .
He hide himself in the hall behind a great picture , that he might see what would happen .
At noon he hear a great noise , so that he tremble with fear .
When he take courage to look out from behind the picture , he saw twelve eagle fly in .
At this sight his fear become still great .
The eagle fly to the basin of a fountain that be there and bath themselves , when suddenly they be change into twelve handsome youth .
Now they seat themselves at the table , and one of them take up a goblet fill with wine , and say , ' A health to my father ! '
And another say , ' A health to my mother ! '
and so the health go round .
Then one of them say : ' A health to my dear lady , Long may she live and well !
But a curse on the cruel mother That burnt my golden shell ! '
And so say he weep bitterly .
Then the youth rise from the table , go back to the great stone fountain , turn themselves into eagle again , and fly away .
Then the old man go away too , return to the light of day , and go home .
Soon after he hear that the Princess be ill , and that the only thing that do her good be have story tell to her .
He therefore go to the royal castle , obtain an audience of the Princess , and tell her about the strange thing he have see in the underground palace .
No sooner have he finish than the Princess ask him whether he could find the way to that palace .
` Yes , ' he answer , ` certainly . '
And now she desire him to guide her thither at once .
The old man do so , and when they come to the palace he hide her behind the great picture and advise her to keep quite still , and he place himself behind the picture also .
Presently the eagle come fly in , and change themselves into young men , and in a moment the Princess recognise her husband amongst them all , and try to come out of her hiding-place ; but the old man hold her back .
The youth seat themselves at the table ; and now the Prince say again , while he take up the cup of wine : ' A health to my dear lady , Long may she live and well !
But a curse on the cruel mother That burnt my golden shell ! '
Then the Princess could restrain herself no longer , but run forward and throw her arm round her husband .
And immediately he know her again , and say : ` Do you remember how I tell you that day that you would betray me ?
Now you see that I speak the truth .
But all that bad time be past .
Now listen to me : I must still remain enchanted for three month .
Will you stay here with me till that time be over ? '
So the Princess stay with him , and say to the old man , ` Go back to the castle and tell my parent that I be stay here . '
Her parent be very much vexed when the old man come back and tell them this , but as soon a the three month of the Prince 's enchantment be over , he cease to be an eagle and become once more a man , and they return home together .
And then they live happily , and we who hear the story be happy still .
THE IRON STOVE -LRB- 7 -RRB- -LRB- 7 -RRB- Grimm .
Once upon a time when wish come true there be a king 's son who be enchant by an old witch , so that he be oblige to sit in a large iron stove in a wood .
There he live for many year , and no one could free him .
At last a king 's daughter come into the wood ; she have lose her way , and could not find her father 's kingdom again .
She have be wander round and round for nine day , and she come at last to the iron case .
A voice come from within and ask her , ` Where do you come from , and where do you want to go ? '
She answer , ' I have lose my way to my father 's kingdom , and I shall never get home again . '
Then the voice from the iron stove say , ' I will help you to find your home again , and that in a very short time , if you will promise to do what I ask you .
I be a great prince than you be a princess , and I will marry you . '
Then she grow frightened , and think , ` What can a young lassie do with an iron stove ? '
But a she want very much to go home to her father , she promise to do what he wish .
He say , ` You must come again , and bring a knife with you to scrape a hole in the iron . '
Then he give her someone for a guide , who walk near her and say nothing , but he bring her in two hour to her house .
There be great joy in the castle when the Princess come back , and the old King fell on her neck and kiss her .
But she be very much trouble , and say , ` Dear father , listen to what have befall me !
I should never have come home again out of the great wild wood if I have not come to an iron stove , to whom I have have to promise that I will go back to free him and marry him ! '
The old King be so frightened that he nearly faint , for she be his only daughter .
So they consult together , and determine that the miller 's daughter , who be very beautiful , should take her place .
They take her there , give her a knife , and say she must scrape at the iron stove .
She scrap for twenty-four hour , but do not make the least impression .
When the day break , a voice call from the iron stove , ` It seem to me that it be day outside . '
Then she answer , ` It seem so to me ; I think I hear my father 's mill rattle . '
` So you be a miller 's daughter !
Then go away at once , and tell the King 's daughter to come . '
Then she go away , and tell the old King that the thing inside the iron stove would not have her , but want the Princess .
The old King be frighten , and his daughter wept .
But they have a swineherd 's daughter who be even more beautiful than the miller 's daughter , and they give her a piece of gold to go to the iron stove instead of the Princess .
Then she be take out , and have to scrape for four-and-twenty hour , but she could make no impression .
As soon a the day break the voice from the stove call out , ` It seem to be daylight outside . '
Then she answer , ` It seem so to me too ; I think I hear my father blow his horn . '
` So you be a swineherd 's daughter !
Go away at once , and let the King 's daughter come .
And say to her that what I foretell shall come to pass , and if she do not come everything in the kingdom shall fall into ruin , and not one stone shall be leave upon another . '
When the Princess heard this she begin to cry , but it be no good ; she have to keep her word .
She take leave of her father , put a knife in her belt , and go to the iron stove in the wood .
As soon a she reach it she begin to scrape , and the iron give way and before two hour have pass she have make a little hole .
Then she peep in and saw such a beautiful youth all shin with gold and precious stone that she fell in love with him on the spot .
So she scrap away hard than ever , and make the hole so large that he could get out .
Then he say , ` You be mine , and I be thine ; you be my bride and have set me free ! '
He want to take her with him to his kingdom , but she beg him just to let her go once more to her father ; and the Prince let her go , but tell her not to say more than three word to her father , then to come back again .
So she go home , but ala !
she say MORE THAN THREE WORDS ; and immediately the iron stove vanish and go away over a mountain of glass and sharp sword .
But the Prince be free , and be no long shut up in it .

She seek it for nine day , and then her hunger become so great that she do not know how she could live any long .

THE DRAGON AND HIS GRANDMOTHER There be once a great war , and the King have a great many soldier , but he give them so little pay that they could not live upon it .
Then three of them take counsel together and determine to desert .
One of them say to the others , ` If we be catch , we shall be hang on the gallows ; how shall we set about it ? '
The other say , ` Do you see that large cornfield there ?
If we be to hide ourselves in that , no one could find u .
The army can not come into it , and to-morrow it be to march on . '
They creep into the corn , but the army do not march on , but remain encamp close around them .
They sit for two day and two night in the corn , and grow so hungry that they nearly die ; but if they be to venture out , it be certain death .
They say at last , ` What use be it our desert ?
We must perish here miserably . '
Whilst they be speak a fiery dragon come fly through the air .
It hover near them , and ask why they be hide there .
They answer , ` We be three soldier , and have desert because our pay be so small .
Now if we remain here we shall die of hunger , and if we move out we shall be string up on the gallows . '
` If you will serve me for seven year , ' say the dragon , I will lead you through the midst of the army so that no one shall catch you . '
` We have no choice , and must take your offer , ' say they .
Then the dragon seize them in his claw , take them through the air over the army , and set them down on the earth a long way from it .
He give them a little whip , say , ` Whip and slash with this , and as much money a you want will jump up before you .
You can then live a great lord , keep horse , and drive about in carriage .
But after seven year you be mine . '
Then he put a book before them , which he make all three of them sign . '
I will then give you a riddle , ' he say ; ` if you guess it , you shall be free and out of my power . '
The dragon then fly away , and they journey on with their little whip .
They have a much money a they want , wear grand clothes , and make their way into the world .
Wherever they go they live in merrymaking and splendour , drive about with horse and carriage , ate and drank , but do nothing wrong .
The time pass quickly away , and when the seven year be nearly end two of them grow terribly anxious and frightened , but the third make light of it , say , ` Do n't be afraid , brother , I be n't bear yesterday ; I will guess the riddle . '

` Alas !
what have you to do with it ?
You can not help u . '

she answer .
` Only confide your trouble in me . '

and they remain where they be .

` Indeed !
three soldier ! '

` What sort of a riddle be it ? '
she ask . '
I will tell you this .
In the North Sea lie a dead sea-cat -- that shall be their roast meat ; and the rib of a whale -- that shall be their silver spoon ; and the hollow foot of a dead horse -- that shall be their wineglass . '
When the Dragon have go to bed , his old grandmother pull up the stone and let out the soldier .
