THE THREE BROTHERS -LRB- 17 -RRB- -LRB- 17 -RRB- From the Polish .
Kletke .
There be once upon a time a witch , who in the shape of a hawk use every night to break the window of a certain village church .
In the same village there live three brother , who be all determine to kill the mischievous hawk .
But in vain do the two eldest mount guard in the church with their gun ; as soon a the bird appear high above their head , sleep overpower them , and they only awake to hear the window crash in .
Then the young brother take his turn of guard the window , and to prevent his be overcome by sleep he place a lot of thorn under his chin , so that if he felt drowsy and nod his head , they would prick him and keep him awake .
The moon be already rise , and it be as light a day , when suddenly he hear a fearful noise , and at the same time a terrible desire to sleep overpowered him .
His eyelid close , and his head sank on his shoulder , but the thorn run into him and be so painful that he awake at once .
He saw the hawk swoop down upon the church , and in a moment he have seize his gun and shot at the bird .
The hawk fell heavily under a big stone , severely wound in it right wing .
The youth run to look at it , and saw that a huge abyss have open below the stone .
He go at once to fetch his brother , and with their help drag a lot of pine-wood and rope to the spot .
They fasten some of the burn pine-wood to the end of the rope , and let it slowly down to the bottom of the abyss .
At first it be quite dark , and the flaming torch only light up dirty grey stone wall .
But the young brother determine to explore the abyss , and let himself down by the rope he soon reach the bottom .
Here he find a lovely meadow full of green tree and exquisite flower .
In the middle of the meadow stand a huge stone castle , with an iron gate lead to it , which be wide open .
Everything in the castle seem to be make of copper , and the only inhabitant he could discover be a lovely girl , who be comb her golden hair ; and he notice that whenever one of her hair fell on the ground it ring out like pure metal .
The youth look at her more closely , and saw that her skin be smooth and fair , her blue eye bright and sparkling , and her hair as golden a the sun .
He fell in love with her on the spot , and kneel at her foot , he implore her to become his wife .
The lovely girl accept his proposal gladly ; but at the same time she warn him that she could never come up to the world above till her mother , the old witch , be dead .
And she go on to tell him that the only way in which the old creature could be kill be with the sword that hang up in the castle ; but the sword be so heavy that no one could lift it .
Then the youth go into a room in the castle where everything be make of silver , and here he find another beautiful girl , the sister of his bride .
She be comb her silver hair , and every hair that fell on the ground ring out like pure metal .
The second girl hand him the sword , but though he try with all his strength he could not lift it .
At last a third sister come to him and give him a drop of something to drink , which she say would give him the needful strength .
He drink one drop , but still he could not lift the sword ; then he drink a second , and the sword begin to move ; but only after he have drunk a third drop be he able to swing the sword over his head .
Then he hide himself in the castle and await the old witch 's arrival .
At last a it be begin to grow dark she appear .
She swoop down upon a big apple-tree , and after shake some golden apple from it , she pounce down upon the earth .
As soon a her foot touch the ground she become transform from a hawk into a woman .
This be the moment the youth be wait for , and he swing his mighty sword in the air with all his strength and the witch 's head fell off , and her blood spurt up on the wall .
Without fear of any further danger , he pack up all the treasure of the castle into great chest , and give his brother a signal to pull them up out of the abyss .
First the treasure be attach to the rope and then the three lovely girl .
And now everything be up above and only he himself remain below .
But a he be a little suspicious of his brother , he fasten a heavy stone on to the rope and let them pull it up .
At first they heave with a will , but when the stone be half way up they let it drop suddenly , and it fell to the bottom broken into a hundred piece .
` So that 's what would have happen to my bone have I trust myself to them , ' say the youth sadly ; and he begin to cry bitterly , not because of the treasure , but because of the lovely girl with her swanlike neck and golden hair .
For a long time he wander sadly all through the beautiful underworld , and one day he meet a magician who ask him the cause of his tear .
The youth tell him all that have befall him , and the magician say : ` Do not grieve , young man !
If you will guard the child who be hide in the golden apple-tree , I will bring you at once up to the earth .
Another magician who live in this land always eat my child up .
It be in vain that I have hide them under the earth and lock them into the castle .
Now I have hide them in the apple-tree ; hide yourself there too , and at midnight you will see my enemy . '
The youth climb up the tree , and pick some of the beautiful golden apple , which he eat for his supper .
At midnight the wind begin to rise , and a rustle sound be hear at the foot of the tree .
The youth look down and behold a long thick serpent begin to crawl up the tree .
It wind itself round the stem and gradually get high and high .
It stretch it huge head , in which the eye glitter fiercely , among the branch , search for the nest in which the little child lay .
They tremble with terror when they saw the hideous creature , and hide themselves beneath the leaf .
Then the youth swing his mighty sword in the air , and with one blow cut off the serpent 's head .
He cut up the rest of the body into little bit and strew them to the four wind .
The father of the rescued child be so delighted over the death of his enemy that he tell the youth to get on his back , and in this way he carry him up to the world above .
With what joy do he hurry now to his brother ' house !
He burst into a room where they be all assemble , but no one knew who he be .
Only his bride , who be serve as cook to her sister , recognise her lover at once .
His brother , who have quite believe he be dead , yield him up his treasure at once , and fly into the wood in terror .
But the good youth forgive them all they have do , and divide his treasure with them .
Then he build himself a big castle with golden window , and there he live happily with his golden-haired wife till the end of their life .
THE BOY AND THE WOLVES , OR THE BROKEN PROMISE -LRB- 18 -RRB- -LRB- 18 -RRB- A North American Indian story .
Once upon a time an Indian hunter build himself a house in the middle of a great forest , far away from all his tribe ; for his heart be gentle and kind , and he be weary of the treachery and cruel deed of those who have be his friend .
So he leave them , and take his wife and three child , and they journey on until they find a spot near to a clear stream , where they begin to cut down tree , and to make ready their wigwam .
For many year they live peacefully and happily in this sheltered place , never leave it except to hunt the wild animal , which serve them both for food and clothes .
At last , however , the strong man felt sick , and before long he know he must die .
So he gather his family round him , and say his last word to them .
` You , my wife , the companion of my day , will follow me ere many moon have wan to the island of the blest .
But for you , O my child , whose life be but newly begin , the wickedness , unkindness , and ingratitude from which I flee be before you .
Yet I shall go hence in peace , my child , if you will promise always to love each other , and never to forsake your young brother .
` Never ! '
they reply , hold out their hand .
And the hunter die content .
Scarcely eight moon have pass when , just a he have say , the wife go forth , and follow her husband ; but before leave her child she bid the two elder one think of their promise never to forsake the young , for he be a child , and weak .
And while the snow lay thick upon the ground , they tend him and cherish him ; but when the earth show green again , the heart of the young man stir within him , and he long to see the wigwam of the village where his father 's youth be spend .
Therefore he open all his heart to his sister , who answer : ` My brother , I understand your longing for our fellow-men , whom here we can not see .
But remember our father 's word .
Shall we not seek our own pleasure , and forget the little one ? '
But he would not listen , and , make no reply , he take his bow and arrow and leave the hut .
The snow fell and melt , yet he never return ; and at last the heart of the girl grow cold and hard , and her little boy become a burden in her eye , till one day she speak thus to him : ` See , there be food for many day to come .
Stay here within the shelter of the hut .
I go to seek our brother , and when I have find him I shall return hither . '
But when , after hard journeying , she reach the village where her brother dwelt , and saw that he have a wife and be happy , and when she , too , be seek by a young brave , then she also forget the boy alone in the forest , and think only of her husband .
Now as soon a the little boy have eat all the food which his sister have leave him , he go out into the wood , and gather berry and dig up root , and while the sun shone he be content and have his fill .
But when the snow begin and the wind howl , then his stomach felt empty and his limb cold , and he hide in tree all the night , and only creep out to eat what the wolf have leave behind .
And by-and-by , have no other friend , he seek their company , and sit by while they devour their prey , and they grow to know him , and give him food .
And without them he would have die in the snow .
But at last the snow melt , and the ice upon the great lake , and a the wolf go down to the shore , the boy go after them .
And it happen one day that his big brother be fish in his canoe near the shore , and he hear the voice of a child singing in the Indian tone -- ` My brother , my brother !
I be become a wolf , I be become a wolf ! '
And when he have so sung he howl a wolf howl .
Then the heart of the elder sunk , and he hasten towards him , cry , ` Brother , little brother , come to me ; ' but he , be half a wolf , only continue his song .
And the louder the elder call him , ` Brother , little brother , come to me , ' the swifter he flee after his brother the wolf , and the heavy grow his skin , till , with a long howl , he vanish into the depth of the forest .
So , with shame and anguish in his soul , the elder brother go back to his village , and , with his sister , mourn the little boy and the broken promise till the end of his life .
THE GLASS AXE -LRB- 19 -RRB- -LRB- 19 -RRB- From the Hungarian .
Kletke .
There be once upon a time a King and Queen who have everything they could possibly wish for in this world except a child .
At last , after twelve year , the Queen give birth to a son ; but she do not live long to enjoy her happiness , for on the following day she die .
But before her death she call her husband to her and say , ` Never let the child put his foot on the ground , for as soon a he do so he will fall into the power of a wicked Fairy , who will do him much harm . '
And these be the last word the poor Queen spoke .
The boy throve and grow big , and when he be too heavy for his nurse to carry , a chair be make for him on little wheel , in which he could wander through the palace garden without help ; at other time he be carry about on a litter , and he be always carefully watch and guard for fear he should at any time put his foot to the ground .
But a this sort of life be bad for his health , the doctor order him horse exercise , and he soon become a first-rate rider , and use to go out for long excursion on horseback , accompany always by his father 's stud-groom and a numerous retinue .
Every day he ride through the neighbouring field and wood , and always return home in the evening safe and well .
In this way many year pass , and the Prince grow to manhood , and hardly anyone remember the Queen 's warning , though precaution be still take , more from use and wont than for any other reason .
One day the Prince and his suite go out for a ride in a wood where his father sometimes hold a hunt .
Their way lead through a stream whose bank be overgrow with thick brushwood .
Just a the horseman be about to ford the river , a hare , startle by the sound of the horse ' hoof , start up from the grass and run towards the thicket .
The young Prince pursue the little creature , and have almost overtake it , when the girth of his saddle suddenly break in two and he fell heavily to the ground .
No sooner have his foot touch the earth than he disappear before the eye of the horrified courtier .
They seek for him far and near , but all in vain , and they be force to recognise the power of the evil Fairy , against which the Queen have warn them on her death-bed .
The old King be much grieve when they bring him the news of his son 's disappearance , but a he could do nothing to free him from his fate , he give himself up to an old age of grief and loneliness , cherish at the same time the hope that some lucky chance might one day deliver the youth out of the hand of his enemy .
Hardly have the Prince touch the ground than he felt himself violently seize by an unseen power , and hurry away he know not whither .
A whole new world stretch out before him , quite unlike the one he have leave .
A splendid castle surround by a huge lake be the abode of the Fairy , and the only approach to it be over a bridge of cloud .
On the other side of the lake high mountain rise up , and dark wood stretch along the bank ; over all hung a thick mist , and deep silence reign everywhere .
No sooner have the Fairy reach her own domain than she make herself visible , and turn to the Prince she tell him that unless he obey all her command down to the minute detail he would be severely punish .
Then she give him an axe make of glass , and bid him cross the bridge of cloud and go into the wood beyond and cut down all the tree there before sunset .
At the same time she caution him with many angry word against speak to a black girl he would most likely meet in the wood .
The Prince listen to her word meekly , and when she have finish take up the glass axe and set out for the forest .
At every step he seem to sink into the cloud , but fear give wing to his foot , and he cross the lake in safety and set to work at once .
But no sooner have he strike the first blow with his axe than it break into a thousand piece against the tree .
The poor youth be so terrified he do not know what to do , for he be in mortal dread of the punishment the wicked old Fairy would inflict on him .
He wander to and fro in the wood , not know where he be go , and at last , wear out by fatigue and misery , he sink on the ground and fell fast asleep .
He do not know how long he have sleep when a sudden sound awake him , and open his eye he saw a black girl stand beside him .
Mindful of the Fairy 's warning he do not dare to address her , but she on her part greet him in the most friendly manner , and ask him at once if he be under the power of the wicked Fairy .
The Prince nod his head silently in answer .
Then the black girl tell him that she too be in the power of the Fairy , who have doom her to wander about in her present guise until some youth should take pity on her and bear her in safety to the other side of the river which they saw in the distance , and on the other side of which the Fairy 's domain and power end .
The girl 's word so inspire the Prince with confidence that he tell her all his tale of woe , and end up by ask her advice a to how he be to escape the punishment the Fairy would be sure to inflict on him when she discover that he have not cut down the tree in the wood and that he have break her axe .
` You must know , ' answer the black girl , ` that the Fairy in whose power we both be be my own mother , but you must not betray this secret , for it would cost me my life .
If you will only promise to try and free me I will stand by you , and will accomplish for you all the task which my mother set you . '
The Prince promise joyfully all she ask ; then have once more warn him not to betray her confidence , she hand him a draught to drink which very soon sink his sens in a deep slumber .
His astonishment be great when he awake to find the glass axe whole and unbroken at his side , and all the tree of the wood lie fell around him !
He make all haste across the bridge of cloud , and tell the Fairy that her command be obey .
She be much amaze when she hear that all the wood be cut down , and saw the axe unbroken in his hand , and since she could not believe that he have do all this by himself , she question him narrowly if he have see or speak to the black girl .
But the Prince lie manfully , and swore he have never look up from his work for a moment .
Seeing she could get nothing more out of him , she give him a little bread and water , and show him to a small dark cupboard she tell him he might sleep there .
Morning have hardly dawn when the Fairy awake the Prince , and give him the glass axe again she tell him to cut up all the wood he have fell the day before , and to put it in bundle ready for firewood ; at the same time she warn him once more against approach or speak a word to the black girl if he meet her in the wood .
Although his task be no easy than that of the day before , the youth set out much more cheerfully , because he know he could count an the help of the black girl .
With quicker and light step he cross the bridge of cloud , and hardly have he reach the other side than his friend stand before him and greet him cheerfully .
When she hear what the Fairy demand this time , she answer smilingly , ` Never fear , ' and hand him another draught , which very soon cause the Prince to sink into a deep sleep .
When he awake everything , be do .
All the tree of the wood be cut up into firewood and arrange in bundle ready for use .
He return to the castle as quickly a he could , and tell the Fairy that her command be obey .
She be even more amazed than she have be before , and ask him again if he have either see or speak to the black girl ; but the Prince know good than to betray his word , and once more lied freely .
On the following day the Fairy set him a third task to do , even hard than the other two .
She tell him he must build a castle on the other side of the lake , make of nothing but gold , silver , and precious stone , and unless he could accomplish this within an hour , the most frightful doom await him .
The Prince hear her word without anxiety , so entirely do he rely on the help of his black friend .
Full of hope he hurry across the bridge , and recognise at once the spot where the castle be to stand , for spade , hammer , ax , and every other building implement lay scatter on the ground ready for the workman 's hand , but of gold , silver , and precious stone there be not a sign .
But before the Prince have time to feel despondent the black girl beckon to him in the distance from behind a rock , where she have hide herself for fear her mother should catch sight of her .
Full of joy the youth hurry towards her , and beg her aid and counsel in the new piece of work he have be give to do .
But this time the Fairy have watch the Prince 's movement from her window , and she saw him hide himself behind the rock with her daughter .
She utter a piercing shriek so that the mountain re-echoed with the sound of it , and the terrified pair have hardly dare to look out from their hiding-place when the enraged woman , with her dress and hair fly in the wind , hurry over the bridge of cloud .
The Prince at once give himself up for lose , but the girl tell him to be of good courage and to follow her as quickly a he could .
But before they leave their shelter she break off a little bit of the rock , speak some magic word over it , and throw it in the direction her mother be come from .
In a moment a glitter palace arise before the eye of the Fairy which blind her with it dazzle splendour , and with it many door and passage prevent her for some time from find her way out of it .
In the meantime the black girl hurry on with the Prince , hasten to reach the river , where once on the other side they would for ever be out of the wicked Fairy 's power .
But before they have accomplish half the way they hear again the rustle of her garment and her muttered curse pursue them closely .
The Prince be terrify ; he dare not look back , and he felt his strength give way .
But before he have time to despair the girl utter some more magic word , and immediately she herself be change into a pond , and the Prince into a duck swim on it surface .
When the Fairy saw this her rage know no bound , and she use all her magic wit to make the pond disappear ; she cause a hill of sand to arise at her foot , mean it to dry up the water at once .
But the sand hill only drive the pond a little farther away , and it water seem to increase instead of diminish .
When the old woman saw that the power of her magic be of so little avail , she have recourse to cunning .
She throw a lot of gold nut into the pond , hop in this way to catch the duck , but all her effort be fruitless , for the little creature refuse to let itself be catch .
Then a new idea strike the wicked old woman , and hide herself behind the rock which have shelter the fugitive , she wait behind it , watch carefully for the moment when the Prince and her daughter should resume their natural form and continue their journey .
She have not to wait long , for as soon a the girl think her mother be safely out of the way , she change herself and the Prince once more into their human shape , and set out cheerfully for the river .
But they have not go many step when the wicked Fairy hurry after them , a drawn dagger in her hand , and be close upon them , when suddenly , instead of the Prince and her daughter , she find herself in front of a great stone church , whose entrance be carefully guard by a huge monk .
Breathless with rage and passion , she try to plunge her dagger into the monk 's heart , but it fell shatter in piece at her foot .
In her desperation she determine to pull down the church , and thus to destroy her two victim for ever .
She stamp three time on the ground , and the earth tremble , and both the church and the monk begin to shake .
As soon a the Fairy saw this she retreat to some distance from the building , so a not to be hurt herself by it fall .
But once more her scheme be doom to failure , for hardly have she go a yard from the church than both it and the monk disappear , and she find herself in a wood black a night , and full of wolf and bear and wild animal of all sort and description .
Then her wrath give place to terror , for she fear every moment to be tear in piece by the beast who one and all seem to defy her power .
She think it wise to make her way a best she could out of the forest , and then to pursue the fugitive once more and accomplish their destruction either by force or cunning .
In the meantime the Prince and the black girl have again assume their natural form , and be hurry on as fast a they could to reach the river .
But when they get there they find that there be no way in which they could cross it , and the girl 's magic art seem no long to have any power .
Then turn to the Prince she say , ` The hour for my deliverance have not yet come , but a you promise to do all you could to free me , you must do exactly a I bid you now .
Take this bow and arrow and kill every beast you see with them , and be sure you spare no living creature . '
With these word she disappear , and hardly have she do so than a huge wild boar start out of the thicket near and make straight for the Prince .
But the youth do not lose his presence of mind , and draw his bow he pierce the beast with his arrow right through the skull .
The creature fell heavily on the ground , and out of it side spring a little hare , which run like the wind along the river bank .
The Prince draw his bow once more , and the hare lay dead at his foot ; but at the same moment a dove rise up in the air , and circle round the Prince 's head in the most confiding manner .
But mindful of the black girl 's command , he dare not spare the little creature 's life , and take another arrow from his quiver he lay it as dead a the boar and the hare .
But when he go to look at the body of the bird he find instead of the dove a round white egg lie on the ground .
While he be gaze on it and wonder what it could mean , he hear the sweeping of wing above him , and look up he saw a huge vulture with open claw swoop down upon him .
In a moment he seize the egg and flung it at the bird with all his might , and lo and behold !
instead of the ugly monster the most beautiful girl he have ever see stood before the astonished eye of the Prince .
But while all this be go on the wicked old Fairy have manage to make her way out of the wood , and be now use the last resource in her power to overtake her daughter and the Prince .
As soon a she be in the open again she mount her chariot , which be draw by a fiery dragon , and fly through the air in it .
But just a she get to the river she saw the two lover in each other 's arm swim through the water as easily a two fish .
Quick a lightning , and forgetful of every danger , she fly down upon them .
But the water seize her chariot and sunk it in the low depth , and the wave bore the wicked old woman down the stream till she be catch in some thorn bush , where she make a good meal for all the little fish that be swim about .
And so at last the Prince and his lovely Bride be free .
They hurry as quickly a they could to the old King , who receive them with joy and gladness .
On the following day a most gorgeous wedding feast be hold , and as far a we know the Prince and his bride live happily for ever afterwards .
THE DEAD WIFE -LRB- 20 -RRB- -LRB- 20 -RRB- From the Iroquois .
Once upon a time there be a man and his wife who live in the forest , very far from the rest of the tribe .
Very often they spend the day in hunt together , but after a while the wife find that she have so many thing to do that she be oblige to stay at home ; so he go alone , though he find that when his wife be not with him he never have any luck .
One day , when he be away hunt , the woman fell ill , and in a few day she die .
Her husband grieve bitterly , and bury her in the house where she have pass her life ; but a the time go on he felt so lonely without her that he make a wooden doll about her height and size for company , and dress it in her clothes .
He seat it in front of the fire , and try to think he have his wife back again .
The next day he go out to hunt , and when he come home the first thing he do be to go up to the doll and brush off some of the ash from the fire which have fall on it face .
But he be very busy now , for he have to cook and mend , besides get food , for there be no one to help him .
And so a whole year pass away .
At the end of that time he come back from hunt one night and find some wood by the door and a fire within .
The next night there be not only wood and fire , but a piece of meat in the kettle , nearly ready for eat .
He search all about to see who could have do this , but could find no one .
The next time he go to hunt he take care not to go far , and come in quite early .
And while he be still a long way off he saw a woman go into the house with wood on her shoulder .
So he make haste , and open the door quickly , and instead of the wooden doll , his wife sit in front of the fire .
Then she speak to him and say , ` The Great Spirit felt sorry for you , because you would not be comfort , so he let me come back to you , but you must not stretch out your hand to touch me till we have see the rest of our people .
If you do , I shall die . '
So the man listen to her word , and the woman dwelt there , and bring the wood and kindle the fire , till one day her husband say to her , ` It be now two year since you die .
Let u now go back to our tribe .
Then you will be well , and I can touch you . '
And with that he prepare food for the journey , a string of deer 's flesh for her to carry , and one for himself ; and so they start .
Now the camp of the tribe be distant six day ' journey , and when they be yet one day 's journey off it begin to snow , and they felt weary and long for rest .
Therefore they make a fire , cook some food , and spread out their skin to sleep .
Then the heart of the man be greatly stir , and he stretch out his arm to his wife , but she wave her hand and say , ` We have see no one yet ; it be too soon . '
But he would not listen to her , and catch her to him , and behold !
he be clasp the wooden doll .
And when he saw it be the doll he push it from him in his misery and rush away to the camp , and tell them all his story .
And some doubt , and they go back with him to the place where he and his wife have stop to rest , and there lay the doll , and besides , they saw in the snow the step of two people , and the foot of one be like the foot of the doll .
And the man grieve sore all the day of his life .
IN THE LAND OF SOULS -LRB- 21 -RRB- -LRB- 21 -RRB- From the Red Indian .
Far away , in North America , where the Red Indians dwell , there live a long time ago a beautiful maiden , who be lovely than any other girl in the whole tribe .
Many of the young brave seek her in marriage , but she would listen to one only -- a handsome chief , who have take her fancy some year before .
So they be to be marry , and great rejoicing be make , and the two look forward to a long life of happiness together , when the very night before the wedding feast a sudden illness seize the girl , and , without a word to her friend who be weep round her , she pass silently away .
The heart of her lover have be set upon her , and the thought of her remain with him night and day .
He put aside his bow , and go neither to fight nor to hunt , but from sunrise to sunset he sit by the place where she be lay , think of his happiness that be bury there .
At last , after many day , a light seem to come to him out of the darkness .
He remember have hear from the old , old people of the tribe , that there be a path that lead to the Land of Souls -- that if you seek carefully you could find it .
So the next morning he get up early , and put some food in his pouch and sling an extra skin over his shoulder , for he know not how long his journey would take , nor what sort of country he would have to go through .
Only one thing he know , that if the path be there , he would find it .
At first he be puzzle , a there seem no reason he should go in one direction more than another .
Then all at once he think he have hear one of the old men say that the Land of Souls lay to the south , and so , fill with new hope and courage , he set his face southward .
For many , many mile the country look the same a it do round his own home .
The forest , the hill , and the river all seem exactly like the one he have leave .
The only thing that be different be the snow , which have lain thick upon the hill and tree when he start , but grow less and less the farther he go south , till it disappear altogether .
Soon the tree put forth their bud , and flower spring up under his foot , and instead of thick cloud there be blue sky over his head , and everywhere the bird be sing .
Then he know that he be in the right road .
The thought that he should soon behold his lose bride make his heart beat for joy , and he speed along lightly and swiftly .
Now his way lead through a dark wood , and then over some steep cliff , and on the top of these he find a hut or wigwam .
An old man clothe in skin , and hold a staff in his hand , stood in the doorway ; and he say to the young chief who be begin to tell his story , ' I be wait for you , wherefore you have come I know .
It be but a short while since she whom you seek be here .
Rest in my hut , a she also rest , and I will tell you what you ask , and whither you should go . '
On hear these word , the young man enter the hut , but his heart be too eager within him to suffer him to rest , and when he arise , the old man rise too , and stand with him at the door .
` Look , ' he say , ` at the water which lie far out yonder , and the plain which stretch beyond .
That be the Land of Souls , but no man enter it without leave his body behind him .
So , lay down your body here ; your bow and arrow , your skin and your dog .
They shall be keep for you safely . '
Then he turn away , and the young chief , light a air , seem hardly to touch the ground ; and a he fly along the scent grow sweeter and the flower more beautiful , while the animal rub their nose against him , instead of hiding a he approach , and bird circle round him , and fish lift up their head and look a he go by .
Very soon he notice with wonder , that neither rock nor tree bar his path .
He pass through them without know it , for indeed , they be not rock and tree at all , but only the soul of them ; for this be the Land of Shadows .
So he go on with winged foot till he come to the shore of a great lake , with a lovely island in the middle of it ; while on the bank of the lake be a canoe of glitter stone , and in the canoe be two shin paddle .
The chief jump straight into the canoe , and seize the paddle push off from the shore , when to his joy and wonder he saw follow him in another canoe exactly like his own the maiden for whose sake he have make this long journey .
But they could not touch each other , for between them roll great wave , which look a if they would sink the boat , yet never do .
And the young man and the maiden shrank with fear , for down in the depth of the water they saw the bone of those who have die before , and in the wave themselves men and woman be struggle , and but few pass over .
Only the child have no fear , and reach the other side in safety .
Still , though the chief and the young girl quail in terror at these horrible sight and sound , no harm come to them , for their life have be free from evil , and the Master of Life have say that no evil should happen unto them .
So they reach unhurt the shore of the Happy Island , and wander through the flowery field and by the bank of rush stream , and they know not hunger nor thirst ; neither cold nor heat .
The air feed them and the sun warm them , and they forget the dead , for they saw no graf , and the young man 's thought turn not to war , neither to the hunting of animal .
And gladly would these two have walk thus for ever , but in the murmur of the wind he hear the Master of Life say to him , ` Return whither you come , for I have work for you to do , and your people need you , and for many year you shall rule over them .
At the gate my messenger await you , and you shall take again your body which you leave behind , and he will show you what you be to do .
Listen to him , and have patience , and in time to come you shall rejoin her whom you must now leave , for she be accept , and will remain ever young and beautiful , a when I call her hence from the Land of Snows . '
THE WHITE DUCK Once upon a time a great and powerful King marry a lovely Princess .
No couple be ever so happy ; but before their honeymoon be over they be force to part , for the King have to go on a warlike expedition to a far country , and leave his young wife alone at home .
Bitter be the tear she shed , while her husband seek in vain to soothe her with word of comfort and counsel , warn her , above all thing , never to leave the castle , to hold no intercourse with stranger , to beware of evil counsellor , and especially to be on her guard against strange woman .
And the Queen promise faithfully to obey her royal lord and master in these four matter .
So when the King set out on his expedition she shut herself up with her lady in her own apartment , and spend her time in spin and weaving , and in thinking of her royal husband .
Often she be very sad and lonely , and it happen that one day while she be seat at the window , let salt tear drop on her work , an old woman , a kind , homely-looking old body , step up to the window , and , lean upon her crutch , address the Queen in friendly , flatter tone , say : ` Why be you sad and cast down , fair Queen ?
You should not mope all day in your room , but should come out into the green garden , and hear the bird sing with joy among the tree , and see the butterfly flutter above the flower , and hear the bee and insect hum , and watch the sunbeams chase the dew-drops through the rose-leaves and in the lily-cups .
All the brightness outside would help to drive away your care , O Queen . '
For long the Queen resist her coaxing word , remember the promise she have give the King , her husband ; but at last she think to herself : After all , what harm would it do if I be to go into the garden for a short time and enjoy myself among the tree and flower , and the singing bird and flutter butterfly and hum insect , and look at the dew-drops hiding from the sunbeam in the heart of the rose and lily , and wander about in the sunshine , instead of remain all day in this room ?
For she have no idea that the kind-looking old woman lean on her crutch be in reality a wicked witch , who envy the Queen her good fortune , and be determine to ruin her .
And so , in all ignorance , the Queen follow her out into the garden and listen to her smooth , flatter word .
Now , in the middle of the garden there be a pond of water , clear a crystal , and the old woman say to the Queen : ` The day be so warm , and the sun 's ray so scorch , that the water in the pond look very cool and inviting .
Would you not like to bathe in it , fair Queen ? '
` No , I think not , ' answer the Queen ; but the next moment she regret her word , and think to herself : Why should n't I bathe in that cool , fresh water ?
No harm could come of it .
And , so say , she slip off her robe and step into the water .
But scarcely have her tender foot touch the cool ripple when she felt a great shove on her shoulder , and the wicked witch have push her into the deep water , exclaim : ` Swim henceforth , White Duck ! '
And the witch herself assume the form of the Queen , and deck herself out in the royal robe , and sit among the Court lady , await the King 's return .
And suddenly the tramp of horse ' hoof be hear , and the barking of dog , and the witch hasten forward to meet the royal carriage , and , throw her arm round the King 's neck , kiss him .
And in his great joy the King do not know that the woman he hold in his arm be not his own dear wife , but a wicked witch .
In the meantime , outside the palace wall , the poor White Duck swim up and down the pond ; and near it lay three egg , out of which there come one morning two little fluffy duckling and a little ugly drake .
And the White Duck bring the little creature up , and they paddle after her in the pond , and catch gold-fish , and hop upon the bank and waddle about , ruffle their feather and say ` Quack , quack ' a they strut about on the green bank of the pond .
But their mother use to warn them not to stray too far , tell them that a wicked witch live in the castle beyond the garden , add , ` She have ruin me , and she will do her best to ruin you . '
But the young one do not listen to their mother , and , play about the garden one day , they stray close up to the castle windows .
The witch at once recognise them by their smell , and ground her teeth with anger ; but she hide her feeling , and , pretend to be very kind she call them to her and joke with them , and lead them into a beautiful room , where she give them food to eat , and show them a soft cushion on which they might sleep .
Then she leave them and go down into the palace kitchens , where she tell the servant to sharpen the knife , and to make a great fire ready , and hang a large kettleful of water over it .
In the meantime the two little duckling have fall asleep , and the little drake lay between them , cover up by their wing , to be keep warm under their feather .
But the little drake could not go to sleep , and a he lay there wide awake in the night he hear the witch come to the door and say : ` Little one , be you asleep ? '
And the little drake answer for the other two : ` We can not sleep , we wake and weep , Sharp be the knife , to take our life ; The fire be hot , now boil the pot , And so we wake , and lie and quake . '
` They be not asleep yet , ' mutter the witch to herself ; and she walk up and down in the passage , and then come back to the door , and say : ` Little one , be you asleep ? '
And again the little drake answer for his sister : ` We can not sleep , we wake and weep , Sharp be the knife , to take our life ; The fire be hot , now boil the pot , And so we wake , and lie and quake . '
` Just the same answer , ' mutter the witch ; ' I think I 'll go in and see . '
So she open the door gently , and see the two little duckling sound asleep , she there and then kill them .
The next morning the White Duck wander round the pond in a distracted manner , look for her little one ; she call and she search , but could find no trace of them .
And in her heart she have a foreboding that evil have befall them , and she flutter up out of the water and fly to the palace .
And there , lay out on the marble floor of the court , dead and stone cold , be her three child .
The White Duck throw herself upon them , and , cover up their little body with her wing , she cry : ` Quack , quack -- my little love !
Quack , quack -- my turtle-doves !
I bring you up with grief and pain , And now before my eye you 're slain .
I give you always of the best ; I keep you warm in my soft nest .
I love and watch you day and night -- You be my joy , my one delight . '
The King hear the sad complaint of the White Duck , and call to the witch : ` Wife , what a wonder be this ?
Listen to that White Duck . '
But the witch answer , ` My dear husband , what do you mean ?
There be nothing wonderful in a duck 's quacking .
Here , servant !
Chase that duck out of the courtyard . '
But though the servant chase and chivy , they could not get rid of the duck ; for she circle round and round , and always come back to the spot where her child lay , cry : ` Quack , quack -- my little love !
Quack , quack -- my turtle-doves !
The wicked witch your life do take -- The wicked witch , the cunning snake .
First she steal my King away , Then my child do she slay .
Changed me , from a happy wife , To a duck for all my life .
Would I be the Queen again ; Would that you have never be slain . '
And a the King hear her word he begin to suspect that he have be deceive , and he call out to the servant , ` Catch that duck , and bring it here . '
But , though they run to and fro , the duck always flee past them , and would not let herself be catch .
So the King himself step down amongst them , and instantly the duck flutter down into his hand .
And a he stroke her wing she be change into a beautiful woman , and he recognise his dear wife .
And she tell him that a bottle would be find in her nest in the garden , contain some drop from the spring of healing .
And it be bring to her ; and the duckling and little drake be sprinkle with the water , and from the little dead body three lovely child arise .
And the King and Queen be overjoy when they saw their child , and they all live happily together in the beautiful palace .
But the wicked witch be take by the King 's command , and she come to no good end .
THE WITCH AND HER SERVANTS -LRB- 22 -RRB- -LRB- 22 -RRB- From the Russian .
Kletke .
Long time ago there live a King who have three son ; the eldest be call Szabo , the second Warza , and the young Iwanich .
One beautiful spring morning the King be walk through his garden with these three son , gaze with admiration at the various fruit-trees , some of which be a mass of blossom , whilst others be bow to the ground lade with rich fruit .
During their wandering they come unperceived on a piece of waste land where three splendid tree grow .
The King look on them for a moment , and then , shake his head sadly , he pass on in silence .
The son , who could not understand why he do this , ask him the reason of his dejection , and the King tell them a follow : ` These three tree , which I can not see without sorrow , be plant by me on this spot when I be a youth of twenty .
A celebrated magician , who have give the seed to my father , promise him that they would grow into the three fine tree the world have ever see .
My father do not live to see his word come true ; but on his death-bed he bid me transplant them here , and to look after them with the great care , which I accordingly do .
At last , after the lapse of five long year , I notice some blossom on the branch , and a few day later the most exquisite fruit my eye have ever see . '
I give my head-gardener the strict order to watch the tree carefully , for the magician have warn my father that if one unripe fruit be pluck from the tree , all the rest would become rotten at once .
When it be quite ripe the fruit would become a golden yellow .
` Every day I gaze on the lovely fruit , which become gradually more and more tempting-looking , and it be all I could do not to break the magician 's command .
` One night I dream that the fruit be perfectly ripe ; I eat some of it , and it be more delicious than anything I have ever taste in real life .
As soon a I awake I send for the gardener and ask him if the fruit on the three tree have not ripen in the night to perfection .
` But instead of reply , the gardener throw himself at my foot and swore that he be innocent .

` Grieved a I be over the theft , I do not punish the gardener , of whose fidelity I be well assure , but I determine to pluck off all the fruit in the following year before it be ripe , a I have not much belief in the magician 's warning . '

For some time past I have give up even have the tree watch . '
When the King have finish his story , Szabo , his eldest son , say to him : ` Forgive me , father , if I say I think you be mistake .
I be sure there be many men in your kingdom who could protect these tree from the cunning art of a thieving magician ; I myself , who a your eldest son claim the first right to do so , will mount guard over the fruit this very night . '
