The whole capital be in a stir , and everyone share in the King 's joy ; the Prince alone take no part in the festivity .
While the King be at a banquet , Iwanich take some purse of gold , and mount the quick horse in the royal stable , he speed off like the wind without a single soul be any the wiser .
It be only on the next day that they miss him ; the King be very distressed at his disappearance , and send search-parties all over the kingdom to look for him , but in vain ; and after six month they give him up a dead , and in another six month they have forget all about him .
But in the meantime the Prince , with the help of his ring , have have a most successful journey , and no evil have befall him .
At the end of three month he come to the entrance of a huge forest , which look a if it have never be tread by human foot before , and which seem to stretch out indefinitely .
The Prince be about to enter the wood by a little path he have discover , when he hear a voice shout to him : ` Hold , youth !
Whither be you go ? '
Iwanich turn round , and saw a tall , gaunt-looking man , clad in miserable rag , lean on a crooked staff and seat at the foot of an oak tree , which be so much the same colour a himself that it be little wonder the Prince have ride past the tree without notice him .
` Where else should I be go , ' he say , ` than through the wood ? '
` Through the wood ? '
say the old man in amazement .
` It 's easily see that you have hear nothing of this forest , that you rush so blindly to meet your doom .
Well , listen to me before you ride any far ; let me tell you that this wood hide in it depth a countless number of the fierce tiger , hyena , wolf , bear , and snake , and all sort of other monster .
If I be to cut you and your horse up into tiny morsel and throw them to the beast , there would n't be one bit for each hundred of them .
Take my advice , therefore , and if you wish to save your life follow some other path . '
The Prince be rather take aback by the old man 's word , and consider for a minute what he should do ; then look at his ring , and perceive that it sparkle as brightly a ever , he call out : ` If this wood hold even more terrible thing than it do , I can not help myself , for I must go through it . '
Here he spur his horse and rode on ; but the old beggar scream so loudly after him that the Prince turn round and ride back to the oak tree . '
I be really sorry for you , ' say the beggar , ` but if you be quite determine to brave the danger of the forest , let me at least give you a piece of advice which will help you against these monster .
` Take this bagful of bread-crumbs and this live hare .
I will make you a present of them both , a I be anxious to save your life ; but you must leave your horse behind you , for it would stumble over the fall tree or get entangle in the brier and thorn .
When you have go about a hundred yard into the wood the wild beast will surround you .
Then you must instantly seize your bag , and scatter the bread-crumbs among them .
They will rush to eat them up greedily , and when you have scatter the last crumb you must lose no time in throw the hare to them ; as soon a the hare feel itself on the ground it will run away as quickly a possible , and the wild beast will turn to pursue it .
In this way you will be able to get through the wood unhurt . '
Iwanich thank the old man for his counsel , dismount from his horse , and , take the bag and the hare in his arm , he enter the forest .
He have hardly lose sight of his gaunt grey friend when he hear growl and snarl in the thicket close to him , and before he have time to think he find himself surround by the most dreadful-looking creature .
On one side he saw the glitter eye of a cruel tiger , on the other the gleam teeth of a great she-wolf ; here a huge bear growl fiercely , and there a horrible snake coil itself in the grass at his foot .
But Iwanich do not forget the old man 's advice , and quickly put his hand into the bag and take out a many bread-crumbs a he could hold in his hand at a time .
He throw them to the beast , but soon the bag grow light and light , and the Prince begin to feel a little frightened .
And now the last crumb be go , and the hungry beast throng round him , greedy for fresh prey .
Then he seize the hare and throw it to them .
No sooner do the little creature feel itself on the ground than it lay back it ear and fly through the wood like an arrow from a bow , closely pursue by the wild beast , and the Prince be leave alone .
He look at his ring , and when he saw that it sparkle as brightly a ever he go straight on through the forest .
He have n't go very far when he saw a most extraordinary look man come towards him .
He be not more than three foot high , his leg be quite crook , and all his body be cover with prickle like a hedgehog .
Two lion walk with him , fasten to his side by the two end of his long beard .
He stop the Prince and ask him in a harsh voice : ` Are you the man who have just feed my body-guard ? '
Iwanich be so startled that he could hardly reply , but the little man continue : ' I be most grateful to you for your kindness ; what can I give you a a reward ? '
` All I ask , ' reply Iwanich , ` be , that I should be allow to go through this wood in safety . '
` Most certainly , ' answer the little man ; ` and for great security I will give you one of my lion a a protector .
But when you leave this wood and come near a palace which do not belong to my domain , let the lion go , in order that he may not fall into the hand of an enemy and be kill . '
With these word he loosen the lion from his beard and bid the beast guard the youth carefully .
With this new protector Iwanich wander on through the forest , and though he come upon a great many more wolf , hyena , leopard , and other wild beast , they always keep at a respectful distance when they saw what sort of an escort the Prince have with him .
Iwanich hurry through the wood as quickly a his leg would carry him , but , nevertheless , hour after hour go by and not a trace of a green field or a human habitation meet his eye .
At length , towards evening , the mass of tree grow more transparent , and through the interlaced branch a wide plain be visible .
At the exit of the wood the lion stand still , and the Prince take leave of him , have first thank him warmly for his kind protection .
It have become quite dark , and Iwanich be force to wait for daylight before continue his journey .
He make himself a bed of grass and leaf , light a fire of dry branch , and sleep soundly till the next morning .
Then he get up and walk towards a beautiful white palace which he saw gleam in the distance .
In about an hour he reach the building , and open the door he walk in .
After wander through many marble hall , he come to a huge staircase make of porphyry , lead down to a lovely garden .
The Prince burst into a shout of joy when he suddenly perceive Militza in the centre of a group of girl who be weave wreath of flower with which to deck their mistress .
As soon a Militza saw the Prince she run up to him and embrace him tenderly ; and after he have tell her all his adventure , they go into the palace , where a sumptuous meal await them .
Then the Princess call her court together , and introduce Iwanich to them a her future husband .
Preparations be at once make for the wedding , which be hold soon after with great pomp and magnificence .
Three month of great happiness follow , when Militza receive one day an invitation to visit her mother 's sister .
Although the Princess be very unhappy at leave her husband , she do not like to refuse the invitation , and , promise to return in seven day at the late , she take a tender farewell of the Prince , and say : ` Before I go I will hand you over all the key of the castle .
Go everywhere and do anything you like ; only one thing I beg and beseech you , do not open the little iron door in the north tower , which be close with seven lock and seven bolt ; for if you do , we shall both suffer for it . '
Iwanich promise what she ask , and Militza depart , repeat her promise to return in seven day .
When the Prince find himself alone he begin to be torment by pang of curiosity a to what the room in the tower contain .
For two day he resist the temptation to go and look , but on the third he could stand it no longer , and take a torch in his hand he hurry to the tower , and unfasten one lock after the other of the little iron door until it burst open .
What an unexpected sight meet his gaze !
The Prince perceive a small room black with smoke , light up feebly by a fire from which issue long blue flame .
Over the fire hang a huge cauldron full of boil pitch , and fasten into the cauldron by iron chain stand a wretched man scream with agony .
Iwanich be much horrify at the sight before him , and ask the man what terrible crime he have commit to be punish in this dreadful fashion . '
I will tell you everything , ' say the man in the cauldron ; ` but first relieve my torment a little , I implore you . '
` And how can I do that ? '
ask the Prince .
` With a little water , ' reply the man ; ` only sprinkle a few drop over me and I shall feel well . '
The Prince , move by pity , without think what he be do , run to the courtyard of the castle , and fill a jug with water , which he pour over the man in the cauldron .
In a moment a most fearful crash be heard , a if all the pillar of the palace be give way , and the palace itself , with tower and door , window and the cauldron , whirl round the bewildered Prince 's head .
This continue for a few minute , and then everything vanish into thin air , and Iwanich find himself suddenly alone upon a desolate heath cover with rock and stone .
The Prince , who now realise what his heedlessness have do , curse too late his spirit of curiosity .
In his despair he wander on over the heath , never look where he put his foot , and full of sorrowful thought .
At last he saw a light in the distance , which come from a miserable-looking little hut .
The owner of it be none other than the kind-hearted gaunt grey beggar who have give the Prince the bag of bread-crumbs and the hare .
Without recognise Iwanich , he open the door when he knock and give him shelter for the night .
On the following morning the Prince ask his host if he could get him any work to do , a he be quite unknown in the neighbourhood , and have not enough money to take him home .
` My son , ' reply the old man , ` all this country round here be uninhabited ; I myself have to wander to distant village for my living , and even then I do not very often find enough to satisfy my hunger .
But if you would like to take service with the old witch Corva , go straight up the little stream which flow below my hut for about three hour , and you will come to a sand-hill on the left-hand side ; that be where she live . '
Iwanich thank the gaunt grey beggar for his information , and go on his way .
After walk for about three hour the Prince come upon a dreary-looking grey stone wall ; this be the back of the building and do not attract him ; but when he come upon the front of the house he find it even less inviting , for the old witch have surround her dwelling with a fence of spike , on every one of which a man 's skull be stick .
In this horrible enclosure stand a small black house , which have only two grate window , all cover with cobweb , and a battered iron door .
The Prince knock , and a rasp woman 's voice tell him to enter .
Iwanich open the door , and find himself in a smoke-begrimed kitchen , in the presence of a hideous old woman who be warm her skinny hand at a fire .
The Prince offer to become her servant , and the old hag tell him she be badly in want of one , and he seem to be just the person to suit her .
When Iwanich ask what his work , and how much his wage would be , the witch bid him follow her , and lead the way through a narrow damp passage into a vault , which serve a a stable .
Here he perceive two pitch-black horse in a stall .
` You see before you , ' say the old woman , ' a mare and her foal ; you have nothing to do but to lead them out to the field every day , and to see that neither of them run away from you .
If you look after them both for a whole year I will give you anything you like to ask ; but if , on the other hand , you let either of the animal escape you , your last hour be come , and your head shall be stick on the last spike of my fence .
The other spike , a you see , be already adorn , and the skull be all those of different servant I have have who have fail to do what I demand . '
Iwanich , who think he could not be much bad off than he be already , agree to the witch 's proposal .
At daybreak nest morning he drive his horse to the field , and bring them back in the evening without their ever have attempt to break away from him .
The witch stand at her door and receive him kindly , and set a good meal before him .
So it continue for some time , and all go well with the Prince .
Early every morning he lead the horse out to the field , and bring them home safe and sound in the evening .
One day , while he be watch the horse , he come to the bank of a river , and saw a big fish , which through some mischance have be cast on the land , struggle hard to get back into the water .
Iwanich , who felt sorry for the poor creature , seize it in his arm and fling it into the stream .
But no sooner do the fish find itself in the water again , than , to the Prince 's amazement , it swim up to the bank and say : ` My kind benefactor , how can I reward you for your goodness ? ' '
I desire nothing , ' answer the Prince . '
I be quite content to have be able to be of some service to you . '
` You must do me the favour , ' reply the fish , ` to take a scale from my body , and keep it carefully .
If you should ever need my help , throw it into the river , and I will come to your aid at once . '
Iwanich bow , loosen a scale from the body of the grateful beast , put it carefully away , and return home .
A short time after this , when he be go early one morning to the usual grazing place with his horse , he notice a flock of bird assemble together make a great noise and fly wildly backwards and forward .
Full of curiosity , Iwanich hurry up to the spot , and saw that a large number of raven have attack an eagle , and although the eagle be big and powerful and be make a brave fight , it be overpower at last by number , and have to give in .
But the Prince , who be sorry for the poor bird , seize the branch of a tree and hit out at the raven with it ; terrify at this unexpected onslaught they fly away , leave many of their number dead or wound on the battlefield .
As soon a the eagle saw itself free from it tormentor it pluck a feather from it wing , and , hand it to the Prince , say : ` Here , my kind benefactor , take this feather a a proof of my gratitude ; should you ever be in need of my help blow this feather into the air , and I will help you as much a be in my power . '
Iwanich thank the bird , and place the feather beside the scale he drive the horse home .
Another day he have wander far than usual , and come close to a farmyard ; the place please the Prince , and a there be plenty of good grass for the horse he determine to spend the day there .
Just a he be sit down under a tree he hear a cry close to him , and saw a fox which have be catch in a trap place there by the farmer .
In vain do the poor beast try to free itself ; then the good-natured Prince come once more to the rescue , and let the fox out of the trap .
The fox thank him heartily , tore two hair out of his bushy tail , and say : ` Should you ever stand in need of my help throw these two hair into the fire , and in a moment I shall be at your side ready to obey you . '
Iwanich put the fox 's hair with the scale and the feather , and a it be get dark he hasten home with his horse .
In the meantime his service be draw near to an end , and in three more day the year be up , and he would be able to get his reward and leave the witch .
On the first evening of these last three day , when he come home and be eat his supper , he notice the old woman steal into the stable .
The Prince follow her secretly to see what she be go to do .
He crouch down in the doorway and hear the wicked witch tell the horse to wait next morning till Iwanich be asleep , and then to go and hide themselves in the river , and to stay there till she tell them to return ; and if they do n't do a she tell them the old woman threaten to beat them till they bleed .
When Iwanich hear all this he go back to his room , determine that nothing should induce him to fall asleep next day .
On the following morning he lead the mare and foal to the field a usual , but bound a cord round them both which he keep in his hand .
But after a few hour , by the magic art of the old witch , he be overpower by sleep , and the mare and foal escape and do a they have be tell to do .
The Prince do not awake till late in the evening ; and when he do , he find , to his horror , that the horse have disappear .
Filled with despair , he curse the moment when he have enter the service of the cruel witch , and already he saw his head stick up on the sharp spike beside the others .
Then he suddenly remember the fish 's scale , which , with the eagle 's feather and the fox 's hair , he always carry about with him .
He draw the scale from his pocket , and hurry to the river he throw it in .
In a minute the grateful fish swam towards the bank on which Iwanich be stand , and say : ` What do you command , my friend and benefactor ? '
The Prince reply : ' I have to look after a mare and foal , and they have run away from me and have hide themselves in the river ; if you wish to save my life drive them back to the land . '
` Wait a moment , ' answer the fish , ` and I and my friend will soon drive them out of the water . '
With these word the creature disappear into the depth of the stream .
Almost immediately a rush hissing sound be hear in the water , the wave dash against the bank , the foam be toss into the air , and the two horse leap suddenly on to the dry land , tremble and shake with fear .
Iwanich sprang at once on to the mare 's back , seize the foal by it bridle , and hasten home in the high spirit .
When the witch saw the Prince bring the horse home she could hardly conceal her wrath , and as soon a she have place Iwanich 's supper before him she steal away again to the stable .
The Prince follow her , and hear her scold the beast harshly for not have hide themselves good .
She bid them wait next morning till Iwanich be asleep and then to hide themselves in the cloud , and to remain there till she call .
If they do not do a she tell them she would beat them till they bleed .
The next morning , after Iwanich have lead his horse to the field , he fell once more into a magic sleep .
The horse at once ran away and hid themselves in the cloud , which hang down from the mountain in soft billowy mass .
When the Prince awoke and find that both the mare and the foal have disappear , he bethink him at once of the eagle , and take the feather out of his pocket he blow it into the air .
In a moment the bird swoop down beside him and ask : ` What do you wish me to do ? '
` My mare and foal , ' reply the Prince , ` have run away from me , and have hide themselves in the cloud ; if you wish to save my life , restore both animal to me . '
` Wait a minute , ' answer the eagle ; ` with the help of my friend I will soon drive them back to you . '
With these word the bird fly up into the air and disappear among the cloud .
Almost directly Iwanich saw his two horse be drive towards him by a host of eagle of all size .
He catch the mare and foal , and have thank the eagle he drive them cheerfully home again .
The old witch be more disgusted than ever when she saw him appear , and have set his supper before him she steal into the stable , and Iwanich hear her abuse the horse for not have hide themselves well in the cloud .
Then she bid them hide themselves next morning , as soon a Iwanich be asleep , in the King 's hen-house , which stand on a lonely part of the heath , and to remain there till she call .
If they fail to do a she tell them she would certainly beat them this time till they bleed .
On the following morning the Prince drive his horse a usual to the field .
After he have be overpower by sleep , a on the former day , the mare and foal run away and hid themselves in the royal hen house .
When the Prince awoke and find the horse go he determine to appeal to the fox ; so , light a fire , he throw the two hair into it , and in a few moment the fox stand beside him and ask : ` In what way can I serve you ? ' '
I wish to know , ' reply Iwanich , ` where the King 's hen-house be . '
` Hardly an hour 's walk from here , ' answer the fox , and offer to show the Prince the way to it .
While they be walk along the fox ask him what he want to do at the royal hen-house .
The Prince tell him of the misfortune that have befall him , and of the necessity of recover the mare and foal .
` That be no easy matter , ' reply the fox .
` But wait a moment .
I have an idea .
Stand at the door of the hen-house , and wait there for your horse .
In the meantime I will slip in among the hen through a hole in the wall and give them a good chase , so that the noise they make will arouse the royal henwives , and they will come to see what be the matter .
When they see the horse they will at once imagine them to be the cause of the disturbance , and will drive them out .
Then you must lay hand on the mare and foal and catch them .
All turn out exactly a the sly fox have foreseen .
The Prince swung himself on the mare , seize the foal by it bridle , and hurry home .
While he be rid over the heath in the high of spirit the mare suddenly say to her rider : ` You be the first person who have ever succeed in outwit the old witch Corva , and now you may ask what reward you like for your service .
If you promise never to betray me I will give you a piece of advice which you will do well to follow . '
The Prince promise never to betray her confidence , and the mare continue : ` Ask nothing else a a reward than my foal , for it have not it like in the world , and be not to be buy for love or money ; for it can go from one end of the earth to another in a few minute .
Of course the cunning Corva will do her best to dissuade you from take the foal , and will tell you that it be both idle and sickly ; but do not believe her , and stick to your point . '
Iwanich long to possess such an animal , and promise the mare to follow her advice .
This time Corva receive him in the most friendly manner , and set a sumptuous repast before him .
As soon a he have finish she ask him what reward he demand for his year 's service .
` Nothing more nor less , ' reply the Prince , ` than the foal of your mare . '
The witch pretend to be much astonish at his request , and say that he deserve something much well than the foal , for the beast be lazy and nervous , blind in one eye , and , in short , be quite worthless .
But the Prince know what he want , and when the old witch saw that he have make up his mind to have the foal , she say , ' I be oblige to keep my promise and to hand you over the foal ; and a I know who you be and what you want , I will tell you in what way the animal will be useful to you .
The man in the cauldron of boil pitch , whom you set free , be a mighty magician ; through your curiosity and thoughtlessness Militza come into his power , and he have transport her and her castle and belonging into a distant country .
` You be the only person who can kill him ; and in consequence he fear you to such an extent that he have set spy to watch you , and they report your movement to him daily .
` When you have reach him , beware of speak a single word to him , or you will fall into the power of his friend .
Seize him at once by the beard and dash him to the ground . '
Iwanich thank the old witch , mount his foal , put spur to it side , and they fly like lightning through the air .
Already it be grow dark , when Iwanich perceive some figure in the distance ; they soon come up to them , and then the Prince saw that it be the magician and his friend who be drive through the air in a carriage draw by owl .
When the magician find himself face to face with Iwanich , without hope of escape , he turn to him with false friendliness and say : ` Thrice my kind benefactor ! '
But the Prince , without say a word , seize him at once by his beard and dash him to the ground .
At the same moment the foal sprang on the top of the magician and kick and stamp on him with his hoof till he die .
Then Iwanich find himself once more in the palace of his bride , and Militza herself fly into his arm .
From this time forward they live in undisturbed peace and happiness till the end of their life .
THE MAGIC RING Once upon a time there live an old couple who have one son call Martin .
Now when the old man 's time have come , he stretch himself out on his bed and die .
Though all his life long he have toil and moil , he only leave his widow and son two hundred florin .
The old woman determine to put by the money for a rainy day ; but ala !
the rainy day be close at hand , for their meal be all consume , and who be prepare to face starvation with two hundred florin at their disposal ?
So the old woman count out a hundred of her florin , and give them to Martin , tell him to go into the town and lay in a store of meal for a year .
So Martin start off for the town .
When he reach the meat-market he find the whole place in turmoil , and a great noise of angry voice and barking of dog .
Mixing in the crowd , he notice a stag-hound which the butcher have catch and tie to a post , and which be be flog in a merciless manner .
Overcome with pity , Martin speak to the butcher , say : ` Friends , why be you beat the poor dog so cruelly ? '
` We have every right to beat him , ' they reply ; ` he have just devour a newly-killed pig . '
` Leave off beat him , ' say Martin , ` and sell him to me instead . '
` If you choose to buy him , ' answer the butcher derisively ; ` but for such a treasure we wo n't take a penny less than a hundred florin . ' '
A hundred ! '
exclaim Martin .
` Well , so be it , if you will not take less ; ' and , take the money out of his pocket , he hand it over in exchange for the dog , whose name be Schurka .
When Martin get home , his mother meet him with the question : ` Well , what have you buy ? '
` Schurka , the dog , ' reply Martin , point to his new possession .
Whereupon his mother become very angry , and abuse him roundly .
He ought to be ashamed of himself , when there be scarcely a handful of meal in the house , to have spend the money on a useless brute like that .
On the following day she send him back to the town , say , ` Here , take our last hundred florin , and buy provision with them .
I have just empty the last grain of meal out of the chest , and bake a bannock ; but it wo n't last over to-morrow . '
Just a Martin be enter the town he meet a rough-looking peasant who be drag a cat after him by a string which be fasten round the poor beast 's neck .
` Stop , ' cry Martin ; ` where be you drag that poor cat ? ' '
I mean to drown him , ' be the answer .
` What harm have the poor beast do ? '
say Martin .
` It have just kill a goose , ' reply the peasant .
` Do n't drown him , sell him to me instead , ' beg Martin .
` Not for a hundred florin , ' be the answer .
` Surely for a hundred florin you 'll sell it ? '
say Martin .
` See !
here be the money ; ' and , so say , he hand him the hundred florin , which the peasant pocket , and Martin take possession of the cat , which be call Waska .
When he reach his home his mother greet him with the question : ` Well , what have you bring back ? ' '
I have bring this cat , Waska , ' answer Martin .
` And what besides ? ' '
I have no money over to buy anything else with , ' reply Martin .
` You useless ne'er - do-weel ! '
exclaim his mother in a great passion .
` Leave the house at once , and go and beg your bread among stranger ; ' and a Martin do not dare to contradict her , he call Schurka and Waska and start off with them to the near village in search of work .
On the way he meet a rich peasant , who ask him where he be go . '
I want to get work a a day labourer , ' he answer .
` Come along with me , then .
But I must tell you I engage my labourer without wage .
If you serve me faithfully for a year , I promise you it shall be for your advantage . '
So Martin consent , and for a year he work diligently , and serve his master faithfully , not spar himself in any way .
When the day of reckon have come the peasant lead him into a barn , and point to two full sack , say : ` Take whichever of these you choose . '
Martin examine the content of the sack , and see that one be full of silver and the other of sand , he say to himself : ` There must be some trick about this ; I have well take the sand . '
And throw the sack over his shoulder he start out into the world , in search of fresh work .
On and on he walk , and at last he reach a great gloomy wood .
In the middle of the wood he come upon a meadow , where a fire be burn , and in the midst of the fire , surround by flame , be a lovely damsel , more beautiful than anything that Martin have ever see , and when she saw him she call to him : ` Martin , if you would win happiness , save my life .
Extinguish the flame with the sand that you earn in payment of your faithful service . '
` Truly , ' think Martin to himself , ` it would be more sensible to save a fellow-being 's life with this sand than to drag it about on one 's back , see what a weight it be . '
And forthwith he lower the sack from his shoulder and empty it content on the flame , and instantly the fire be extinguish ; but at the same moment lo !
and behold the lovely damsel turn into a Serpent , and , dart upon him , coil itself round his neck , and whisper lovingly in his ear : ` Do not be afraid of me , Martin ; I love you , and will go with you through the world .
But first you must follow me boldly into my Father 's Kingdom , underneath the earth ; and when we get there , remember this -- he will offer you gold and silver , and dazzle gem , but do not touch them .
Ask him , instead , for the ring which he wear on his little finger , for in that ring lie a magic power ; you have only to throw it from one hand to the other , and at once twelve young men will appear , who will do your bidding , no matter how difficult , in a single night . '
So they start on their way , and after much wandering they reach a spot where a great rock rise straight up in the middle of the road .
Instantly the Serpent uncoil itself from his neck , and , a it touch the damp earth , it resume the shape of the lovely damsel .
Pointing to the rock , she show him an opening just big enough for a man to wriggle through .
Passing into it , they enter a long underground passage , which lead out on to a wide field , above which spread a blue sky .
In the middle of the field stand a magnificent castle , build out of porphyry , with a roof of gold and with glittering battlement .
And his beautiful guide tell him that this be the palace in which her father live and reign over his kingdom in the Under-world .
Together they enter the palace , and be receive by the King with great kindness .
Turning to his daughter , he say : ` My child , I have almost give up the hope of ever see you again .
Where have you be all these year ? '
` My father , ' she reply , ' I owe my life to this youth , who save me from a terrible death . '
Upon which the King turn to Martin with a gracious smile , say : ' I will reward your courage by grant you whatever your heart desire .
Take a much gold , silver , and precious stone a you choose . ' '
I thank you , mighty King , for your gracious offer , ' answer Martin , ' ` but I do not covet either gold , silver , or precious stone ; yet if you will grant me a favour , give me , I beg , the ring from off the little finger of your royal hand .
Every time my eye fall on it I shall think of your gracious Majesty , and when I marry I shall present it to my bride . '
So the King take the ring from his finger and give it to Martin , say : ` Take it , good youth ; but with it I make one condition -- you be never to confide to anyone that this be a magic ring .
If you do , you will straightway bring misfortune on yourself . '
Martin take the ring , and , have thank the King , he set out on the same road by which he have come down into the Under-world .
When he have regain the upper air he start for his old home , and have find his mother still live in the old house where he have leave her , they settle down together very happily .
So uneventful be their life that it almost seem a if it would go on in this way always , without let or hindrance .
But one day it suddenly come into his mind that he would like to get married , and , moreover , that he would choose a very grand wife -- a King 's daughter , in short .
But a he do not trust himself a a wooer , he determine to send his old mother on the mission .
` You must go to the King , ' he say to her , ` and demand the hand of his lovely daughter in marriage for me . '
` What be you think of , my son ? '
answer the old woman , aghast at the idea .
` Why can not you marry someone in your own rank ?
That would be far more fitting than to send a poor old woman like me a-wooing to the King 's Court for the hand of a Princess .
Why , it be as much a our head be worth .
Neither my life nor yours would be worth anything if I go on such a fool 's errand . '
` Never fear , little mother , ' answer Martin .
` Trust me ; all will be well .
But see that you do not come back without an answer of some kind . '
And so , obedient to her son 's behest , the old woman hobble off to the palace , and , without be hinder , reach the courtyard , and begin to mount the flight of step lead to the royal presence chamber .
At the head of the landing row of courtier be collect in magnificent attire , who star at the queer old figure , and call to her , and explain to her , with every kind of sign , that it be strictly forbidden to mount those step .
But their stern word and forbid gesture make no impression whatever on the old woman , and she resolutely continue to climb the stair , bent on carry out her son 's order .
Upon this some of the courtier seize her by the arm , and hold her back by sheer force , at which she set up such a yell that the King himself hear it , and step out on to the balcony to see what be the matter .
When he behold the old woman fling her arm wildly about , and hear her scream that she would not leave the place till she have lay her case before the King , he order that she should be bring into his presence .
And forthwith she be conduct into the golden presence chamber , where , lean back amongst cushion of royal purple , the King sat , surround by his counsellor and courtier .
Courtesying low , the old woman stand silent before him .
` Well , my good old dame , what can I do for you ? '
ask the King . '
I have come , ' reply Martin 's mother -- ` and your Majesty must not be angry with me -- I have come a-wooing . '
` Is the woman out of her mind ? '
say the King , with an angry frown .
But Martin 's mother answer boldly : ` If the King will only listen patiently to me , and give me a straightforward answer , he will see that I be not out of my mind .
You , O King , have a lovely daughter to give in marriage .
I have a son -- a wooer -- a clever a youth and as good a son-in-law a you will find in your whole kingdom .
There be nothing that he can not do .
Now tell me , O King , plump and plain , will you give your daughter to my son a wife ? '
The King listen to the end of the old woman 's strange request , but every moment his face grow blacker , and his feature sterner ; till all at once he think to himself , ` Is it worth while that I , the King , should be angry with this poor old fool ? '
And all the courtier and counsellor be amaze when they saw the hard line round his mouth and the frown on his brow grow smooth , and hear the mild but mock tone in which he answer the old woman , say : ` If your son be a wonderfully clever a you say , and if there be nothing in the world that he can not do , let him build a magnificent castle , just opposite my palace window , in four and twenty hour .
The palace must be join together by a bridge of pure crystal .
On each side of the bridge there must be grow tree , have golden and silver apple , and with bird of Paradise among the branch .
At the right of the bridge there must be a church , with five golden cupola ; in this church your son shall be wed to my daughter , and we will keep the wedding festivity in the new castle .
But if he fail to execute this my royal command , then , a a just but mild monarch , I shall give order that you and he be take , and first dip in tar and then in feather , and you shall be execute in the market-place for the entertainment of my courtier . '
And a smile play round the King 's lip a he finish speaking , and his courtier and counsellor shake with laughter when they think of the old woman 's folly , and praise the King 's wise device , and say to each other , ` What a joke it will be when we see the pair of them tar and feather !
The son be just as able to grow a beard on the palm of his hand a to execute such a task in twenty-four hour . '
Now the poor old woman be mortally afraid and , in a trembling voice she ask : ` Is that really your royal will , O King ?
Must I take this order to my poor son ? '
` Yes , old dame ; such be my command .
If your son carry out my order , he shall be reward with my daughter ; but if he fail , away to the tar-barrel and the stake with you both ! '
On her way home the poor old woman shed bitter tear , and when she saw Martin she tell him what the King have say , and sob out : ` Did n't I tell you , my son , that you should marry someone of your own rank ?
It would have be good for u this day if you have .
As I tell you , my go to Court have be as much a our life be worth , and now we will both be tar and feather , and burnt in the public market-place .
It be terrible ! '
and she moan and cry .
` Never fear , little mother , ' answer Martin ; ` trust me , and you will see all will be well .
You may go to sleep with a quiet mind . '
And , step to the front of the hut , Martin throw his ring from the palm of one hand into the other , upon which twelve youth instantly appear , and demand what he want them to do .
Then he tell them the King 's command , and they answer that by next morning all should be accomplish exactly a the King have order .
Next morning when the King awoke , and look out of his window , to his amazement he behold a magnificent castle , just opposite his own palace , and join to it a bridge of pure crystal .
At each side of the bridge tree be grow , from whose branch hang golden and silver apple , among which bird of Paradise perch .

Now , though the King would much rather have see his future son-in-law tar , feather , and burnt at the stake , he remember his royal oath , and have to make the best of a bad business .
So he take heart of grace , and make Martin a Duke , and give his daughter a rich dowry , and prepare the grand wedding-feast that have ever be see , so that to this day the old people in the country still talk of it .
After the wedding Martin and his royal bride go to dwell in the magnificent new palace , and here Martin live in the great comfort and luxury , such luxury a he have never imagine .
But though he be as happy a the day be long , and as merry a a grig , the King 's daughter fret all day , thinking of the indignity that have be do her in make her marry Martin , the poor widow 's son , instead of a rich young Prince from a foreign country .
So unhappy be she that she spend all her time wonder how she should get rid of her undesirable husband .
And first she determine to learn the secret of his power , and , with flattering , caress word , she try to coax him to tell her how he be so clever that there be nothing in the world that he could not do .
At first he would tell her nothing ; but once , when he be in a yielding mood , she approach him with a win smile on her lovely face , and , speak flatter word to him , she give him a potion to drink , with a sweet , strong taste .
And when he have drunk it Martin 's lip be unsealed , and he tell her that all his power lay in the magic ring that he wear on his finger , and he describe to her how to use it , and , still speak , he fell into a deep sleep .

On the instant the twelve youth appear , and ask her what she command them to do .
Then she tell them that by the next morning they be to do away with the castle , and the bridge , and the church , and put in their stead the humble hut in which Martin use to live with his mother , and that while he sleep her husband be to be carry to his old lowly room ; and that they be to bear her away to the utmost end of the earth , where an old King live who would make her welcome in his palace , and surround her with the state that befit a royal Princess .
` You shall be obey , ' answer the twelve youth at the same moment .
And lo and behold !
the following morning , when the King awoke and look out of his window he behold to his amazement that the palace , bridge , church , and tree have all vanish , and there be nothing in their place but a bare , miserable-looking hut .

But Martin look at his royal father-in-law , and answer never a word .
Then the King be very angry , and , call a council together , he charge Martin with have be guilty of witchcraft , and of have deceive the King , and have make away with the Princess ; and he be condemn to imprisonment in a high stone tower , with neither meat nor drink , till he should die of starvation .
Then , in the hour of his dire necessity , his old friend Schurka -LRB- the dog -RRB- and Waska -LRB- the cat -RRB- remember how Martin have once save them from a cruel death ; and they take counsel together a to how they should help him .
And Schurka growl , and be of opinion that he would like to tear everyone in piece ; but Waska purr meditatively , and scratch the back of her ear with a velvet paw , and remain lose in thought .
At the end of a few minute she have make up her mind , and , turn to Schurka , say : ` Let u go together into the town , and the moment we meet a baker you must make a rush between his leg and upset the tray from off his head ; I will lay hold of the roll , and will carry them off to our master . '
No sooner say than do .
Together the two faithful creature trot off into the town , and very soon they meet a baker bear a tray on his head , and look round on all side , while he cry : ` Fresh roll , sweet cake , Fancy bread of every kind .
Come and buy , come and take , Sure you 'll find it to your mind , ' At that moment Schurka make a rush between his leg -- the baker stumble , the tray be upset , the roll fell to the ground , and , while the man angrily pursue Schurka , Waska manage to drag the roll out of sight behind a bush .
And when a moment later Schurka join her , they set off at full tilt to the stone tower where Martin be a prisoner , take the roll with them .
Waska , be very agile , climb up by the outside to the grate window , and call in an anxious voice : ` Are you alive , master ? '
` Scarcely alive -- almost starve to death , ' answer Martin in a weak voice . '
I little think it would come to this , that I should die of hunger . '
` Never fear , dear master .
Schurka and I will look after you , ' say Waska .
And in another moment she have climb down and bring him back a roll , and then another , and another , till she have bring him the whole tray-load .
Upon which she say : ` Dear master , Schurka and I be go off to a distant kingdom at the utmost end of the earth to fetch you back your magic ring .
You must be careful that the roll last till our return . '
And Waska take leave of her beloved master , and set off with Schurka on their journey .
On and on they travel , look always to right and leave for trace of the Princess , follow up every track , make inquiry of every cat and dog they meet , listen to the talk of every wayfarer they pass ; and at last they hear that the kingdom at the utmost end of the earth where the twelve youth have bear the Princess be not very far off .
And at last one day they reach that distant kingdom , and , go at once to the palace , they begin to make friend with all the dog and cat in the place , and to question them about the Princess and the magic ring ; but no one could tell them much about either .

I will do everything in my power for you ; for I be the King of the Mice , and if I perish the whole race will die out . '
` So be it , ' say Waska . '
I will spare your life ; but in return you must do something for me .
In this castle there live a Princess , the wicked wife of my dear master .
She have steal away his magic ring .
You must get it away from her at whatever cost ; do you hear ?
Till you have do this I wo n't take my claw out of your fur . '
` Good ! '
reply the mouse ; ' I will do what you ask . '
And , so say , he summon all the mouse in his kingdom together .
A countless number of mouse , small and big , brown and grey , assemble , and form a circle round their king , who be a prisoner under Waska 's claw .
Turning to them he say : ` Dear and faithful subject , who ever among you will steal the magic ring from the strange Princess will release me from a cruel death ; and I shall honour him above all the other mouse in the kingdom . '
Instantly a tiny mouse step forward and say : ' I often creep about the Princess 's bedroom at night , and I have notice that she have a ring which she treasure a the apple of her eye .
All day she wear it on her finger , and at night she keep it in her mouth .
I will undertake , sire , to steal away the ring for you . '

And the fluff fly into the Princess 's nose , and into her mouth , and start up she sneeze and cough , and the ring fell out of her mouth on to the coverlet .
In a flash the tiny mouse have seize it , and bring it to Waska a a ransom for the King of the Mice .

` Ah !
Waska , my faithful little cat , be that you ? '
reply a weak voice . '
I be die of hunger .
For three day I have not taste food . '

At these word Martin 's joy know no bound , and he stroke her fondly , and she rub up against him and purr happily , while below Schurka bound in the air , and bark joyfully .

` Fetch me first something to eat and drink , as quickly a possible ; and after that bring musicians hither , and let u have music all day long . '

And Martin 's heart be soften and he forgive his wife , and they live happily together ever after .
And his old mother come and live with him , and he never part with Schurka and Waska ; and I need hardly tell you that he never again let the ring out of his possession .
THE FLOWER QUEEN 'S DAUGHTER -LRB- 23 -RRB- -LRB- 23 -RRB- From the Bukowinaer .
Von Wliolocki .
A young Prince be rid one day through a meadow that stretch for mile in front of him , when he come to a deep open ditch .
He be turn aside to avoid it , when he hear the sound of someone cry in the ditch .
He dismount from his horse , and step along in the direction the sound come from .
To his astonishment he find an old woman , who beg him to help her out of the ditch .
The Prince bend down and lift her out of her living grave , ask her at the same time how she have manage to get there .
` My son , ' answer the old woman , ' I be a very poor woman , and soon after midnight I set out for the neighbouring town in order to sell my egg in the market on the following morning ; but I lose my way in the dark , and fell into this deep ditch , where I might have remain for ever but for your kindness . '
Then the Prince say to her , ` You can hardly walk ; I will put you on my horse and lead you home .
Where do you live ? '
` Over there , at the edge of the forest in the little hut you see in the distance , ' reply the old woman .
The Prince lift her on to his horse , and soon they reach the hut , where the old woman get down , and turn to the Prince say , ` Just wait a moment , and I will give you something . '
And she disappear into her hut , but return very soon and say , ` You be a mighty Prince , but at the same time you have a kind heart , which deserve to be reward .
Would you like to have the most beautiful woman in the world for your wife ? '
` Most certainly I would , ' reply the Prince .
So the old woman continue , ` The most beautiful woman in the whole world be the daughter of the Queen of the Flowers , who have be capture by a dragon .
If you wish to marry her , you must first set her free , and this I will help you to do .
I will give you this little bell : if you ring it once , the King of the Eagles will appear ; if you ring it twice , the King of the Foxes will come to you ; and if you ring it three time , you will see the King of the Fishes by your side .
These will help you if you be in any difficulty .
Now farewell , and heaven prosper your undertaking . '
She hand him the little bell , and there disappear hut and all , a though the earth have swallow her up .
Then it dawn on the Prince that he have be speak to a good fairy , and put the little bell carefully in his pocket , he ride home and tell his father that he mean to set the daughter of the Flower Queen free , and intend set out on the following day into the wide world in search of the maid .
So the next morning the Prince mount his fine horse and leave his home .
He have roam round the world for a whole year , and his horse have die of exhaustion , while he himself have suffer much from want and misery , but still he have come on no trace of her he be in search of .
At last one day he come to a hut , in front of which sit a very old man .
The Prince ask him , ` Do you not know where the Dragon life who keep the daughter of the Flower Queen prisoner ? '
` No , I do not , ' answer the old man .
` But if you go straight along this road for a year , you will reach a hut where my father life , and possibly he may be able to tell you . '
The Prince thank him for his information , and continue his journey for a whole year along the same road , and at the end of it come to the little hut , where he find a very old man .
He ask him the same question , and the old man answer , ` No , I do not know where the Dragon life .
But go straight along this road for another year , and you will come to a hut in which my father life .
I know he can tell you . '
And so the Prince wander on for another year , always on the same road , and at last reach the hut where he find the third old man .
He put the same question to him a he have put to his son and grandson ; but this time the old man answer , ` The Dragon live up there on the mountain , and he have just begin his year of sleep .
For one whole year he be always awake , and the next he sleep .
But if you wish to see the Flower Queen 's daughter go up the second mountain : the Dragon 's old mother live there , and she have a ball every night , to which the Flower Queen 's daughter go regularly . '
So the Prince go up the second mountain , where he find a castle all make of gold with diamond window .
He open the big gate lead into the courtyard , and be just go to walk in , when seven dragon rush on him and ask him what he want ?
The Prince reply , ' I have hear so much of the beauty and kindness of the Dragon 's Mother , and would like to enter her service . '
This flattering speech please the dragon , and the eldest of them say , ` Well , you may come with me , and I will take you to the Mother Dragon . '
They enter the castle and walk through twelve splendid hall , all make of gold and diamond .
In the twelfth room they find the Mother Dragon seat on a diamond throne .
She be the ugly woman under the sun , and , add to it all , she have three head .
Her appearance be a great shock to the Prince , and so be her voice , which be like the croaking of many raven .
She ask him , ` Why have you come here ? '
The Prince answer at once , ' I have hear so much of your beauty and kindness , that I would very much like to enter your service . '
` Very well , ' say the Mother Dragon ; ` but if you wish to enter my service , you must first lead my mare out to the meadow and look after her for three day ; but if you do n't bring her home safely every evening , we will eat you up . '
The Prince undertake the task and lead the mare out to the meadow .
But no sooner have they reach the grass than she vanish .
The Prince seek for her in vain , and at last in despair sit down on a big stone and contemplate his sad fate .
As he sit thus lose in thought , he notice an eagle fly over his head .
Then he suddenly bethink him of his little bell , and take it out of his pocket he ring it once .
In a moment he hear a rustle sound in the air beside him , and the King of the Eagles sank at his foot . '
I know what you want of me , ' the bird say .
` You be look for the Mother Dragon 's mare who be gallop about among the cloud .
I will summon all the eagle of the air together , and order them to catch the mare and bring her to you . '
And with these word the King of the Eagles fly away .
Towards even the Prince hear a mighty rush sound in the air , and when he look up he saw thousand of eagle drive the mare before them .
They sink at his foot on to the ground and give the mare over to him .
Then the Prince ride home to the old Mother Dragon , who be full of wonder when she saw him , and say , ` You have succeed to-day in look after my mare , and a a reward you shall come to my ball to-night . '
She give him at the same time a cloak make of copper , and lead him to a big room where several young he-dragons and she-dragons be dance together .
Here , too , be the Flower Queen 's beautiful daughter .
Her dress be weave out of the most lovely flower in the world , and her complexion be like lily and rose .
As the Prince be dance with her he manage to whisper in her ear , ' I have come to set you free ! '
Then the beautiful girl say to him , ` If you succeed in bring the mare back safely the third day , ask the Mother Dragon to give you a foal of the mare a a reward . '
The ball come to an end at midnight , and early next morning the Prince again lead the Mother Dragon 's mare out into the meadow .
But again she vanish before his eye .
Then he take out his little bell and ring it twice .
In a moment the King of the Foxes stand before him and say : ' I know already what you want , and will summon all the fox of the world together to find the mare who have hide herself in a hill . '
With these word the King of the Foxes disappear , and in the evening many thousand fox bring the mare to the Prince .
Then he ride home to the Mother-Dragon , from whom he receive this time a cloak make of silver , and again she lead him to the ball-room .
The Flower Queen 's daughter be delight to see him safe and sound , and when they be dance together she whisper in his ear : ` If you succeed again to-morrow , wait for me with the foal in the meadow .
After the ball we will fly away together . '
On the third day the Prince lead the mare to the meadow again ; but once more she vanish before his eye .
Then the Prince take out his little bell and ring it three time .
In a moment the King of the Fishes appear , and say to him : ' I know quite well what you want me to do , and I will summon all the fish of the sea together , and tell them to bring you back the mare , who be hide herself in a river . '
Towards even the mare be return to him , and when he lead her home to the Mother Dragon she say to him : ` You be a brave youth , and I will make you my body-servant .
But what shall I give you a a reward to begin with ? '
The Prince beg for a foal of the mare , which the Mother Dragon at once give him , and over and above , a cloak make of gold , for she have fall in love with him because he have praise her beauty .
So in the evening he appear at the ball in his golden cloak ; but before the entertainment be over he slip away , and go straight to the stable , where he mount his foal and ride out into the meadow to wait for the Flower Queen 's daughter .
Towards midnight the beautiful girl appear , and place her in front of him on his horse , the Prince and she fly like the wind till they reach the Flower Queen 's dwelling .
But the dragon have notice their flight , and wake their brother out of his year 's sleep .
He fly into a terrible rage when he hear what have happen , and determine to lay siege to the Flower Queen 's palace ; but the Queen cause a forest of flower as high a the sky to grow up round her dwelling , through which no one could force a way .
When the Flower Queen hear that her daughter want to marry the Prince , she say to him : ' I will give my consent to your marriage gladly , but my daughter can only stay with you in summer .
In winter , when everything be dead and the ground cover with snow , she must come and live with me in my palace underground . '
The Prince consent to this , and lead his beautiful bride home , where the wedding be hold with great pomp and magnificence .
The young couple live happily together till winter come , when the Flower Queen 's daughter depart and go home to her mother .
In summer she return to her husband , and their life of joy and happiness begin again , and last till the approach of winter , when the Flower Queen 's daughter go back again to her mother .
This come and go continued all her life long , and in spite of it they always live happily together .
THE FLYING SHIP -LRB- 24 -RRB- -LRB- 24 -RRB- From the Russian .
Once upon a time there live an old couple who have three son ; the two elder be clever , but the third be a regular dunce .
The clever son be very fond of their mother , give her good clothes , and always speak pleasantly to her ; but the young be always get in her way , and she have no patience with him .
Now , one day it be announce in the village that the King have issue a decree , offer his daughter , the Princess , in marriage to whoever should build a ship that could fly .
Immediately the two elder brother determine to try their luck , and ask their parent ' blessing .
So the old mother smartened up their clothes , and give them a store of provision for their journey , not forget to add a bottle of brandy .
When they have go the poor Simpleton begin to tease his mother to smarten him up and let him start off .
` What would become of a dolt like you ? '
she answer .
` Why , you would be eat up by wolf . '
But the foolish youth keep repeat , ' I will go , I will go , I will go ! '
Seeing that she could do nothing with him , the mother give him a crust of bread and a bottle of water , and take no further heed of him .
So the Simpleton set off on his way .
When he have go a short distance he meet a little old manikin .
They greet one another , and the manikin ask him where he be go . '
I be off to the King 's Court , ' he answer .
` He have promise to give his daughter to whoever can make a fly ship . '
` And can you make such a ship ? '
` Not I. ' ` Then why in the world be you go ? '
` Ca n't tell , ' reply the Simpleton .
` Well , if that be the case , ' say the manikin , ` sit down beside me ; we can rest for a little and have something to eat .
Give me what you have get in your satchel . '
Now , the poor Simpleton be ashamed to show what be in it .
However , he think it best not to make a fuss , so he open the satchel , and could scarcely believe his own eye , for , instead of the hard crust , he saw two beautiful fresh roll and some cold meat .
He share them with the manikin , who lick his lip and say : ` Now , go into that wood , and stop in front of the first tree , bow three time , and then strike the tree with your axe , fall on your knee on the ground , with your face on the earth , and remain there till you be raise up .
You will then find a ship at your side , step into it and fly to the King 's Palace .
If you meet anyone on the way , take him with you . '
The Simpleton thank the manikin very kindly , bid him farewell , and go into the road .
When he get to the first tree he stop in front of it , do everything just a he have be tell , and , kneel on the ground with his face to the earth , fell asleep .
After a little time he be arouse ; he awake and , rub his eye , saw a ready-made ship at his side , and at once get into it .

THE SNOW-DAUGHTER AND THE FIRE-SON -LRB- 25 -RRB- -LRB- 25 -RRB- From the Bukowinaer Tales and Legends .
Von Wliolocki .
There be once upon a time a man and his wife , and they have no child , which be a great grief to them .
One winter 's day , when the sun be shin brightly , the couple be stand outside their cottage , and the woman be look at all the little icicle which hang from the roof .
She sigh , and turn to her husband say , ' I wish I have a many child a there be icicle hang there . '
` Nothing would please me more either , ' reply her husband .
Then a tiny icicle detach itself from the roof , and drop into the woman 's mouth , who swallow it with a smile , and say , ` Perhaps I shall give birth to a snow child now ! '
Her husband laugh at his wife 's strange idea , and they go back into the house .
But after a short time the woman give birth to a little girl , who be as white a snow and as cold a ice .
If they bring the child anywhere near the fire , it scream loudly till they put it back into some cool place .
The little maid throve wonderfully , and in a few month she could run about and speak .
But she be not altogether easy to bring up , and give her parent much trouble and anxiety , for all summer she insist on spending in the cellar , and in the winter she would sleep outside in the snow , and the colder it be the happy she seem to be .
Her father and mother call her simply ` Our Snow-daughter , ' and this name stick to her all her life .
One day her parent sit by the fire , talk over the extraordinary behaviour of their daughter , who be disport herself in the snowstorm that rag outside .
The woman sigh deeply and say , ' I wish I have give birth to a Fire-son ! '
As she say these word , a spark from the big wood fire fly into the woman 's lap , and she say with a laugh , ` Now perhaps I shall give birth to a Fire-son ! '
The man laugh at his wife 's word , and think it be a good joke .
But he cease to think it a joke when his wife shortly afterwards give birth to a boy , who scream lustily till he be put quite close to the fire , and who nearly yell himself into a fit if the Snow-daughter come anywhere near him .
The Snow-daughter herself avoid him as much a she could , and always creep into a corner a far away from him a possible .
The parent call the boy simply ` Our Fire-son , ' a name which stick to him all his life .
They have a great deal of trouble and worry with him too ; but he thrive and grow very quickly , and before he be a year old he could run about and talk .
He be as red a fire , and a hot to touch , and he always sit on the hearth quite close to the fire , and complain of the cold ; if his sister be in the room he almost creep into the flame , while the girl on her part always complain of the great heat if her brother be anywhere near .
In summer the boy always lay out in the sun , while the girl hid herself in the cellar : so it happen that the brother and sister come very little into contact with each other -- in fact , they carefully avoid it .
Just a the girl grow up into a beautiful woman , her father and mother both die one after the other .
Then the Fire-son , who have grow up in the meantime into a fine , strong young man , say to his sister , ' I be go out into the world , for what be the use of remain on here ? ' '
I shall go with you , ' she answer , ` for , except you , I have no one in the world , and I have a feeling that if we set out together we shall be lucky . '
The Fire-son say , ' I love you with all my heart , but at the same time I always freeze if you be near me , and you nearly die of heat if I approach you !
How shall we travel about together without be odious the one to the other ? '
` Do n't worry about that , ' reply the girl , ` for I 've think it all over , and have settle on a plan which will make u each able to bear with the other !
See , I have have a fur cloak make for each of u , and if we put them on I shall not feel the heat so much nor you the cold . '
So they put on the fur cloak , and set out cheerfully on their way , and for the first time in their life quite happy in each other 's company .
For a long time the Fire-son and the Snow-daughter wander through the world , and when at the beginning of winter they come to a big wood they determine to stay there till spring .
The Fire-son build himself a hut where he always keep up a huge fire , while his sister with very few clothes on stayed outside night and day .
Now it happen one day that the King of the land hold a hunt in this wood , and saw the Snow-daughter wander about in the open air .
He wonder very much who the beautiful girl clad in such garment could be , and he stop and speak to her .
He soon learn that she could not stand heat , and that her brother could not endure cold .
The King be so charm by the Snow-daughter , that he ask her to be his wife .
The girl consent , and the wedding be hold with much state .
The King have a huge house of ice make for his wife underground , so that even in summer it do not melt .
But for his brother-in-law he have a house build with huge oven all round it , that be keep heat all day and night .
The Fire-son be delight , but the perpetual heat in which he live make his body so hot , that it be dangerous to go too close to him .
One day the King give a great feast , and ask his brother-in-law among the other guest .
The Fire-son do not appear till everyone have assemble , and when he do , everyone flee outside to the open air , so intense be the heat he give forth .
Then the King be very angry and say , ` If I have know what a lot of trouble you would have be , I would never have take you into my house . '
Then the Fire-son reply with a laugh , ` Do n't be angry , dear brother !
I love heat and my sister love cold -- come here and let me embrace you , and then I 'll go home at once . '
And before the King have time to reply , the Fire-son seize him in a tight embrace .
The King scream aloud in agony , and when his wife , the Snow-daughter , who have take refuge from her brother in the next room , hurry to him , the King lay dead on the ground burn to a cinder .
When the Snow-daughter saw this she turn on her brother and fly at him .
Then a fight begin , the like of which have never be see on earth .
When the people , attract by the noise , hurry to the spot , they saw the Snow-daughter melting into water and the Fire-son burn to a cinder .
And so end the unhappy brother and sister .
THE STORY OF KING FROST -LRB- 26 -RRB- -LRB- 26 -RRB- From the Russian .
There be once upon a time a peasant-woman who have a daughter and a step-daughter .
The daughter have her own way in everything , and whatever she do be right in her mother 's eye ; but the poor step-daughter have a hard time .
Let her do what she would , she be always blame , and get small thanks for all the trouble she take ; nothing be right , everything wrong ; and yet , if the truth be know , the girl be worth her weight in gold -- she be so unselfish and good-hearted .
But her step-mother do not like her , and the poor girl 's day be spend in weep ; for it be impossible to live peacefully with the woman .
The wicked shrew be determine to get rid of the girl by fair mean or foul , and keep say to her father : ` Send her away , old man ; send her away -- anywhere so that my eye sha 'n ' t be plague any longer by the sight of her , or my ear torment by the sound of her voice .
Send her out into the field , and let the cut frost do for her . '
In vain do the poor old father weep and implore her pity ; she be firm , and he dare not gainsay her .
So he place his daughter in a sledge , not even dare to give her a horse-cloth to keep herself warm with , and drive her out on to the bare , open field , where he kiss her and leave her , drive home as fast a he could , that he might not witness her miserable death .
Deserted by her father , the poor girl sit down under a fir-tree at the edge of the forest and begin to weep silently .
Suddenly she hear a faint sound : it be King Frost spring from tree to tree , and crack his finger a he go .
At length he reach the fir-tree beneath which she be sit , and with a crisp crackle sound he alight beside her , and look at her lovely face .
` Well , maiden , ' he snap out , ` do you know who I be ?
I be King Frost , king of the red-noses . '
` All hail to you , great King ! '
answer the girl , in a gentle , tremble voice .
` Have you come to take me ? '
` Are you warm , maiden ? '
he reply .
` Quite warm , King Frost , ' she answer , though she shiver a she speak .
Then King Frost stoop down , and bent over the girl , and the crackling sound grow loud , and the air seem to be full of knife and dart ; and again he ask : ` Maiden , be you warm ?
Are you warm , you beautiful girl ? '
And though her breath be almost frozen on her lip , she whisper gently , ` Quite warm , King Frost . '
Then King Frost gnash his teeth , and crack his finger , and his eye sparkle , and the crackling , crisp sound be louder than ever , and for the last time he ask her : ` Maiden , be you still warm ?
Are you still warm , little love ? '
And the poor girl be so stiff and numb that she could just gasp , ` Still warm , O King ! '
Now her gentle , courteous word and her uncomplaining way touch King Frost , and he have pity on her , and he wrap her up in fur , and cover her with blanket , and he fetch a great box , in which be beautiful jewel and a rich robe embroider in gold and silver .
And she put it on , and look more lovely than ever , and King Frost step with her into his sledge , with six white horse .
In the meantime the wicked step-mother be wait at home for news of the girl 's death , and prepare pancake for the funeral feast .
And she say to her husband : ` Old man , you have good go out into the field and find your daughter 's body and bury her . '
Just a the old man be leave the house the little dog under the table begin to bark , say : ` YOUR daughter shall live to be your delight ; HER daughter shall die this very night . '
` Hold your tongue , you foolish beast ! '
scold the woman .
` There 's a pancake for you , but you must say : `` HER daughter shall have much silver and gold ; HIS daughter be frozen quite stiff and cold . '' '
But the doggie eat up the pancake and bark , say : ` His daughter shall wear a crown on her head ; Her daughter shall die unwooed , unwed . '
Then the old woman try to coax the doggie with more pancake and to terrify it with blow , but he bark on , always repeat the same word .
And suddenly the door creak and fly open , and a great heavy chest be push in , and behind it come the step-daughter , radiant and beautiful , in a dress all glitter with silver and gold .
For a moment the step-mother 's eye be dazzle .
Then she call to her husband : ` Old man , yoke the horse at once into the sledge , and take my daughter to the same field and leave her on the same spot exactly ; ` and so the old man take the girl and leave her beneath the same tree where he have part from his daughter .
In a few minute King Frost come past , and , look at the girl , he say : ` Are you warm , maiden ? '
` What a blind old fool you must be to ask such a question ! '
she answer angrily .
` Ca n't you see that my hand and foot be nearly frozen ? '
Then King Frost sprang to and fro in front of her , question her , and get only rude , rough word in reply , till at last he get very angry , and crack his finger , and gnash his teeth , and freeze her to death .
But in the hut her mother be wait for her return , and a she grow impatient she say to her husband : ` Get out the horse , old man , to go and fetch her home ; but see that you be careful not to upset the sledge and lose the chest . '
But the doggie beneath the table begin to bark , say : ` Your daughter be frozen quite stiff and cold , And shall never have a chest full of gold . '
` Do n't tell such wicked lie ! '
scold the woman .
` There 's a cake for you ; now say : `` HER daughter shall marry a mighty King . ''
At that moment the door fly open , and she rush out to meet her daughter , and a she take her frozen body in her arm she too be chill to death .
THE DEATH OF THE SUN-HERO -LRB- 27 -RRB- -LRB- 27 -RRB- From the Bukowinaer Tales and Legends .
Von Wliolocki .
Many , many thousand year ago there live a mighty King whom heaven have bless with a clever and beautiful son .
When he be only ten year old the boy be clever than all the King 's counsellor put together , and when he be twenty he be the great hero in the whole kingdom .
His father could not make enough of his son , and always have him clothe in golden garment which shone and sparkle like the sun ; and his mother give him a white horse , which never sleep , and which fly like the wind .
All the people in the land love him dearly , and call him the Sun-Hero , for they do not think his like exist under the sun .
Now it happen one night that both his parent have the same extraordinary dream .
They dream that a girl all dress in red have come to them and say : ` If you wish that your son should really become the Sun-Hero in deed and not only in name , let him go out into the world and search for the Tree of the Sun , and when he have find it , let him pluck a golden apple from it and bring it home . '
When the King and Queen have each relate their dream to the other , they be much amaze that they should both have dream exactly the same about their son , and the King say to his wife , ` This be clearly a sign from heaven that we should send our son out into the world in order that he may come home the great Sun-Hero , a the Red Girl say , not only in name but in deed . '
The Queen consent with many tear , and the King at once bid his son set forth in search of the Tree of the Sun , from which he be to pluck a golden apple .
The Prince be delight at the prospect , and set out on his travel that very day .
For a long time he wander all through the world , and it be not till the ninety-ninth day after he start that he find an old man who be able to tell him where the Tree of the Sun grow .
He follow his direction , and rode on his way , and after another ninety-nine day he arrive at a golden castle , which stand in the middle of a vast wilderness .
He knock at the door , which be open noiselessly and by invisible hand .
Finding no one about , the Prince rode on , and come to a great meadow , where the Sun-Tree grow .
When he reach the tree he put out his hand to pick a golden apple ; but all of a sudden the tree grow high , so that he could not reach it fruit .
Then he hear some one behind him laugh .
Turning round , he saw the girl in red walking towards him , who address him in these word : ` Do you really imagine , brave son of the earth , that you can pluck an apple so easily from the Tree of the Sun ?
Before you can do that , you have a difficult task before you .
You must guard the tree for nine day and nine night from the ravage of two wild black wolf , who will try to harm it .
Do you think you can undertake this ? '
` Yes , ' answer the Sun-Hero , ' I will guard the Tree of the Sun nine day and nine night . '
Then the girl continue : ` Remember , though , if you do not succeed the Sun will kill you .
Now begin your watch . '
With these word the Red Girl go back into the golden castle .
She have hardly leave him when the two black wolf appear : but the Sun-Hero beat them off with his sword , and they retire , only , however , to reappear in a very short time .
The Sun-Hero chase them away once more , but he have hardly sit down to rest when the two black wolf be on the scene again .
This go on for seven day and night , when the white horse , who have never do such a thing before , turn to the Sun-Hero and say in a human voice : ` Listen to what I be go to say .
A Fairy give me to your mother in order that I might be of service to you ; so let me tell you , that if you go to sleep and let the wolf harm the tree , the Sun will surely kill you .
The Fairy , foresee this , put everyone in the world under a spell , which prevent their obey the Sun 's command to take your life .
But all the same , she have forget one person , who will certainly kill you if you fall asleep and let the wolf damage the tree .
So watch and keep the wolf away . '
Then the Sun-Hero strove with all his might and keep the black wolf at bay , and conquer his desire to sleep ; but on the eighth night his strength fail him , and he fell fast asleep .
When he awake a woman in black stood beside him , who say : ` You have fulfil your task very badly , for you have let the two black wolf damage the Tree of the Sun .
I be the mother of the Sun , and I command you to ride away from here at once , and I pronounce sentence of death upon you , for you proudly let yourself be call the Sun-Hero without have do anything to deserve the name . '
The youth mount his horse sadly , and ride home .
The people all throng round him on his return , anxious to hear his adventure , but he tell them nothing , and only to his mother do he confide what have befall him .
But the old Queen laugh , and say to her son : ` Do n't worry , my child ; you see , the Fairy have protect you so far , and the Sun have find no one to kill you .
So cheer up and be happy . '
After a time the Prince forget all about his adventure , and marry a beautiful Princess , with whom he live very happily for some time .
But one day when he be out hunt he felt very thirsty , and come to a stream he stoop down to drink from it , and this cause his death , for a crab come swim up , and with it claw tear out his tongue .
He be carry home in a die condition , and a he lay on his death-bed the black woman appear and say : ` So the Sun have , after all , find someone , who be not under the Fairy 's spell , who have cause your death .
And a similar fate will overtake everyone under the Sun who wrongfully assume a title to which he have no right . '
THE WITCH -LRB- 28 -RRB- -LRB- 28 -RRB- From the Russian .
Once upon a time there be a peasant whose wife die , leave him with two child -- twin -- a boy and a girl .
For some year the poor man live on alone with the child , care for them as best he could ; but everything in the house seem to go wrong without a woman to look after it , and at last he make up his mind to marry again , feel that a wife would bring peace and order to his household and take care of his motherless child .
So he marry , and in the following year several child be bear to him ; but peace and order do not come to the household .
For the step-mother be very cruel to the twin , and beat them , and half-starved them , and constantly drive them out of the house ; for her one idea be to get them out of the way .
All day she think of nothing but how she should get rid of them ; and at last an evil idea come into her head , and she determine to send them out into the great gloomy wood where a wicked witch live .
And so one morning she speak to them , say : ` You have be such good child that I be go to send you to visit my granny , who live in a dear little hut in the wood .
