You will have to wait upon her and serve her , but you will be well reward , for she will give you the best of everything . '
So the child leave the house together ; and the little sister , who be very wise for her year , say to the brother : ` We will first go and see our own dear grandmother , and tell her where our step-mother be send u . '
And when the grandmother heard where they be go , she cry and say : ` You poor motherless child !
How I pity you ; and yet I can do nothing to help you !
Your step-mother be not send you to her granny , but to a wicked witch who live in that great gloomy wood .
Now listen to me , child .
You must be civil and kind to everyone , and never say a cross word to anyone , and never touch a crumb belong to anyone else .
Who know if , after all , help may not be send to you ? '
And she give her grandchild a bottle of milk and a piece of ham and a loaf of bread , and they set out for the great gloomy wood .
When they reach it they saw in front of them , in the thickest of the tree , a queer little hut , and when they look into it , there lay the witch , with her head on the threshold of the door , with one foot in one corner and the other in the other corner , and her knee cock up , almost touch the ceiling .
` Who 's there ? '
she snarl , in an awful voice , when she saw the child .
And they answer civilly , though they be so terrify that they hide behind one another , and say : ` Good-morning , granny ; our step-mother have send u to wait upon you , and serve you . '
` See that you do it well , then , ' growl the witch .
` If I be pleased with you , I 'll reward you ; but if I be not , I 'll put you in a pan and fry you in the oven -- that 's what I 'll do with you , my pretty dear !
You have be gently rear , but you 'll find my work hard enough .
See if you do n't . '
And , so say , she set the girl down to spin yarn , and she give the boy a sieve in which to carry water from the well , and she herself go out into the wood .
Now , a the girl be sit at her distaff , weep bitterly because she could not spin , she hear the sound of hundred of little foot , and from every hole and corner in the hut mouse come patter along the floor , squeak and say : ` Little girl , why be your eye so red ?
If you want help , then give u some bread . '
And the girl give them the bread that her grandmother have give her .
Then the mouse tell her that the witch have a cat , and the cat be very fond of ham ; if she would give the cat her ham , it would show her the way out of the wood , and in the meantime they would spin the yarn for her .
So the girl set out to look for the cat , and , a she be hunt about , she meet her brother , in great trouble because he could not carry water from the well in a sieve , a it come pour out as fast a he put it in .
And a she be try to comfort him they hear a rustling of wing , and a flight of wren alight on the ground beside them .
And the wren say : ` Give u some crumb , then you need not grieve .
For you 'll find that water will stay in the sieve . '
Then the twin crumble their bread on the ground , and the wren peck it , and chirrup and chirp .
And when they have eat the last crumb they tell the boy to fill up the hole of the sieve with clay , and then to draw water from the well .
So he do what they say , and carry the sieve full of water into the hut without spill a drop .
When they enter the hut the cat be curl up on the floor .
So they stroke her , and feed her with ham , and say to her : ` Pussy , grey pussy , tell u how we be to get away from the witch ? '
Then the cat thank them for the ham , and give them a pocket-handkerchief and a comb , and tell them that when the witch pursue them , a she certainly would , all they have to do be to throw the handkerchief on the ground and run as fast a they could .
As soon a the handkerchief touch the ground a deep , broad river would spring up , which would hinder the witch 's progress .
If she manage to get across it , they must throw the comb behind them and run for their life , for where the comb fell a dense forest would start up , which would delay the witch so long that they would be able to get safely away .
The cat have scarcely finish speaking when the witch return to see if the child have fulfil their task .
` Well , you have do well enough for to-day , ' she grumble ; ` but to-morrow you 'll have something more difficult to do , and if you do n't do it well , you pamper brat , straight into the oven you go . '
Half-dead with fright , and tremble in every limb , the poor child lay down to sleep on a heap of straw in the corner of the hut ; but they dare not close their eye , and scarcely venture to breathe .
In the morning the witch give the girl two piece of linen to weave before night , and the boy a pile of wood to cut into chip .
Then the witch leave them to their task , and go out into the wood .
As soon a she have go out of sight the child take the comb and the handkerchief , and , take one another by the hand , they start and run , and run , and run .
And first they meet the watch-dog , who be go to leap on them and tear them to piece ; but they throw the remains of their bread to him , and he eat them and wag his tail .
Then they be hinder by the birch-trees , whose branch almost put their eye out .
But the little sister tie the twig together with a piece of ribbon , and they get past safely , and , after run through the wood , come out on to the open field .
In the meantime in the hut the cat be busy weave the linen and tangle the thread a it weave .
And the witch return to see how the child be get on ; and she creep up to the window , and whisper : ` Are you weave , my little dear ? '
` Yes , granny , I be weave , ' answer the cat .
When the witch saw that the child have escape her , she be furious , and , hit the cat with a porringer , she say : ` Why do you let the child leave the hut ?
Why do you not scratch their eye out ? '
But the cat curl up it tail and put it back up , and answer : ' I have serve you all these year and you never even throw me a bone , but the dear child give me their own piece of ham . '
Then the witch be furious with the watch-dog and with the birch-trees , because they have let the child pas .
But the dog answer : ' I have serve you all these year and you never give me so much a a hard crust , but the dear child give me their own loaf of bread . '
And the birch rustle it leaf , and say : ' I have serve you long than I can say , and you never tie a bit of twine even round my branch ; and the dear child bind them up with their bright ribbon . '
So the witch saw there be no help to be get from her old servant , and that the best thing she could do be to mount on her broom and set off in pursuit of the child .
And a the child run they hear the sound of the broom sweep the ground close behind them , so instantly they throw the handkerchief down over their shoulder , and in a moment a deep , broad river flow behind them .
When the witch come up to it , it take her a long time before she find a place which she could ford over on her broom-stick ; but at last she get across , and continue the chase faster than before .
And a the child run they hear a sound , and the little sister put her ear to the ground , and hear the broom sweep the earth close behind them ; so , quick a thought , she throw the comb down on the ground , and in an instant , a the cat have say , a dense forest sprung up , in which the root and branch be so closely intertwined , that it be impossible to force a way through it .
So when the witch come up to it on her broom she find that there be nothing for it but to turn round and go back to her hut .
But the twin run straight on till they reach their own home .
Then they tell their father all that they have suffer , and he be so angry with their step-mother that he drive her out of the house , and never let her return ; but he and the child live happily together ; and he take care of them himself , and never let a stranger come near them .
THE HAZEL-NUT CHILD -LRB- 29 -RRB- -LRB- 29 -RRB- From the Bukowniaer .
Van Wliolocki .
There be once upon a time a couple who have no child , and they pray Heaven every day to send them a child , though it be no big than a hazel-nut .
At last Heaven hear their prayer and send them a child exactly the size of a hazel-nut , and it never grow an inch .
The parent be very devote to the little creature , and nursed and tend it carefully .
Their tiny son too be as clever a he could be , and so sharp and sensible that all the neighbour marvel over the wise thing he say and do .
When the Hazel-nut child be fifteen year old , and be sit one day in an egg-shell on the table beside his mother , she turn to him and say , ` You be now fifteen year old , and nothing can be do with you .
What do you intend to be ? ' '
A messenger , ' answer the Hazel-nut child .
Then his mother burst out laughing and say , ` What an idea !
You a messenger !
Why , your little foot would take an hour to go the distance an ordinary person could do in a minute ! '
But the Hazel-nut child reply , ` Nevertheless I mean to be a messenger !
Just send me a message and you 'll see that I shall be back in next to no time . '
So his mother say , ` Very well , go to your aunt in the neighbouring village , and fetch me a comb . '
The Hazel-nut child jump quickly out of the egg-shell and run out into the street .
Here he find a man on horseback who be just set out for the neighbouring village .
He creep up the horse 's leg , sit down under the saddle , and then begin to pinch the horse and to prick it with a pin .
The horse plunge and rear and then set off at a hard gallop , which it continue in spite of it rider 's effort to stop it .
When they reach the village , the Hazel-nut child leave off prick the horse , and the poor tired creature pursue it way at a snail 's pace .
The Hazel-nut child take advantage of this , and creep down the horse 's leg ; then he run to his aunt and ask her for a comb .
On the way home he meet another rider , and do the return journey in exactly the same way .
When he hand his mother the comb that his aunt have give him , she be much amaze and ask him , ` But how do you manage to get back so quickly ? '
` Ah !
mother , ' he reply , ` you see I be quite right when I say I know a messenger be the profession for me . '
His father too possess a horse which he often use to take out into the field to graze .
One day he take the Hazel-nut child with him .
At midday the father turn to his small son and say , ` Stay here and look after the horse .
I must go home and give your mother a message , but I shall be back soon . '
When his father have go , a robber pass by and saw the horse graze without any one watching it , for of course he could not see the Hazel-nut child hidden in the grass .
So he mount the horse and ride away .
But the Hazel-nut child , who be the most active little creature , climb up the horse 's tail and begin to bite it on the back , enrage the creature to such an extent that it pay no attention to the direction the robber try to make it go in , but gallop straight home .
The father be much astonish when he saw a stranger rid his horse , but the Hazel-nut child climb down quickly and tell him all that have happen , and his father have the robber arrest at once and put into prison .
One autumn when the Hazel-nut child be twenty year old he say to his parent : ` Farewell , my dear father and mother .
I be go to set out into the world , and as soon a I have become rich I will return home to you . '
The parent laugh at the little man 's word , but do not believe him for a moment .
In the even the Hazel-nut child crept on to the roof , where some stork have build their nest .
The stork be fast asleep , and he climb on to the back of the father-stork and bind a silk cord round the joint of one of it wing , then he creep among it soft downy feather and fell asleep .
The next morning the stork fly towards the south , for winter be approach .
The Hazel-nut child fly through the air on the stork 's back , and when he want to rest he bind his silk cord on to the joint of the bird 's other wing , so that it could not fly any farther .
In this way he reach the country of the black people , where the stork take up their abode close to the capital .
When the people saw the Hazel-nut child they be much astonish , and take him with the stork to the King of the country .
The King be delight with the little creature and keep him always beside him , and he soon grow so fond of the little man that he give him a diamond four time as big a himself .
The Hazel-nut child fasten the diamond firmly under the stork 's neck with a ribbon , and when he saw that the other stork be get ready for their northern flight , he untie the silk cord from his stork 's wing , and away they go , get near home every minute .
At length the Hazel-nut child come to his native village ; then he undo the ribbon from the stork 's neck and the diamond fell to the ground ; he cover it first with sand and stone , and then run to get his parent , so that they might carry the treasure home , for he himself be not able to lift the great diamond .
So the Hazel-nut child and his parent live in happiness and prosperity after this till they die .
THE STORY OF BIG KLAUS AND LITTLE KLAUS In a certain village there live two people who have both the same name .
Both be call Klaus , but one own four horse and the other only one .
In order to distinguish the one from the other , the one who have four horse be call Big Klaus , and the one who have only one horse , Little Klaus .
Now you shall hear what befall them both , for this be a true story .
The whole week through Little Klaus have to plough for Big Klaus , and lend him his one horse ; then Big Klaus lend him his four horse , but only once a week , and that be on Sunday .
Hurrah !
how loudly Little Klaus crack his whip over all the five horse !
for they be indeed as good a his on this one day .
The sun shone brightly , and all the bell in the church-towers be peal ; the people be dress in their best clothes , and be go to church , with their hymn book under their arm , to hear the minister preach .
They saw Little Klaus plough with the five horse ; but he be so happy that he keep on crack his whip , and call out ` Gee-up , my five horse ! '
` You must n't say that , ' say Big Klaus .
` Only one horse be yours . '
But as soon a someone else be go by Little Klaus forget that he must not say it , and call out ` Gee-up , my five horse ! '
` Now you have good stop that , ' say Big Klaus , ` for if you say it once more I will give your horse such a crack on the head that it will drop down dead on the spot ! ' '
I really wo n't say it again ! '
say Little Klaus .
But as soon a more people pass by , and nod him good-morning , he become so happy in think how well it look to have five horse plough his field that , crack his whip , he call out ` Gee-up , my five horse ! '
` I 'll see to your horse ! '
say Big Klaus ; and , seize an iron bar , he strike Little Klaus ' one horse such a blow on the head that it fell down and die on the spot .
` Alas !
Now I have no horse ! '
say Little Klaus , begin to cry .
Then he flay the skin off his horse , dry it , and put it in a sack , which he throw over his shoulder , and go into the town to sell it .
He have a long way to go , and have to pass through a great dark forest .
A dreadful storm come on , in which he lose his way , and before he could get on to the right road night come on , and it be impossible to reach the town that even .
Right in front of him be a large farm-house .
The window-shutters be close , but the light come through the chink . '
I should very much like to be allow to spend the night there , ' think Little Klaus ; and he go and knock at the door .
The farmer 's wife open it , but when she hear what he want she tell him to go away ; her husband be not at home , and she take in no stranger .
` Well , I must lie down outside , ' say Little Klaus ; and the farmer 's wife shut the door in his face .
Close by stand a large haystack , and between it and the house a little out-house , cover with a flat thatch roof . '
I can lie down there , ' think Little Klaus , look at the roof ; ` it will make a splendid bed , if only the stork wo n't fly down and bite my leg . '
For a live stork be stand on the roof , where it have it nest .
So Little Klaus creep up into the out-house , where he lay down , and make himself comfortable for the night .
The wooden shutter over the window be not shut at the top , and he could just see into the room .
There stand a large table , spread with wine and roast meat and a beautiful fish .
The farmer 's wife and the sexton sit at the table , but there be no one else .
She be fill up his glass , while he stick his fork into the fish which be his favourite dish .
` If one could only get some of that ! '
think Little Klaus , stretch his head towards the window .
Ah , what delicious cake he saw stand there !
It WAS a feast !
Then he hear someone rid along the road towards the house .
It be the farmer come home .
He be a very worthy man ; but he have one great peculiarity -- namely , that he could not bear to see a sexton .
If he saw one he be make quite mad .
That be why the sexton have go to say good-day to the farmer 's wife when he know that her husband be not at home , and the good woman therefore put in front of him the best food she have .
But when they hear the farmer come they be frighten , and the farmer 's wife beg the sexton to creep into a great empty chest .
He do so , a he know the poor man could not bear to see a sexton .
The wife hastily hide all the beautiful food and the wine in her oven ; for if her husband have see it , he would have be sure to ask what it all meant .
` Oh , dear !
oh , dear ! '
groan Little Klaus up in the shed , when he saw the good food disappearing .
` Is anybody up there ? '
ask the farmer , catch sight of Little Klaus .
` Why be you lie there ?
Come with me into the house . '
Then Little Klaus tell him how he have lose his way , and beg to be allow to spend the night there .
` Yes , certainly , ' say the farmer ; ` but we must first have something to eat ! '
The wife receive them both very kindly , spread a long table , and give them a large plate of porridge .
The farmer be hungry , and ate with a good appetite ; but Little Klaus could not help thinking of the delicious dish of fish and roast meat and cake which he know be in the oven .
Under the table at his foot he have lay the sack with the horse-skin in it , for , a we know , he be go to the town to sell it .
The porridge do not taste good to him , so he tread upon his sack , and the dry skin in the sack squeak loudly .
` Hush ! '
say Little Klaus to his sack , at the same time tread on it again so that it squeak even loud than before .
` Hallo !
what have you get in your sack ? '
ask the farmer .
` Oh , it be a wizard ! '
say Little Klaus .
` He say we should not eat porridge , for he have conjure the whole oven full of roast meat and fish and cake . '
` Goodness me ! '
say the farmer ; and open the oven he saw all the delicious , tempt dish his wife have hide there , but which he now believe the wizard in the sack have conjure up for them .
The wife could say nothing , but she put the food at once on the table , and they eat the fish , the roast meat , and the cake .
Little Klaus now tread again on his sack , so that the skin squeak .
` What do he say now ? '
ask the farmer .
` He say , ' reply Little Klans , ` that he have also conjure up for u three bottle of wine ; they be stand in the corner by the oven ! '
The wife have to fetch the wine which she have hide , and the farmer drank and grow very merry .
He would very much like to have have such a wizard a Little Klaus have in the sack .
` Can he conjure up the Devil ? '
ask the farmer . '
I should like to see him very much , for I feel just now in very good spirit ! '
` Yes , ' say Little Klaus ; ` my wizard can do everything that I ask .
Is n't that true ? '
he ask , tread on the sack so that it squeak .
` Do you hear ?
He say '' Yes ; '' but that the Devil look so ugly that we should not like to see him . '
` Oh !
I 'm not at all afraid .
What do he look like ? '
` He will show himself in the shape of a sexton ! ' '
I say ! '
say the farmer , ` he must be ugly !
You must know that I ca n't bear to look at a sexton !
But it do n't matter .
I know that it be the Devil , and I sha 'n ' t mind !
I feel up to it now .
But he must not come too near me ! ' '
I must ask my wizard , ' say Little Klaus , tread on the sack and put his ear to it .
` What do he say ? '
` He say you can open the chest in the corner there , and you will see the Devil squatting inside it ; but you must hold the lid so that he shall not escape . '
` Will you help me to hold him ? '
beg the farmer , go towards the chest where his wife have hide the real sexton , who be sit inside in a terrible fright .
The farmer open the lid a little way , and saw him inside .
` Ugh ! '
he shriek , spring back .
` Yes , now I have see him ; he look just like our sexton .
Oh , it be horrid ! '
So he have to drink again , and they drink till far on into the night .
` You MUST sell me the wizard , ' say the farmer .
` Ask anything you like !
I will pay you down a bushelful of money on the spot . '
` No , I really ca n't , ' say Little Klans .
` Just think how many thing I can get from this wizard ! '
` Ah !
I should like to have him so much ! '
say the farmer , beg very hard .
` Well ! '
say Little Klaus at last , ` a you have be so good a to give me shelter to-night , I will sell him .
You shall have the wizard for a bushel of money , but I must have full measure . '
` That you shall , ' say the farmer .
` But you must take the chest with you .
I wo n't keep it another hour in the house .
Who know that he be n't in there still ? '
Little Klaus give the farmer his sack with the dry skin , and get instead a good bushelful of money .
The farmer also give him a wheelbarrow to carry away his money and the chest .
` Farewell , ' say Little Klaus ; and away he go with his money and the big chest , wherein sit the sexton .
On the other side of the wood be a large deep river .
The water flow so rapidly that you could scarcely swim against the stream .
A great new bridge have be build over it , on the middle of which Little Klaus stop , and say aloud so that the sexton might hear : ` Now , what be I to do with this stupid chest ?
It be as heavy a if it be fill with stone !
I shall only be tire , drag it along ; I will throw it into the river .
If it swim home to me , well and good ; and if it do n't , it 's no matter . '
Then he take the chest with one hand and lift it up a little , a if he be go to throw it into the water .
` No , do n't do that ! '
call out the sexton in the chest .
` Let me get out first ! '
` Oh , oh ! '
say Little Klaus , pretend that he be afraid .
` He be still in there !
I must throw him quickly into the water to drown him ! '
` Oh !
no , no ! '
cry the sexton . '
I will give you a whole bushelful of money if you will let me go ! '
` Ah , that 's quite another thing ! '
say Little Klaus , open the chest .
The sexton creep out very quickly , push the empty chest into the water and go to his house , where he give Little Klaus a bushel of money .
One he have have already from the farmer , and now he have his wheelbarrow full of money .
` Well , I have get a good price for the horse ! '
say he to himself when he shake all his money out in a heap in his room .
` This will put Big Klaus in a rage when he hear how rich I have become through my one horse ; but I wo n't tell him just yet ! '
So he send a boy to Big Klaus to borrow a bushel measure from him .
` Now what can he want with it ? '
think Big Klaus ; and he smear some tar at the bottom , so that of whatever be measure a little should remain in it .
And this be just what happen ; for when he get his measure back , three new silver five-shilling piece be stick to it .
What do this mean ? '
say Big Klaus , and he run off at once to Little Klaus .
` Where do you get so much money from ? '
` Oh , that be from my horse-skin .
I sell it yesterday even . '
` That 's certainly a good price ! '
say Big Klaus ; and run home in great haste , he take an axe , knock all his four horse on the head , skin them , and go into the town .
` Skins !
skin !
Who will buy skin ? '
he cry through the street .
All the shoemaker and tanner come run to ask him what he want for them . '
A bushel of money for each , ' say Big Klaus .
` Are you mad ? '
they all exclaim .
` Do you think we have money by the bushel ? '
` Skins !
skin !
Who will buy skin ? '
he cry again , and to all who ask him what they cost , he answer , ' A bushel of money . '
` He be make game of u , ' they say ; and the shoemaker seize their yard measure and the tanner their leathern apron and they give Big Klaus a good beating .
` Skins !
skin ! '
they cry mockingly ; yes , we will tan YOUR skin for you !
Out of the town with him ! '
they shout ; and Big Klaus have to hurry off as quickly a he could , if he want to save his life .
` Aha ! '
say he when he come home , ` Little Klaus shall pay dearly for this .
I will kill him ! '
Little Klaus ' grandmother have just die .
Though she have be very unkind to him , he be very much distress , and he take the dead woman and lay her in his warm bed to try if he could not bring her back to life .
There she lay the whole night , while he sit in the corner and sleep on a chair , which he have often do before .
And in the night a he sit there the door open , and Big Klaus come in with his axe .
He know quite well where Little Klaus 's bed stand , and go up to it he strike the grandmother on the head just where he think Little Klaus would be .
` There ! '
say he .
` Now you wo n't get the best of me again ! '
And he go home .
` What a very wicked man ! '
think Little Klaus .
` He be go to kill me !
It be a good thing for my grandmother that she be dead already , or else he would have kill her ! '
Then he dress his grandmother in her Sunday clothes , borrow a horse from his neighbour , harness the cart to it , sit his grandmother on the back seat so that she could not fall out when he drive , and away they go .
When the sun rise they be in front of a large inn .
Little Klaus get down , and go in to get something to drink .
The host be very rich .
He be a very worthy but hot-tempered man .
` Good morning ! '
say he to Little Klaus .
` You be early on the road . '
` Yes , ' say Little Klaus . '
I be go to the town with my grandmother .
She be sit outside in the cart ; I can not bring her in .
Will you not give her a glass of mead ?
But you will have to speak loud , for she be very hard of hear . '
` Oh yes , certainly I will ! '
say the host ; and , pour out a large glass of mead , he take it out to the dead grandmother , who be sit upright in the cart .
` Here be a glass of mead from your son , ' say the host .
But the dead woman do not answer a word , and sit still .
` Do n't you hear ? '
cry the host as loud a he could .
` Here be a glass of mead from your son ! '
Then he shout the same thing again , and yet again , but she never move in her place ; and at last he grow angry , throw the glass in her face , so that she fell back into the cart , for she be not tie in her place .
` Hullo ! '
cry Little Klaus , run out of the door , and seize the host by the throat .
` You have kill my grandmother !
Look !
there be a great hole in her forehead ! '
` Oh , what a misfortune ! '
cry the host , wring his hand .
` It all come from my hot temper !
Dear Little Klaus !
I will give you a bushel of money , and will bury your grandmother a if she be my own ; only do n't tell about it , or I shall have my head cut off , and that would be very uncomfortable . '
So Little Klaus get a bushel of money , and the host bury his grandmother a if she have be his own .
Now when Little Klaus again reach home with so much money he send his boy to Big Klaus to borrow his bushel measure .
` What 's this ? '
say Big Klaus .
` Did n't I kill him ?
I must see to this myself ! '
So he go himself to Little Klaus with the measure .
` Well , now , where do you get all this money ? '
ask he , open his eye at the heap .
` You kill my grandmother -- not me , ' say Little Klaus . '
I sell her , and get a bushel of money for her . '
` That be indeed a good price ! '
say Big Klaus ; and , hurry home , he take an axe and kill his grandmother , lay her in the cart , and drive off to the apothecary 's , and ask whether he want to buy a dead body .
` Who be it , and how do you get it ? '
ask the apothecary .
` It be my grandmother , ' say Big Klaus . '
I kill her in order to get a bushel of money . '
` You be mad ! '
say the apothecary .
` Do n't mention such thing , or you will lose your head ! '
And he begin to tell him what a dreadful thing he have do , and what a wicked man he be , and that he ought to be punish ; till Big Klaus be so frightened that he jump into the cart and drive home as hard a he could .
The apothecary and all the people think he must be mad , so they let him go .
` You shall pay for this ! '
say Big Klaus a he drive home .
` You shall pay for this dearly , Little Klaus ! '
So as soon a he get home he take the large sack he could find , and go to Little Klaus and say : ` You have fool me again !
First I kill my horse , then my grandmother !
It be all your fault ; but you sha 'n ' t do it again ! '
And he seize Little Klaus , push him in the sack , throw it over his shoulder , cry out ` Now I be go to drown you ! '
He have to go a long way before he come to the river , and Little Klaus be not very light .
The road pass by the church ; the organ be sound , and the people be sing most beautifully .
Big Klaus put down the sack with Little Klaus in it by the church-door , and think that he might as well go in and hear a psalm before go on farther .
Little Klaus could not get out , and everybody be in church ; so he go in .
` Oh , dear !
oh , dear ! '
groan Little Klaus in the sack , twist and turn himself .
But he could not undo the string .
There come by an old , old shepherd , with snow-white hair and a long staff in his hand .
He be drive a herd of cow and ox .
These push against the sack so that it be overturn .
` Alas ! '
moan Little Klans , ' I be so young and yet I must die ! '
` And I , poor man , ' say the cattle-driver , ' I be so old and yet I can not die ! '
` Open the sack , ' call out Little Klaus ; ` creep in here instead of me , and you will die in a moment ! ' '
I will gladly do that , ' say the cattle-driver ; and he open the sack , and Little Klaus struggle out at once .
` You will take care of the cattle , wo n't you ? '
ask the old man , creep into the sack , which Little Klaus fasten up and then go on with the cow and ox .
Soon after Big Klaus come out of the church , and take up the sack on his shoulder it seem to him a if it have become lighter ; for the old cattle-driver be not half as heavy a Little Klaus .
` How easy he be to carry now !
That must be because I hear part of the service . '
So he go to the river , which be deep and broad , throw in the sack with the old driver , and call after it , for he think Little Klaus be inside : ` Down you go !
You wo n't mock me any more now ! '
Then he go home ; but when he come to the cross-roads , there he meet Little Klaus , who be drive his cattle .
` What 's this ? '
say Big Klaus .
` Have n't I drown you ? '
` Yes , ' reply Little Klaus ; ` you throw me into the river a good half-hour ago ! '
` But how do you get those splendid cattle ? '
ask Big Klaus .
` They be sea-cattle ! '
say Little Klaus . '
I will tell you the whole story , and I thank you for have drown me , because now I be on dry land and really rich !
How frighten I be when I be in the sack !
How the wind whistle in my ear a you throw me from the bridge into the cold water !
I sink at once to the bottom ; but I do not hurt myself for underneath be grow the most beautiful soft grass .
I fell on this , and immediately the sack open ; the lovely maiden in snow-white garment , with a green garland round her wet hair , take me by the hand , and say ! ''
Are you Little Klaus ?
Here be some cattle for you to begin with , and a mile far down the road there be another herd , which I will give you a a present ! ''
Now I saw that the river be a great high-road for the sea-people .
Along it they travel underneath from the sea to the land till the river end .
It be so beautiful , full of flower and fresh grass ; the fish which be swim in the water shot past my ear a the bird do here in the air .
What lovely people there be , and what fine cattle be graze in the ditch and dyke ! '
` But why do you come up to u again ? '
ask Big Klaus . '
I should not have do so , if it be so beautiful down below ! '
` Oh ! '
say Little Klaus , ` that be just so politic of me .
You hear what I tell you , that the sea-maiden say to me a mile far along the road -- and by the road she mean the river , for she can go by no other way -- there be another herd of cattle wait for me .
But I know what wind the river make , now here , now there , so that it be a long way round .
Therefore it make it much short if one come on the land and drive across the field to the river .
Thus I have spar myself quite half a mile , and have come much quicker to my sea-cattle ! '
` Oh , you 're a lucky fellow ! '
say Big Klaus .
` Do you think I should also get some cattle if I go to the bottom of the river ? '
` Oh , yes !
I think so , ' say Little Klaus .
` But I ca n't carry you in a sack to the river ; you be too heavy for me !
If you like to go there yourself and then creep into the sack , I will throw you in with the great of pleasure . '
` Thank you , ' say Big Klaus ; ` but if I do n't get any sea-cattle when I come there , you will have a good hiding , mind ! '
` Oh , no !
Do n't be so hard on me ! '
Then they go to the river .
When the cattle , which be thirsty , caught sight of the water , they run as quickly a they could to drink .
` Look how they be run ! '
say Little Klaus .
` They want to go to the bottom again ! '
` Yes ; but help me first , ' say Big Klaus , ` or else you shall have a beating ! '
And so he creep into the large sack , which be lie on the back of one of the ox .
` Put a stone in , for I be afraid I may not reach the bottom , ' say Big Klaus .
` It go all right ! '
say Little Klaus ; but still he lay a big stone in the sack , fasten it up tight , and then push it in .
Plump !
there be Big Klaus in the water , and he sink like lead to the bottom . '
I doubt if he will find any cattle ! '
say Little Klaus a he drive his own home .
PRINCE RING -LRB- 30 -RRB- -LRB- 30 -RRB- From the Icelandic .
Once upon a time there be a King and his Queen in their kingdom .
They have one daughter , who be call Ingiborg , and one son , whose name be Ring .
He be less fond of adventure than men of rank usually be in those day , and be not famous for strength or feat of arm .
When he be twelve year old , one fine winter day he ride into the forest along with his men to enjoy himself .
They go on a long way , until they catch sight of a hind with a gold ring on it horn .
The Prince be eager to catch it , if possible , so they give chase and rode on without stop until all the horse begin to founder beneath them .
At last the Prince 's horse give way too , and then there come over them a darkness so black that they could no longer see the hind .
By this time they be far away from any house , and think it be high time to be make their way home again , but they find they have get lose now .
At first they all keep together , but soon each begin to think that he know the right way best ; so they separate , and all go in different direction .
The Prince , too , have get lose like the rest , and wander on for a time until he come to a little clearing in the forest not far from the sea , where he saw a woman sit on a chair and a big barrel stand beside her .
The Prince go up to her and salute her politely , and she receive him very graciously .
He look down into the barrel then , and saw lie at the bottom an unusually beautiful gold ring , which please him so much that he could not take his eye off it .
The woman saw this , and say that he might have it if he would take the trouble to get it ; for which the Prince thank her , and say it be at least worth try .
So he lean over into the barrel , which do not seem very deep , and think he would easily reach the ring ; but the more he stretch down after it the deep grow the barrel .
As he be thus bend down into it the woman suddenly rise up and push him in head first , say that now he could take up his quarter there .
Then she fix the top on the barrel and throw it out into the sea .
The Prince think himself in a bad plight now , a he felt the barrel float out from the land and toss about on the wave .
How many day he spend thus he could not tell , but at last he felt that the barrel be knock against rock , at which he be a little cheered , think it be probably land and not merely a reef in the sea .
Being something of a swimmer , he at last make up his mind to kick the bottom out of the barrel , and have do so he be able to get on shore , for the rock by the sea be smooth and level ; but overhead there be high cliff .
It seem difficult to get up these , but he go along the foot of them for a little , till at last he try to climb up , which at last he do .
Having get to the top , he look round about him and saw that he be on an island , which be cover with forest , with apple grow , and altogether pleasant as far a the land be concern .
After he have be there several day , he one day hear a great noise in the forest , which make him terribly afraid , so that he run to hide himself among the tree .
Then he saw a Giant approaching , drag a sledge load with wood , and make straight for him , so that he could see nothing for it but to lie down just where he be .
When the Giant come across him , he stand still and look at the Prince for a little ; then he take him up in his arm and carry him home to his house , and be exceedingly kind to him .
He give him to his wife , say he have find this child in the wood , and she could have it to help her in the house .
The old woman be greatly pleased , and begin to fondle the Prince with the utmost delight .
He stay there with them , and be very willing and obedient to them in everything , while they grow kinder to him every day .
One day the Giant take him round and show him all his room except the parlour ; this make the Prince curious to have a look into it , think there must be some very rare treasure there .
So one day , when the Giant have go into the forest , he try to get into the parlour , and manage to get the door open half-way .
Then he saw that some living creature move inside and run along the floor towards him and say something , which make him so frighten that he spring back from the door and shut it again .
As soon a the fright begin to pass off he try it again , for he think it would be interest to hear what it say ; but thing go just a before with him .
He then get angry with himself , and , summon up all his courage , try it a third time , and open the door of the room and stand firm .
Then he saw that it be a big Dog , which speak to him and say : ` Choose me , Prince Ring . '
The Prince go away rather afraid , think with himself that it be no great treasure after all ; but all the same what it have say to him stick in his mind .
It be not say how long the Prince stay with the Giant , but one day the latter come to him and say he would now take him over to the mainland out of the island , for he himself have no long time to live .
He also thank him for his good service , and tell him to choose some-one of his possession , for he would get whatever he want .
Ring thank him heartily , and say there be no need to pay him for his service , they be so little worth ; but if he do wish to give him anything he would choose what be in the parlour .
The Giant be take by surprise , and say : ` There , you choose my old woman 's right hand ; but I must not break my word . '
Upon this he go to get the Dog , which come run with sign of great delight ; but the Prince be so much afraid of it that it be all he could do to keep from show his alarm .
After this the Giant accompany him down to the sea , where he saw a stone boat which be just big enough to hold the two of them and the Dog .
On reach the mainland the Giant take a friendly farewell of Ring , and tell him he might take possession of all that be in the island after he and his wife die , which would happen within two week from that time .
The Prince thank him for this and for all his other kindness , and the Giant return home , while Ring go up some distance from the sea ; but he do not know what land he have come to , and be afraid to speak to the Dog .
After he have walk on in silence for a time the Dog speak to him and say : ` You do n't seem to have much curiosity , see you never ask my name . '
The Prince then force himself to ask , ` What be your name ? '
` You have best call me Snati-Snati , ' say the Dog .
` Now we be come to a King 's seat , and you must ask the King to keep u all winter , and to give you a little room for both of u . '
The Prince now begin to be less afraid of the Dog .
They come to the King and ask him to keep them all the winter , to which he agree .
When the King 's men saw the Dog they begin to laugh at it , and make a if they would tease it ; but when the Prince saw this he advise them not to do it , or they might have the bad of it .
They reply that they do n't care a bit what he think .
After Ring have be with the King for some day the latter begin to think there be a great deal in him , and esteem him more than the others .
The King , however , have a counsellor call Red , who become very jealous when he saw how much the King esteem Ring ; and one day he talk to him , and say he could not understand why he have so good an opinion of this stranger , who have not yet show himself superior to other men in anything .
The King reply that it be only a short time since he have come there .
Red then ask him to send them both to cut down wood next morning , and see which of them could do most work .
Snati-Snati heard this and tell it to Ring , advise him to ask the King for two ax , so that he might have one in reserve if the first one get break .
Next morning the King ask Ring and Red to go and cut down tree for him , and both agree .
Ring get the two ax , and each go his own way ; but when the Prince have get out into the wood Snati take one of the ax and begin to hew along with him .
In the even the King come to look over their day 's work , a Red have propose , and find that Ring 's wood-heap be more than twice a big . '
I suspect , ' say the King , ` that Ring be not quite useless ; never have I see such a day 's work . '
Ring be now in far great esteem with the King than before , and Red be all the more discontented .
One day he come to the King and say , ` If Ring be such a mighty man , I think you might ask him to kill the wild ox in the wood here , and flay them the same day , and bring you the horn and the hide in the evening . '
` Do n't you think that a desperate errand ? '
say the King , ` see they be so dangerous , and no one have ever yet venture to go against them ? '
Red answer that he have only one life to lose , and it would be interesting to see how brave he be ; besides , the King would have good reason to ennoble him if he overcome them .
The King at last allow himself , though rather unwillingly , to be win over by Red 's persistency , and one day ask Ring to go and kill the ox that be in the wood for him , and bring their horn and hide to him in the evening .
Not know how dangerous the ox be , Ring be quite ready , and go off at once , to the great delight of Red , who be now sure of his death .
As soon a Ring come in sight of the ox they come bellow to meet him ; one of them be tremendously big , the other rather less .
Ring grow terribly afraid .
` How do you like them ? '
ask Snati .
` Not well at all , ' say the Prince .
` We can do nothing else , ' say Snati , ` than attack them , if it be to go well ; you will go against the little one , and I shall take the other . '
With this Snati leapt at the big one , and be not long in bring him down .
Meanwhile the Prince go against the other with fear and trembling , and by the time Snati come to help him the ox have nearly get him under , but Snati be not slow in help his master to kill it .
Each of them then begin to flay their own ox , but Ring be only half through by the time Snati have finish his .
In the evening , after they have finish this task , the Prince think himself unfit to carry all the horn and both the hide , so Snati tell him to lay them all on his back until they get to the Palace gate .
The Prince agree , and lay everything on the Dog except the skin of the small ox , which he stagger along with himself .
At the Palace gate he leave everything lying , go before the King , and ask him to come that length with him , and there hand over to him the hide and horn of the ox .
The King be greatly surprise at his valour , and say he know no one like him , and thank him heartily for what he have do .
After this the King set Ring next to himself , and all esteem him highly , and hold him to be a great hero ; nor could Red any long say anything against him , though he grow still more determined to destroy him .
One day a good idea come into his head .
He come to the King and say he have something to say to him .
` What be that ? '
say the King .
Red say that he have just remember the gold cloak , gold chess-board , and bright gold piece that the King have lose about a year before .
` Do n't remind me of them ! '
say the King .
Red , however , go on to say that , since Ring be such a mighty man that he could do everything , it have occur to him to advise the King to ask him to search for these treasure , and come back with them before Christmas ; in return the King should promise him his daughter .
The King reply that he think it altogether unbecoming to propose such a thing to Ring , see that he could not tell him where the thing be ; but Red pretend not to hear the King 's excuse , and go on talk about it until the King give in to him .
One day , a month or so before Christmas , the King speak to Ring , say that he wish to ask a great favour of him .
` What be that ? '
say Ring .
` It be this , ' say the King : ` that you find for me my gold cloak , my gold chess-board , and my bright gold piece , that be steal from me about a year ago .
If you can bring them to me before Christmas I will give you my daughter in marriage . '
` Where be I to look for them , then ? '
say Ring .
` That you must find out for yourself , ' say the King : ' I do n't know . '
Ring now leave the King , and be very silent , for he saw he be in a great difficulty : but , on the other hand , he think it be excellent to have such a chance of win the King 's daughter .
Snati notice that his master be at a loss , and say to him that he should not disregard what the King have ask him to do ; but he would have to act upon his advice , otherwise he would get into great difficulty .
The Prince assent to this , and begin to prepare for the journey .
After he have take leave of the King , and be set out on the search , Snati say to him , ` Now you must first of all go about the neighbourhood , and gather as much salt a ever you can . '
The Prince do so , and gather so much salt that he could hardly carry it ; but Snati say , ` Throw it on my back , ' which he accordingly do , and the Dog then run on before the Prince , until they come to the foot of a steep cliff .
` We must go up here , ' say Snati . '
I do n't think that will be child 's play , ' say the Prince .
` Hold fast by my tail , ' say Snati ; and in this way he pull Ring up on the low shelf of the rock .
The Prince begin to get giddy , but up go Snati on to the second shelf .
Ring be nearly swooning by this time , but Snati make a third effort and reach the top of the cliff , where the Prince fell down in a faint .
After a little , however , he recover again , and they go a short distance along a level plain , until they come to a cave .
This be on Christmas Eve .
They go up above the cave , and find a window in it , through which they look , and saw four troll lie asleep beside the fire , over which a large porridge-pot be hang .
` Now you must empty all the salt into the porridge-pot , ' say Snati .
Ring do so , and soon the troll waken up .
The old hag , who be the most frightful of them all , go first to taste the porridge .
` How come this ? '
she say ; ` the porridge be salt !
I get the milk by witchcraft yesterday out of four kingdom , and now it be salt ! '
All the others then come to taste the porridge , and think it nice , but after they have finish it the old hag grow so thirsty that she could stand it no longer , and ask her daughter to go out and bring her some water from the river that run near by . '
I wo n't go , ' say she , ` unless you lend me your bright gold piece . '
` Though I should die you sha n't have that , ' say the hag .
` Die , then , ' say the girl .
` Well , then , take it , you brat , ' say the old hag , ` and be off with you , and make haste with the water . '
The girl take the gold and run out with it , and it be so bright that it shine all over the plain .
As soon a she come to the river she lay down to take a drink of the water , but meanwhile the two of them have get down off the roof and thrust her , head first , into the river .
The old hag begin now to long for the water , and say that the girl would be run about with the gold piece all over the plain , so she ask her son to go and get her a drop of water . '
I wo n't go , ' say he , ` unless I get the gold cloak . '
` Though I should die you sha n't have that , ' say the hag .
` Die , then , ' say the son .
` Well , then , take it , ' say the old hag , ` and be off with you , but you must make haste with the water . '
He put on the cloak , and when he come outside it shine so bright that he could see to go with it .
On reach the river he go to take a drink like his sister , but at that moment Ring and Snati spring upon him , take the cloak from him , and throw him into the river .
The old hag could stand the thirst no longer , and ask her husband to go for a drink for her ; the brat , she say , be of course run about and play themselves , just a she have expect they would , little wretch that they be . '
I wo n't go , ' say the old troll , ` unless you lend me the gold chess-board . '
` Though I should die you sha n't have that , ' say the hag . '
I think you may just as well do that , ' say he , ` since you wo n't grant me such a little favour . '
` Take it , then , you utter disgrace ! '
say the old hag , ` since you be just like these two brat . '
The old troll now go out with the gold chess-board , and down to the river , and be about to take a drink , when Ring and Snati come upon him , take the chess-board from him , and throw him into the river .
Before they have get back again , however , and up on top of the cave , they saw the poor old fellow 's ghost come march up from the river .
Snati immediately spring upon him , and Ring assist in the attack , and after a hard struggle they master him a second time .
When they get back again to the window they saw that the old hag be move towards the door .
` Now we must go in at once , ' say Snati , ` and try to master her there , for if she once get out we shall have no chance with her .
She be the bad witch that ever live , and no iron can cut her .
One of u must pour boil porridge out of the pot on her , and the other punch her with red-hot iron . '
In they go then , and no sooner do the hag see them than she say , ` So you have come , Prince Ring ; you must have see to my husband and child . '
Snati saw that she be about to attack them , and sprang at her with a red-hot iron from the fire , while Ring keep pour boil porridge on her without stopping , and in this way they at last get her kill .
Then they burn the old troll and her to ash , and explore the cave , where they find plenty of gold and treasure .
The most valuable of these they carry with them as far a the cliff , and leave them there .
Then they hasten home to the King with his three treasure , where they arrive late on Christmas night , and Ring hand them over to him .
The King be beside himself with joy , and be astonish at how clever a man Ring be in all kind of feat , so that he esteem him still more highly than before , and betroth his daughter to him ; and the feast for this be to last all through Christmastide .
Ring thank the King courteously for this and all his other kindness , and as soon a he have finish eating and drinking in the hall go off to sleep in his own room .
Snati , however , ask permission to sleep in the Prince 's bed for that night , while the Prince should sleep where the Dog usually lay .
Ring say he be welcome to do so , and that he deserve more from him than that come to .
So Snati go up into the Prince 's bed , but after a time he come back , and tell Ring he could go there himself now , but to take care not to meddle with anything that be in the bed .
Now the story come back to Red , who come into the hall and show the King his right arm want the hand , and say that now he could see what kind of a man his intended son-in-law be , for he have do this to him without any cause whatever .
The King become very angry , and say he would soon find out the truth about it , and if Ring have cut off his hand without good cause he should be hang ; but if it be otherwise , then Red should die .
So the King sent for Ring and ask him for what reason he have do this .
Snati , however , have just tell Ring what have happen during the night , and in reply he ask the King to go with him and he would show him something .
The King go with him to his sleeping-room , and saw lie on the bed a man 's hand hold a sword .
` This hand , ' say Ring , ` come over the partition during the night , and be about to run me through in my bed , if I have not defend myself . '
The King answer that in that case he could not blame him for protect his own life , and that Red be well worthy of death .
So Red be hang , and Ring marry the King 's daughter .
The first night that they go to bed together Snati ask Ring to allow him to lie at their foot , and this Ring allow him to do .
During the night he hear a howling and outcry beside them , strike a light in a hurry and saw an ugly dog 's skin lying near him , and a beautiful Prince in the bed .
Ring instantly take the skin and burn it , and then shake the Prince , who be lie unconscious , until he wake up .
The bridegroom then ask his name ; he reply that he be call Ring , and be a King 's son .
In his youth he have lose his mother , and in her place his father have marry a witch , who have lay a spell on him that he should turn into a dog , and never be release from the spell unless a Prince of the same name a himself allow him to sleep at his foot the first night after his marriage .
He add far , ` As soon a she know that you be my namesake she try to get you destroy , so that you might not free me from the spell .
She be the hind that you and your companion chase ; she be the woman that you find in the clearing with the barrel , and the old hag that we just now kill in the cave . '
After the feasting be over the two namesake , along with other men , go to the cliff and bring all the treasure home to the Palace .
Then they go to the island and remove all that be valuable from it .
Ring give to his namesake , whom he have free from the spell , his sister Ingiborg and his father 's kingdom to look after , but he himself stay with his father-in-law the King , and have half the kingdom while he live and the whole of it after his death .
THE SWINEHERD There be once a poor Prince .
He possess a kingdom which , though small , be yet large enough for him to marry on , and marry he wish to be .
Now it be certainly a little audacious of him to venture to say to the Emperor 's daughter , ` Will you marry me ? '
But he do venture to say so , for his name be know far and wide .
There be hundred of princess who would gladly have say ` Yes , ' but would she say the same ?
Well , we shall see .
On the grave of the Prince 's father grow a rose-tree , a very beautiful rose-tree .
It only bloom every five year , and then bore but a single rise , but oh , such a rise !
Its scent be so sweet that when you smelt it you forget all your care and trouble .
And he have also a nightingale which could sing a if all the beautiful melody in the world be shut up in it little throat .
This rise and this nightingale the Princess be to have , and so they be both put into silver casket and send to her .
The Emperor have them bring to him in the great hall , where the Princess be play ` Here come a duke a-riding ' with her lady-in-waiting .
And when she catch sight of the big casket which contain the present , she clap her hand for joy .
` If only it be a little pussy cat ! '
she say .
But the rose-tree with the beautiful rise come out .
` But how prettily it be make ! '
say all the lady-in-waiting .
` It be more than pretty , ' say the Emperor , ` it be charm ! '
But the Princess felt it , and then she almost begin to cry .
` Ugh !
Papa , ' she say , ` it be not artificial , it be REAL ! '
` Ugh ! '
say all the ladies-in-waiting , ` it be real ! '
` Let u see first what be in the other casket before we begin to be angry , ' think the Emperor , and there come out the nightingale .
It sing so beautifully that one could scarcely utter a cross word against it .
` Superbe !
charmant ! '
say the lady-in-waiting , for they all chatter French , each one bad than the other .
` How much the bird remind me of the musical snuff-box of the late Empress ! '
say an old courtier .
` Ah , yes , it be the same tone , the same execution ! '
` Yes , ' say the Emperor ; and then he weep like a little child . '
I hope that this , at least , be not real ? '
ask the Princess .
` Yes , it be a real bird , ' say those who have bring it .
` Then let the bird fly away , ' say the Princess ; and she would not on any account allow the Prince to come .
` But he be nothing daunt .
He paint his face brown and black , draw his cap well over his face , and knock at the door .
` Good-day , Emperor , ' he say .
` Can I get a place here a servant in the castle ? '
` Yes , ' say the Emperor , ` but there be so many who ask for a place that I do n't know whether there will be one for you ; but , still , I will think of you .
Stay , it have just occur to me that I want someone to look after the swine , for I have so very many of them . '
And the Prince get the situation of Imperial Swineherd .
He have a wretched little room close to the pigsty ; here he have to stay , but the whole day he sit work , and when evening be come he have make a pretty little pot .
All round it be little bell , and when the pot boil they jingle most beautifully and play the old tune -- ` Where be Augustus dear ?
Alas !
he 's not here , here , here ! '
But the most wonderful thing be , that when one hold one 's finger in the steam of the pot , then at once one could smell what dinner be ready in any fire-place in the town .
That be indeed something quite different from the rise .
Now the Princess come walk past with all her lady-in-waiting , and when she hear the tune she stand still and her face beam with joy , for she also could play ` Where be Augustus dear ? '
It be the only tune she know , but that she could play with one finger .
` Why , that be what I play ! '
she say .
` He must be a most accomplished Swineherd !
Listen !
Go down and ask him what the instrument cost . '
And one of the lady-in-waiting have to go down ; but she put on wooden clog .
` What will you take for the pot ? '
ask the lady-in-waiting . '
I will have ten kiss from the Princess , ' answer the Swineherd .
` Heaven forbid ! '
say the lady-in-waiting .
` Yes , I will sell it for nothing less , ' reply the Swineherd .
` Well , what do he say ? '
ask the Princess . '
I really hardly like to tell you , ' answer the lady-in-waiting .
` Oh , then you can whisper it to me . '
` He be disoblige ! '
say the Princess , and go away .
But she have only go a few step when the bell ring out so prettily -- ` Where be Augustus dear ?
Alas !
he 's not here , here , here . '
` Listen ! '
say the Princess .
` Ask him whether he will take ten kiss from my ladies-in-waiting . '
` No , thank you , ' say the Swineherd .
` Ten kiss from the Princess , or else I keep my pot . '
` That be very tiresome ! '
say the Princess .
` But you must put yourselves in front of me , so that no one can see . '
And the ladies-in-waiting placed themselves in front and then spread out their dress ; so the Swineherd get his ten kiss , and she get the pot .
What happiness that be !
The whole night and the whole day the pot be make to boil ; there be not a fire-place in the whole town where they do not know what be be cook , whether it be at the chancellor 's or at the shoemaker 's .
The lady-in-waiting dance and clap their hand .
` We know who be go to have soup and pancake ; we know who be go to have porridge and sausage -- be n't it interest ? '
` Yes , very interesting ! '
say the first lady-in-waiting .
` But do n't say anything about it , for I be the Emperor 's daughter . '
` Oh , no , of course we wo n't ! '
say everyone .
The Swineherd -- that be to say , the Prince -LRB- though they do not know he be anything but a true Swineherd -RRB- -- let no day pass without make something , and one day he make a rattle which , when it be turn round , play all the waltz , galops , and polka which have ever be know since the world begin .
` But that be superbe ! '
say the Princess a she pass by . '
I have never hear a more beautiful composition .
Listen !
Go down and ask him what this instrument cost ; but I wo n't kiss him again . '
` He want a hundred kiss from the Princess , ' say the lady-in-waiting who have go down to ask him . '
I believe he be mad ! '
say the Princess , and then she go on ; but she have only go a few step when she stop .
` One ought to encourage art , ' she say . '
I be the Emperor 's daughter !
Tell him he shall have , a before , ten kiss ; the rest he can take from my ladies-in-waiting . '
` But we do n't at all like be kiss by him , ' say the lady-in-waiting .
` That 's nonsense , ' say the Princess ; ` and if I can kiss him , you can too .
Besides , remember that I give you board and lodge . '
So the lady-in-waiting have to go down to him again . '
A hundred kiss from the Princess , ' say he , ` or each keep his own . '
` Put yourselves in front of u , ' she say then ; and so all the ladies-in-waiting put themselves in front , and he begin to kiss the Princess .
` What can that commotion be by the pigsty ? '
ask the Emperor , who be stand on the balcony .
He rub his eye and put on his spectacle .
` Why those be the ladies-in-waiting play their game ; I must go down to them . '
So he take off his shoe , which be shoe though he have tread them down into slipper .
What a hurry he be in , to be sure !
As soon a he come into the yard he walk very softly , and the ladies-in-waiting be so busy count the kiss and see fair play that they never notice the Emperor .
He stand on tiptoe .
` What be that ? '
he say , when he saw the kissing ; and then he throw one of his slipper at their head just a the Swineherd be take his eighty-sixth kiss .
` Be off with you ! '
say the Emperor , for he be very angry .
And the Princess and the Swineherd be drive out of the empire .
Then she stand still and weep ; the Swineherd be scold , and the rain be stream down .
` Alas , what an unhappy creature I be ! '
sob the Princess .
` If only I have take the beautiful Prince !
Alas , how unfortunate I be ! '
And the Swineherd go behind a tree , wash the black and brown off his face , throw away his old clothes , and then step forward in his splendid dress , look so beautiful that the Princess be oblige to courtesy . '
I now come to this .
I despise you ! '
he say .
` You would have nothing to do with a noble Prince ; you do not understand the rise or the nightingale , but you could kiss the Swineherd for the sake of a toy .
This be what you get for it ! '
And he go into his kingdom and shut the door in her face , and she have to stay outside singing -- ` Where 's my Augustus dear ?

he 's not here , here , here !
HOW TO TELL A TRUE PRINCESS There be once upon a time a Prince who want to marry a Princess , but she must be a true Princess .
So he travel through the whole world to find one , but there be always something against each .
There be plenty of Princesses , but he could not find out if they be true Princesses .
In every case there be some little defect , which show the genuine article be not yet find .
So he come home again in very low spirit , for he have want very much to have a true Princess .
One night there be a dreadful storm ; it thunder and lighten and the rain stream down in torrent .
It be fearful !
There be a knocking heard at the Palace gate , and the old King go to open it .
There stand a Princess outside the gate ; but oh , in what a sad plight she be from the rain and the storm !
The water be run down from her hair and her dress into the point of her shoe and out at the heel again .
And yet she say she be a true Princess !
` Well , we shall soon find that ! '
think the old Queen .
But she say nothing , and go into the sleeping-room , take off all the bed-clothes , and lay a pea on the bottom of the bed .
Then she put twenty mattress on top of the pea , and twenty eider-down quilt on the top of the mattress .
And this be the bed in which the Princess be to sleep .
The next morning she be ask how she have slept .
` Oh , very badly ! '
say the Princess . '
I scarcely close my eye all night !
I be sure I do n't know what be in the bed .
I lay on something so hard that my whole body be black and blue .
It be dreadful ! '
Now they perceive that she be a true Princess , because she have felt the pea through the twenty mattress and the twenty eider-down quilt .
No one but a true Princess could be so sensitive .
So the Prince marry her , for now he know that at last he have get hold of a true Princess .
And the pea be put into the Royal Museum , where it be still to be see if no one have steal it .
Now this be a true story .
THE BLUE MOUNTAINS There be once a Scotsman and an Englishman and an Irishman serving in the army together , who take it into their head to run away on the first opportunity they could get .
The chance come and they take it .
They go on travel for two day through a great forest , without food or drink , and without come across a single house , and every night they have to climb up into the tree through fear of the wild beast that be in the wood .
On the second morning the Scotsman saw from the top of his tree a great castle far away .
He say to himself that he would certainly die if he stay in the forest without anything to eat but the root of grass , which would not keep him alive very long .
As soon , then , a he get down out of the tree he set off towards the castle , without so much a tell his companion that he have see it at all ; perhaps the hunger and want they have suffer have change their nature so much that the one do not care what become of the other if he could save himself .
He travel on most of the day , so that it be quite late when he reach the castle , and to his great disappointment find nothing but close door and no smoke rise from the chimney .
He think there be nothing for it but to die after all , and have lie down beside the wall , when he hear a window be open high above him .
At this he look up , and saw the most beautiful woman he have ever set eye on .
` Oh , it be Fortune that have send you to me , ' he say .
` It be indeed , ' say she .
` What be you in need of , or what have send you here ? '
` Necessity , ' say he . '
I be die for want of food and drink . '
` Come inside , then , ' she say ; ` there be plenty of both here . '
Accordingly he go in to where she be , and she open a large room for him , where he saw a number of men lie asleep .
She then set food before him , and after that show him to the room where the others be .
He lay down on one of the bed and fell sound asleep .
And now we must go back to the two that he leave behind him in the wood .
When nightfall and the time of the wild beast come upon these , the Englishman happen to climb up into the very same tree on which the Scotsman be when he get a sight of the castle ; and as soon a the day begin to dawn and the Englishman look to the four quarter of heaven , what do he see but the castle too !
Off he go without say a word to the Irishman , and everything happen to him just a it have do to the Scotsman .
The poor Irishman be now leave all alone , and do not know where the others have go to , so he just stay where he be , very sad and miserable .
When night come he climb up into the same tree a the Englishman have be on the night before .
As soon a day come he also saw the castle , and set out towards it ; but when he reach it he could see no sign of fire or living be about it .
Before long , however , he hear the window open above his head , look up , and behold the most beautiful woman he have ever see .
He ask if she would give him food and drink , and she answer kindly and heartily that she would , if he would only come inside .
This he do very willingly , and she set before him food and drink that he have never see the like of before .
In the room there be a bed , with diamond ring hang at every loop of the curtain , and everything that be in the room besides astonish him so much that he actually forget that he be hungry .
When she saw that he be not eat at all , she ask him what he want yet , to which he reply that he would neither eat nor drink until he know who she be , or where she come from , or who have put her there . '
I shall tell you that , ' say she . '
I be an enchanted Princess , and my father have promise that the man who release me from the spell shall have the third of his kingdom while he be alive , and the whole of it after he be dead , and marry me as well .
If ever I saw a man who look likely to do this , you be the one .
I have be here for sixteen year now , and no one who ever come to the castle have ask me who I be , except yourself .
Every other man that have come , so long a I have be here , lie asleep in the big room down there . '
` Tell me , then , ' say the Irishman , ` what be the spell that have be lay on you , and how you can be free from it . '
` There be a little room there , ' say the Princess , ` and if I could get a man to stay in it from ten o'clock till midnight for three night on end I should be free from the spell . ' '
I be the man for you , then , ' say he ; ' I will take on hand to do it . '
Thereupon she bring him a pipe and tobacco , and he go into the room ; but before long he hear a hammering and knock on the outside of the door , and be tell to open it . '
I wo n't , ' he say .
The next moment the door come fly in , and those outside along with it .
They knock him down , and kick him , and kneel on his body till it come to midnight ; but as soon a the cock crew they all disappear .
The Irishman be little more than alive by this time .
As soon a daylight appear the Princess come , and find him lie full length on the floor , unable to speak a word .
She take a bottle , rub him from head to foot with something from it , and thereupon he be as sound a ever ; but after what he have get that night he be very unwilling to try it a second time .
The Princess , however , entreat him to stay , say that the next night would not be so bad , and in the end he give in and stay .
When it be get near midnight he hear them order him to open the door , and there be three of them for every one that there have be the previous evening .
He do not make the slight movement to go out to them or to open the door , but before long they break it up , and be in on top of him .
They lay hold of him , and keep throw him between them up to the ceiling , or jump above him , until the cock crew , when they all disappear .
When day come the Princess go to the room to see if he be still alive , and take the bottle put it to his nostril , which soon bring him to himself .
The first thing he say then be that he be a fool to go on get himself kill for anyone he ever saw , and be determine to be off and stay there no longer , When the Princess learn his intention she entreat him to stay , remind him that another night would free her from the spell .
` Besides , ' she say , ` if there be a single spark of life in you when the day come , the stuff that be in this bottle will make you as sound a ever you be . '
With all this the Irishman decide to stay ; but that night there be three at him for every one that be there the two night before , and it look very unlikely that he would be alive in the morning after all that he get .
When morning dawn , and the Princess come to see if he be still alive , she find him lie on the floor a if dead .
She try to see if there be breath in him , but could not quite make it out .
Then she put her hand on his pulse , and find a faint movement in it .
Accordingly she pour what be in the bottle on him , and before long he rise up on his foot , and be as well a ever he be .
So that business be finish , and the Princess be free from the spell .
The Princess then tell the Irishman that she must go away for the present , but would return for him in a few day in a carriage draw by four grey horse .
He tell her to ` be aisy , ' and not speak like that to him . '
I have pay dear for you for the last three night , ' he say , ` if I have to part with you now ; ' but in the twinkling of an eye she have disappear .
He do not know what to do with himself when he saw that she be go , but before she go she have give him a little rod , with which he could , when he please , waken the men who have be sleep there , some of them for sixteen year .
After be thus leave alone , he go in and stretch himself on three chair that be in the room , when what do he see come in at the door but a little fair-haired lad .
` Where do you come from , my lad ? '
say the Irishman . '
I come to make ready your food for you , ' say he .
` Who tell you to do that ? '
say the Irishman .
` My mistress , ' answer the lad -- ` the Princess that be under the spell and be now free . '
By this the Irishman know that she have send the lad to wait on him .
The lad also tell him that his mistress wish him to be ready next morning at nine o'clock , when she would come for him with the carriage , a she have promise .
He be greatly pleased at this , and next morning , when the time be draw near , go out into the garden ; but the little fair-haired lad take a big pin out of his pocket , and stick it into the back of the Irishman 's coat without his notice it , whereupon he fell sound asleep .
Before long the Princess come with the carriage and four horse , and ask the lad whether his master be awake .
He say that he be n't .
` It be bad for him , ' say she , ` when the night be not long enough for him to sleep .
Tell him that if he do n't meet me at this time to-morrow it be not likely that he will ever see me again all his life . '
As soon a she be go the lad take the pin out of his master 's coat , who instantly awake .
The first word he say to the lad be , ` Have you see her ? '
` Yes , ' say he , ` and she bid me tell you that if you do n't meet her at nine o'clock to-morrow you will never see her again . '
He be very sorry when he hear this , and could not understand why the sleep should have fall upon him just when she be come .
He decide , however , to go early to bed that night , in order to rise in time nest morning , and so he do .
When it be get near nine o'clock he go out to the garden to wait till she come , and the fair-haired lad along with him ; but as soon a the lad get the chance he stick the pin into his master 's coat again and he fell asleep a before .
Precisely at nine o'clock come the Princess in the carriage with four horse , and ask the lad if his master have get up yet ; but he say ` No , he be asleep , just a he be the day before . '
` Dear !
dear ! '
say the Princess , ' I be sorry for him .
Was the sleep he have last night not enough for him ?
Tell him that he will never see me here again ; and here be a sword that you will give him in my name , and my blessing along with it . '
With this she go off , and as soon a she have go the lad take the pin out of his master 's coat .
He awake instantly , and the first word he say be , ` Have you see her ? '
The lad say that he have , and there be the sword she have leave for him .
The Irishman be ready to kill the lad out of sheer vexation , but when he give a glance over his shoulder not a trace of the fair-haired lad be leave .
Being thus leave all alone , he think of go into the room where all the men be lie asleep , and there among the rest he find his two comrade who have desert along with him .
Then he remember what the Princess have tell him -- that he have only to touch them with the rod she have give him and they would all awake ; and the first he touch be his own comrade .
They start to their foot at once , and he give them a much silver and gold a they could carry when they go away .
There be plenty to do before he get all the others waken , for the two door of the castle be crowd with them all the day long .
The loss of the Princess , however , keep rankle in his mind day and night , till finally he think he would go about the world to see if he could find anyone to give him news of her .
So he take the best horse in the stable and set out .
Three year he spend travel through forest and wilderness , but could find no one able to tell him anything of the Princess .
At last he fell into so great despair that he think he would put an end to his own life , and for this purpose lay hold of the sword that she have give him by the hand of the fair-haired lad ; but on draw it from it sheath he notice that there be some write on one side of the blade .
He look at this , and read there , ` You will find me in the Blue Mountains . '
This make him take heart again , and he give up the idea of kill himself , think that he would go on in hope of meet some one who could tell him where the Blue Mountains be .
After he have go a long way without think where he be go , he saw at last a light far away , and make straight for it .
On reach it he find it come from a little house , and as soon a the man inside hear the noise of the horse 's foot he come out to see who be there .
Seeing a stranger on horseback , he ask what bring him there and where he be go . '
I have live here , ' say he , ` for three hundred year , and all that time I have not see a single human be but yourself . ' '
I have be go about for the last three year , ' say the Irishman , ` to see if I could find anyone who can tell me where the Blue Mountains be . '
` Come in , ' say the old man , ` and stay with me all night .
I have a book which contain the history of the world , which I shall go through to-night , and if there be such a place a the Blue Mountains in it we shall find it out . '
The Irishman stay there all night , and as soon a morning come rise to go .
