The old man say he have not go to sleep all night for go through the book , but there be not a word about the Blue Mountains in it .
` But I 'll tell you what , ' he say , ` if there be such a place on earth at all , I have a brother who live nine hundred mile from here , and he be sure to know where they be , if anyone in this world do . '
The Irishman answer that he could never go these nine hundred mile , for his horse be give in already .
` That do n't matter , ' say the old man ; ' I can do good than that .
I have only to blow my whistle and you will be at my brother 's house before nightfall . '
So he blow the whistle , and the Irishman do not know where on earth he be until he find himself at the other old man 's door , who also tell him that it be three hundred year since he have see anyone , and ask him where he be go . '
I be go to see if I can find anyone that can tell me where the Blue Mountains be , ' he say .
` If you will stay with me to-night , ' say the old man , ' I have a book of the history of the world , and I shall know where they be before daylight , if there be such a place in it at all . '
He stay there all night , but there be not a word in the book about the Blue Mountains .
Seeing that he be rather cast down , the old man tell him that he have a brother nine hundred mile away , and that if information could be get about them from anyone it would be from him ; ` and I will enable you , ' he say , ` to reach the place where he live before night . '
So he blow his whistle , and the Irishman land at the brother 's house before nightfall .
When the old man saw him he say he have not see a single man for three hundred year , and be very much surprise to see anyone come to him now .
` Where be you go to ? '
he say . '
I be go about ask for the Blue Mountains , ' say the Irishman .
` The Blue Mountains ? '
say the old man .
` Yes , ' say the Irishman . '
I never hear the name before ; but if they do exist I shall find them out .
I be master of all the bird in the world , and have only to blow my whistle and every one will come to me .
I shall then ask each of them to tell where it come from , and if there be any way of find out the Blue Mountains that be it . '
So he blow his whistle , and when he blow it then all the bird of the world begin to gather .
The old man question each of them a to where they have come from , but there be not one of them that have come from the Blue Mountains .
After he have run over them all , however , he miss a big Eagle that be want , and wonder that it have not come .
Soon afterwards he saw something big coming towards him , darken the sky .
It keep come nearer and grow big , and what be this after all but the Eagle ?
When she arrive the old man scold her , and ask what have keep her so long behind . '
I could n't help it , ' she say ; ' I have more than twenty time far to come than any bird that have come here to-day . '
` Where have you come from , then ? '
say the old man .
` From the Blue Mountains , ' say she .
` Indeed ! '
say the old man ; and what be they do there ? '
` They be make ready this very day , ' say the Eagle , ` for the marriage of the daughter of the King of the Blue Mountains .
For three year now she have refuse to marry anyone whatsoever , until she should give up all hope of the come of the man who release her from the spell .
Now she can wait no longer , for three year be the time that she agree with her father to remain without marry . '
The Irishman know that it be for himself she have be wait so long , but he be unable to make any good of it , for he have no hope of reach the Blue Mountains all his life .
The old man notice how sad he grow , and ask the Eagle what she would take for carry this man on her back to the Blue Mountains . '
I must have threescore cattle kill , ' say she , ` and cut up into quarter , and every time I look over my shoulder he must throw one of them into my mouth . '
As soon a the Irishman and the old man hear her demand they go out hunting , and before even they have kill three-score cattle .
They make quarter of them , a the Eagle tell them , and then the old man ask her to lie down , till they would get it all heap up on her back .
First of all , though , they have to get a ladder of fourteen step , to enable them to get on to the Eagle 's back , and there they pile up the meat as well a they could .
Then the old man tell the Irishman to mount , and to remember to throw a quarter of beef to her every time she look round .
He go up , and the old man give the Eagle the word to be off , which she instantly obey ; and every time she turn her head the Irishman throw a quarter of beef into her mouth .
As they come near the border of the kingdom of the Blue Mountains , however , the beef be do , and , when the Eagle look over her shoulder , what be the Irishman at but throw the stone between her tail and her neck !
At this she turn a complete somersault , and throw the Irishman off into the sea , where he fell into the bay that be right in front of the King 's Palace .
Fortunately the point of his toe just touch the bottom , and he manage to get ashore .
When he go up into the town all the street be gleam with light , and the wedding of the Princess be just about to begin .
He go into the first house he come to , and this happen to be the house of the King 's hen-wife .
He ask the old woman what be cause all the noise and light in the town .
` The Princess , ' say she , ` be go to be marry to-night against her will , for she have be expect every day that the man who free her from the spell would come . '
` There be a guinea for you , ' say he ; ` go and bring her here . '
The old woman go , and soon return along with the Princess .
She and the Irishman recognise each other , and be marry , and have a great wedding that last for a year and a day .
THE TINDER-BOX A soldier come march along the high road -- leave , right !
A left , right !
He have his knapsack on his back and a sword by his side , for he have be to the war and be now return home .
An old Witch meet him on the road .
She be very ugly to look at : her under-lip hung down to her breast .
` Good evening , Soldier ! '
she say .
` What a fine sword and knapsack you have !
You be something like a soldier !
You ought to have as much money a you would like to carry ! '
` Thank you , old Witch , ' say the Soldier .
` Do you see that great tree there ? '
say the Witch , point to a tree beside them .
` It be hollow within .
You must climb up to the top , and then you will see a hole through which you can let yourself down into the tree .
I will tie a rope round your waist , so that I may be able to pull you up again when you call . '
` What shall I do down there ? '
ask the Soldier .
` Get money ! '
answer the Witch .
` Listen !
When you reach the bottom of the tree you will find yourself in a large hall ; it be light there , for there be more than three hundred lamp burn .
Then you will see three door , which you can open -- the key be in the lock .
If you go into the first room , you will see a great chest in the middle of the floor with a dog sit upon it ; he have eye as large a saucer , but you need n't trouble about him .
I will give you my blue-check apron , which you must spread out on the floor , and then go back quickly and fetch the dog and set him upon it ; open the chest and take as much money a you like .
It be copper there .
If you would rather have silver , you must go into the next room , where there be a dog with eye as large a mill-wheels .
But do n't take any notice of him ; just set him upon my apron , and help yourself to the money .
If you prefer gold , you can get that too , if you go into the third room , and as much a you like to carry .
But the dog that guard the chest there have eye as large a the Round Tower at Copenhagen !
He be a savage dog , I can tell you ; but you need n't be afraid of him either .
Only , put him on my apron and he wo n't touch you , and you can take out of the chest a much gold a you like ! '
` Come , this be not bad ! '
say the Soldier .
` But what be I to give you , old Witch ; for surely you be not go to do this for nothing ? '
` Yes , I be ! '
reply the Witch .
` Not a single farthing will I take !
For me you shall bring nothing but an old tinder-box which my grandmother forget last time she be down there . '
` Well , tie the rope round my waist !
` say the Soldier .
` Here it be , ' say the Witch , ` and here be my blue-check apron . '
Then the Soldier climb up the tree , let himself down through the hole , and find himself stand , a the Witch have say , underground in the large hall , where the three hundred lamp be burn .
Well , he open the first door .
Ugh !
there sit the dog with eye as big a saucer glare at him .
` You be a fine fellow ! '
say the Soldier , and put him on the Witch 's apron , take as much copper a his pocket could hold ; then he shut the chest , put the dog on it again , and go into the second room .
Sure enough there sit the dog with eye as large a mill-wheels .
` You have well not look at me so hard ! '
say the Soldier .
` Your eye will come out of their socket ! '
And then he set the dog on the apron .
When he saw all the silver in the chest , he throw away the copper he have take , and fill his pocket and knapsack with nothing but silver .
Then he go into the third room .
Horrors !
the dog there have two eye , each as large a the Round Tower at Copenhagen , spin round in his head like wheel .
` Good evening ! '
say the Soldier and salute , for he have never see a dog like this before .
But when he have examine him more closely , he think to himself : ` Now then , I 've have enough of this ! '
and put him down on the floor , and open the chest .
Heavens !
what a heap of gold there be !
With all that he could buy up the whole town , and all the sugar pig , all the tin soldier , whip and rocking-horses in the whole world .
Now he throw away all the silver with which he have fill his pocket and knapsack , and fill them with gold instead -- yes , all his pocket , his knapsack , cap and boot even , so that he could hardly walk .
Now he be rich indeed .
He put the dog back upon the chest , shut the door , and then call up through the tree : ` Now pull me up again , old Witch ! '
` Have you get the tinder-box also ? '
ask the Witch .
` Botheration ! '
say the Soldier , ' I have clean forgotten it ! '
And then he go back and fetch it .
The Witch pull him up , and there he stand again on the high road , with pocket , knapsack , cap and boot fill with gold .
` What do you want to do with the tinder-box ? '
ask the Soldier .
` That do n't matter to you , ' reply the Witch .
` You have get your money , give me my tinder-box . '
` We 'll see ! '
say the Soldier .
` Tell me at once what you want to do with it , or I will draw my sword , and cut off your head ! '
` No ! '
scream the Witch .
The Soldier immediately cut off her head .
That be the end of her !
But he tie up all his gold in her apron , sling it like a bundle over his shoulder , put the tinder-box in his pocket , and set out towards the town .
It be a splendid town !
He turn into the fine inn , order the best chamber and his favourite dinner ; for now that he have so much money he be really rich .
It certainly occur to the servant who have to clean his boot that they be astonishingly old boot for such a rich lord .
But that be because he have not yet buy new one ; next day he appear in respectable boot and fine clothes .
Now , instead of a common soldier he have become a noble lord , and the people tell him about all the grand doings of the town and the King , and what a beautiful Princess his daughter be .
` How can one get to see her ? '
ask the Soldier .
` She be never to be see at all ! '
they tell him ; ` she live in a great copper castle , surround by many wall and tower !
No one except the King may go in or out , for it be prophesy that she will marry a common soldier , and the King can not submit to that . ' '
I should very much like to see her , ' think the Soldier ; but he could not get permission .
Now he live very gaily , go to the theatre , drive in the King 's garden , and give the poor a great deal of money , which be very nice of him ; he have experience in former time how hard it be not to have a farthing in the world .
Now he be rich , wore fine clothes , and make many friend , who all say that he be an excellent man , a real nobleman .
And the Soldier like that .
But a he be always spend money , and never make any more , at last the day come when he have nothing leave but two shilling , and he have to leave the beautiful room in which he have be live , and go into a little attic under the roof , and clean his own boot , and mend them with a darning-needle .
None of his friend come to visit him there , for there be too many stair to climb .
It be a dark evening , and he could not even buy a light .
But all at once it flash across him that there be a little end of tinder in the tinder-box , which he have take from the hollow tree into which the Witch have help him down .
He find the box with the tinder in it ; but just a he be kindle a light , and have strike a spark out of the tinder-box , the door burst open , and the dog with eye as large a saucer , which he have see down in the tree , stand before him and say : ` What do my lord command ? '
` What 's the meaning of this ? '
exclaim the Soldier .
` This be a pretty kind of tinder-box , if I can get whatever I want like this .
Get me money ! '
he cry to the dog , and hey , presto !
he be off and back again , hold a great purse full of money in his mouth .
Now the Soldier know what a capital tinder-box this be .
If he rub once , the dog that sit on the chest of copper appear ; if he rub twice , there come the dog that watch over the silver chest ; and if he rub three time , the one that guard the gold appear .
Now , the Soldier go down again to his beautiful room , and appear once more in splendid clothes .
All his friend immediately recognise him again , and pay him great court .
One day he think to himself : ` It be very strange that no one can get to see the Princess .
They all say she be very pretty , but what 's the use of that if she have to sit for ever in the great copper castle with all the tower ?
Can I not manage to see her somehow ?
Where be my tinder-box ? '
and so he strike a spark , and , presto !
there come the dog with eye as large a saucer .
` It be the middle of the night , I know , ' say the Soldier ; ` but I should very much like to see the Princess for a moment . '
The dog be already outside the door , and before the Soldier could look round , in he come with the Princess .
She be lie asleep on the dog 's back , and be so beautiful that anyone could see she be a real Princess .
The Soldier really could not refrain from kiss her -- he be such a thorough Soldier .
Then the dog run back with the Princess .
But when it be morning , and the King and Queen be drink tea , the Princess say that the night before she have have such a strange dream about a dog and a Soldier : she have ride on the dog 's back , and the Soldier have kiss her .
` That be certainly a fine story , ' say the Queen .
But the next night one of the lady-in-waiting be to watch at the Princess 's bed , to see if it be only a dream , or if it have actually happen .
The Soldier have an overpower longing to see the Princess again , and so the dog come in the middle of the night and fetch her , run as fast a he could .
But the lady-in-waiting slip on india-rubber shoe and follow them .
When she saw them disappear into a large house , she think to herself : ` Now I know where it be ; ` and make a great cross on the door with a piece of chalk .
Then she go home and lay down , and the dog come back also , with the Princess .
But when he saw that a cross have be make on the door of the house where the Soldier live , he take a piece of chalk also , and make cross on all the door in the town ; and that be very clever , for now the lady-in-waiting could not find the right house , a there be cross on all the door .
Early next morning the King , Queen , lady-in-waiting , and officer come out to see where the Princess have be .
` There it be ! '
say the King , when he saw the first door with a cross on it .
` No , there it be , my dear ! '
say the Queen , when she likewise saw a door with a cross .
` But here be one , and there be another ! '
they all exclaim ; wherever they look there be a cross on the door .
Then they realise that the sign would not help them at all .
But the Queen be an extremely clever woman , who could do a great deal more than just drive in a coach .
She take her great golden scissors , cut up a piece of silk , and make a pretty little bag of it .
This she fill with the fine buckwheat grain , and tie it round the Princess ' neck ; this do , she cut a little hole in the bag , so that the grain would strew the whole road wherever the Princess go .
In the night the dog come again , take the Princess on his back and run away with her to the Soldier , who be very much in love with her , and would have like to have be a Prince , so that he might have have her for his wife .
The dog do not notice how the grain be strewn right from the castle to the Soldier 's window , where he run up the wall with the Princess .
In the morning the King and the Queen saw plainly where their daughter have be , and they take the Soldier and put him into prison .
There he sit .
Oh , how dark and dull it be there !
And they tell him : ` To-morrow you be to be hang . '
Hearing that do not exactly cheer him , and he have leave his tinder-box in the inn .
Next morning he could see through the iron grating in front of his little window how the people be hurry out of the town to see him hang .
He hear the drum and saw the soldier march ; all the people be run to and fro .
Just below his window be a shoemaker 's apprentice , with leather apron and shoe ; he be skip along so merrily that one of his shoe fly off and fell against the wall , just where the Soldier be sit peep through the iron grating .
` Oh , shoemaker 's boy , you need n't be in such a hurry ! '
say the Soldier to him .
` There 's nothing go on till I arrive .
But if you will run back to the house where I live , and fetch me my tinder-box , I will give you four shilling .
But you must put your best foot foremost . '
The shoemaker 's boy be very willing to earn four shilling , and fetch the tinder-box , give it to the Soldier , and -- yes -- now you shall hear .
Outside the town a great scaffold have be erect , and all round be stand the soldier , and hundred of thousand of people .
The King and Queen be sit on a magnificent throne opposite the judge and the whole council .
The Soldier be already stand on the top of the ladder ; but when they want to put the rope round his neck , he say that the fulfilment of one innocent request be always grant to a poor criminal before he undergo his punishment .
He would so much like to smoke a small pipe of tobacco ; it would be his last pipe in this world .
The King could not refuse him this , and so he take out his tinder-box , and rub it once , twice , three time .
And lo , and behold I there stand all three dog -- the one with eye as large a saucer , the second with eye as large a mill-wheels , and the third with eye each as large a the Round Tower of Copenhagen .
` Help me now , so that I may not be hang ! '
cry the Soldier .
And thereupon the dog fell upon the judge and the whole council , seize some by the leg , others by the nose , and throw them so high into the air that they fell and be smash into piece . '
I wo n't stand this ! '
say the King ; but the large dog seize him too , and the Queen as well , and throw them up after the others .
This frighten the soldier , and all the people cry : ` Good Soldier , you shall be our King , and marry the beautiful Princess ! '
Then they put the Soldier into the King 's coach , and the three dog dance in front , cry ` Hurrah ! '
And the boy whistle and the soldier present arm .
The Princess come out of the copper castle , and become Queen ; and that please her very much .
The wedding festivity last for eight day , and the dog sit at table and make eye at everyone .
THE WITCH IN THE STONE BOAT -LRB- 31 -RRB- -LRB- 31 -RRB- From the Icelandic .
There be once a King and a Queen , and they have a son call Sigurd , who be very strong and active , and good-looking .
When the King come to be bow down with the weight of year he speak to his son , and say that now it be time for him to look out for a fitting match for himself , for he do not know how long he might last now , and he would like to see him married before he die .
Sigurd be not averse to this , and ask his father where he think it best to look for a wife .
The King answer that in a certain country there be a King who have a beautiful daughter , and he think it would be most desirable if Sigurd could get her .
So the two part , and Sigurd prepare for the journey , and go to where his father have direct him .
He come to the King and ask his daughter 's hand , which he readily grant him , but only on the condition that he should remain there as long a he could , for the King himself be not strong and not very able to govern his kingdom .
Sigurd accept this condition , but add that he would have to get leave to go home again to his own country when he hear news of his father 's death .
After that Sigurd marry the Princess , and help his father-in-law to govern the kingdom .
He and the Princess love each other dearly , and after a year a son come to them , who be two year old when word come to Sigurd that his father be dead .
Sigurd now prepare to return home with his wife and child , and go on board ship to go by sea .
They have sail for several day , when the breeze suddenly fell , and there come a dead calm , at a time when they need only one day 's voyage to reach home .
Sigurd and his Queen be one day on deck , when most of the others on the ship have fall asleep .
There they sit and talk for a while , and have their little son along with them .
After a time Sigurd become so heavy with sleep that he could no longer keep awake , so he go below and lay down , leave the Queen alone on the deck , play with her son .
A good while after Sigurd have go below the Queen saw something black on the sea , which seem to be come nearer .
As it approach she could make out that it be a boat , and could see the figure of some one sit in it and row it .
At last the boat come alongside the ship , and now the Queen saw that it be a stone boat , out of which there come up on board the ship a fearfully ugly Witch .
The Queen be more frightened than word can describe , and could neither speak a word nor move from the place so a to awaken the King or the sailor .
The Witch come right up to the Queen , take the child from her and lay it on the deck ; then she take the Queen , and strip her of all her fine clothes , which she proceed to put on herself , and look then like a human be .
Last of all she take the Queen , put her into the boat , and say -- ` This spell I lay upon you , that you slacken not your course until you come to my brother in the Underworld . '
The Queen sit stun and motionless , but the boat at once shoot away from the ship with her , and before long she be out of sight .
When the boat could no longer be see the child begin to cry , and though the Witch try to quiet it she could not manage it ; so she go below to where the King be sleep with the child on her arm , and awaken him , scold him for leave them alone on deck , while he and all the crew be asleep .
It be great carelessness of him , she say , to leave no one to watch the ship with her .
Sigurd be greatly surprised to hear his Queen scold him so much , for she have never say an angry word to him before ; but he think it be quite excusable in this case , and try to quiet the child along with her , but it be no use .
Then he go and waken the sailor , and bid them hoist the sail , for a breeze have spring up and be blow straight towards the harbour .
They soon reach the land which Sigurd be to rule over , and find all the people sorrowful for the old King 's death , but they become glad when they get Sigurd back to the Court , and make him King over them .
The King 's son , however , hardly ever stop cry from the time he have be take from his mother on the deck of the ship , although he have always be such a good child before , so that at last the King have to get a nurse for him -- one of the maid of the Court .
As soon a the child get into her charge he stop cry , and behave well a before .
After the sea-voyage it seem to the King that the Queen have alter very much in many way , and not for the good .
He think her much more haughty and stubborn and difficult to deal with than she use to be .
Before long others begin to notice this as well a the King .
In the Court there be two young fellow , one of eighteen year old , the other of nineteen , who be very fond of play chess , and often sit long inside play at it .
Their room be next the Queen 's , and often during the day they hear the Queen talk .
One day they pay more attention than usual when they hear her talk , and put their ear close to a crack in the wall between the room , and hear the Queen say quite plainly , ` When I yawn a little , then I be a nice little maiden ; when I yawn half-way , then I be half a troll ; and when I yawn fully , then I be a troll altogether . '
As she say this she yawn tremendously , and in a moment have put on the appearance of a fearfully ugly troll .
Then there come up through the floor of the room a three-headed Giant with a trough full of meat , who salute her a his sister and set down the trough before her .
She begin to eat out of it , and never stop till she have finish it .
The young fellow saw all this go on , but do not hear the two of them say anything to each other .
They be astonish though at how greedily the Queen devour the meat , and how much she ate of it , and be no longer surprise that she take so little when she sit at table with the King .
As soon a she have finish it the Giant disappear with the trough by the same way a he have come , and the Queen return to her human shape .
Now we must go back to the King 's son after he have be put in charge of the nurse .
One evening , after she have lit a candle and be hold the child , several plank spring up in the floor of the room , and out at the opening come a beautiful woman dress in white , with an iron belt round her waist , to which be fasten an iron chain that go down into the ground .
The woman come up to the nurse , take the child from her , and press it to her breast ; then she give it back to the nurse and return by the same way a she have come , and the floor close over her again .
Although the woman have not speak a single word to her , the nurse be very much frighten , but tell no one about it .
Next even the same thing happen again , just a before , but a the woman be go away she say in a sad tone , ` Two be go , and one only be leave , ' and then disappear a before .
The nurse be still more frightened when she hear the woman say this , and think that perhaps some danger be hang over the child , though she have no ill-opinion of the unknown woman , who , indeed , have behave towards the child a if it be her own .
The most mysterious thing be the woman say ` and only one be leave ; ' but the nurse guess that this must mean that only one day be leave , since she have come for two day already .
At last the nurse make up her mind to go to the King , and tell him the whole story , and ask him to be present in person next day about the time when the woman usually come .
The King promise to do so , and come to the nurse 's room a little before the time , and sit down on a chair with his drawn sword in his hand .
Soon after the plank in the floor spring up a before , and the woman come up , dress in white , with the iron belt and chain .
The King saw at once that it be his own Queen , and immediately hew asunder the iron chain that be fasten to the belt .
This be follow by such noise and crashings down in the earth that all the King 's Palace shook , so that no one expect anything else than to see every bit of it shake to piece .
At last , however , the noise and shake stop , and they begin to come to themselves again .
The King and Queen embrace each other , and she tell him the whole story -- how the Witch come to the ship when they be all asleep and send her off in the boat .
After she have go so far that she could not see the ship , she sail on through darkness until she land beside a three-headed Giant .
The Giant wish her to marry him , but she refuse ; whereupon he shut her up by herself , and tell her she would never get free until she consent .
After a time she begin to plan how to get her freedom , and at last tell him that she would consent if he would allow her to visit her son on earth three day on end .
This he agree to , but put on her this iron belt and chain , the other end of which he fasten round his own waist , and the great noise that be hear when the King cut the chain must have be cause by the Giant 's fall down the underground passage when the chain give way so suddenly .
The Giant 's dwelling , indeed , be right under the Palace , and the terrible shaking must have be cause by him in his death-throes .
The King now understand how the Queen he have have for some time past have be so ill-tempered .
He at once have a sack drawn over her head and make her be stone to death , and after that torn in piece by untamed horse .
The two young fellow also tell now what they have hear and see in the Queen 's room , for before this they have be afraid to say anything about it , on account of the Queen 's power .
The real Queen be now restore to all her dignity , and be beloved by all .
The nurse be marry to a nobleman , and the King and Queen give her splendid present .
THUMBELINA There be once a woman who want to have quite a tiny , little child , but she do not know where to get one from .
So one day she go to an old Witch and say to her : ' I should so much like to have a tiny , little child ; can you tell me where I can get one ? '
` Oh , we have just get one ready ! '
say the Witch .
` Here be a barley-corn for you , but it 's not the kind the farmer sow in his field , or feed the cock and hen with , I can tell you .
Put it in a flower-pot , and then you will see something happen . '
` Oh , thank you ! '
say the woman , and give the Witch a shilling , for that be what it cost .
Then she go home and plant the barley-corn ; immediately there grow out of it a large and beautiful flower , which look like a tulip , but the petal be tightly close a if it be still only a bud .
` What a beautiful flower ! '
exclaim the woman , and she kiss the red and yellow petal ; but a she kiss them the flower burst open .
It be a real tulip , such a one can see any day ; but in the middle of the blossom , on the green velvety petal , sit a little girl , quite tiny , trim , and pretty .
She be scarcely half a thumb in height ; so they call her Thumbelina .
An elegant polish walnut-shell serve Thumbelina a a cradle , the blue petal of a violet be her mattress , and a rose-leaf her coverlid .
There she lay at night , but in the day-time she use to play about on the table ; here the woman have put a bowl , surround by a ring of flower , with their stalk in water , in the middle of which float a great tulip pedal , and on this Thumbelina sit , and sail from one side of the bowl to the other , row herself with two white horse-hairs for oar .
It be such a pretty sight !
She could sing , too , with a voice more soft and sweet than have ever be hear before .
One night , when she be lie in her pretty little bed , an old toad crept in through a broken pane in the window .
She be very ugly , clumsy , and clammy ; she hop on to the table where Thumbelina lay asleep under the red rose-leaf .
` This would make a beautiful wife for my son , ' say the toad , take up the walnut-shell , with Thumbelina inside , and hop with it through the window into the garden .
There flow a great wide stream , with slippery and marshy bank ; here the toad live with her son .
Ugh !
how ugly and clammy he be , just like his mother !
` Croak , croak , croak ! '
be all he could say when he saw the pretty little girl in the walnut-shell .
` Do n't talk so load , or you 'll wake her , ' say the old toad .
` She might escape u even now ; she be as light a a feather .
We will put her at once on a broad water-lily leaf in the stream .
That will be quite an island for her ; she be so small and light .
She ca n't run away from u there , whilst we be prepare the guest-chamber under the marsh where she shall live . '
Outside in the brook grow many water-lilies , with broad green leaf , which look a if they be swim about on the water .
The leaf farthest away be the large , and to this the old toad swam with Thumbelina in her walnut-shell .
The tiny Thumbelina wake up very early in the morning , and when she saw where she be she begin to cry bitterly ; for on every side of the great green leaf be water , and she could not get to the land .
The old toad be down under the marsh , decorate her room with rush and yellow marigold leaf , to make it very grand for her new daughter-in-law ; then she swim out with her ugly son to the leaf where Thumbelina lay .
She want to fetch the pretty cradle to put it into her room before Thumbelina herself come there .
The old toad bow low in the water before her , and say : ` Here be my son ; you shall marry him , and live in great magnificence down under the marsh . '
` Croak , croak , croak ! '
be all that the son could say .
Then they take the neat little cradle and swim away with it ; but Thumbelina sit alone on the great green leaf and wept , for she do not want to live with the clammy toad , or marry her ugly son .
The little fish swim about under the water have see the toad quite plainly , and hear what she have say ; so they put up their head to see the little girl .
When they saw her , they think her so pretty that they be very sorry she should go down with the ugly toad to live .
No ; that must not happen .
They assemble in the water round the green stalk which support the leaf on which she be sit , and nibble the stem in two .
Away float the leaf down the stream , bear Thumbelina far beyond the reach of the toad .
On she sail past several town , and the little bird sit in the bush saw her , and sang , ` What a pretty little girl ! '
The leaf float far and far away ; thus Thumbelina leave her native land .
A beautiful little white butterfly flutter above her , and at last settle on the leaf .
Thumbelina please him , and she , too , be delight , for now the toad could not reach her , and it be so beautiful where she be travel ; the sun shone on the water and make it sparkle like the bright silver .
She take off her sash , and tie one end round the butterfly ; the other end she fasten to the leaf , so that now it glide along with her faster than ever .
A great cockchafer come fly past ; he catch sight of Thumbelina , and in a moment have put his arm round her slender waist , and have fly off with her to a tree .
The green leaf float away down the stream , and the butterfly with it , for he be fasten to the leaf and could not get loose from it .
Oh , dear !
how terrified poor little Thumbelina be when the cockchafer fly off with her to the tree !
But she be especially distress on the beautiful white butterfly 's account , a she have tie him fast , so that if he could not get away he must starve to death .
But the cockchafer do not trouble himself about that ; he sit down with her on a large green leaf , give her the honey out of the flower to eat , and tell her that she be very pretty , although she be n't in the least like a cockchafer .
Later on , all the other cockchafer who live in the same tree come to pay call ; they examine Thumbelina closely , and remark , ` Why , she have only two leg !
How very miserable ! '
` She have no feeler ! '
cry another .
` How ugly she be ! '
say all the lady chafers -- and yet Thumbelina be really very pretty .
The cockchafer who have steal her knew this very well ; but when he hear all the lady say she be ugly , he begin to think so too , and would not keep her ; she might go wherever she like .
So he fly down from the tree with her and put her on a daisy .
There she sit and weep , because she be so ugly that the cockchafer would have nothing to do with her ; and yet she be the most beautiful creature imaginable , so soft and delicate , like the lovely rose-leaf .
The whole summer poor little Thumbelina live alone in the great wood .
She plait a bed for herself of blade of grass , and hang it up under a clover-leaf , so that she be protect from the rain ; she gather honey from the flower for food , and drink the dew on the leaf every morning .
Thus the summer and autumn pass , but then come winter -- the long , cold winter .
All the bird who have sing so sweetly about her have fly away ; the tree shed their leaf , the flower die ; the great clover-leaf under which she have live curl up , and nothing remain of it but the withered stalk .
She be terribly cold , for her clothes be rag , and she herself be so small and thin .
Poor little Thumbelina !
she would surely be frozen to death .
It begin to snow , and every snow-flake that fell on her be to her a a whole shovelful throw on one of u , for we be so big , and she be only an inch high .
She wrapt herself round in a dead leaf , but it be tear in the middle and give her no warmth ; she be tremble with cold .
Just outside the wood where she be now live lay a great corn-field .
But the corn have be go a long time ; only the dry , bare stubble be leave standing in the frozen ground .
This make a forest for her to wander about in .
All at once she come across the door of a field-mouse , who have a little hole under a corn-stalk .
There the mouse live warm and snug , with a store-room full of corn , a splendid kitchen and dining-room .
Poor little Thumbelina go up to the door and beg for a little piece of barley , for she have not have anything to eat for the last two day .
` Poor little creature ! '
say the field-mouse , for she be a kind-hearted old thing at the bottom .
` Come into my warm room and have some dinner with me . '
As Thumbelina please her , she say : ` As far a I be concern you may spend the winter with me ; but you must keep my room clean and tidy , and tell me story , for I like that very much . '
And Thumbelina do all that the kind old field-mouse ask , and do it remarkably well too .
` Now I be expect a visitor , ' say the field-mouse ; ` my neighbour come to call on me once a week .
He be in good circumstance than I be , have great , big room , and wear a fine black-velvet coat .
If you could only marry him , you would be well provide for .
But he be blind .
You must tell him all the pretty story you know . '
But Thumbelina do not trouble her head about him , for he be only a mole .
He come and pay them a visit in his black-velvet coat .
` He be so rich and so accomplished , ' the field-mouse tell her .
` His house be twenty time large than mine ; he possess great knowledge , but he can not bear the sun and the beautiful flower , and speak slightingly of them , for he have never see them . '
Thumbelina have to sing to him , so she sing ` Lady-bird , lady-bird , fly away home ! '
and other song so prettily that the mole fell in love with her ; but he do not say anything , he be a very cautious man .
A short time before he have dig a long passage through the ground from his own house to that of his neighbour ; in this he give the field-mouse and Thumbelina permission to walk as often a they like .
But he beg them not to be afraid of the dead bird that lay in the passage : it be a real bird with beak and feather , and must have die a little time ago , and now lay bury just where he have make his tunnel .
The mole take a piece of rotten wood in his mouth , for that glow like fire in the dark , and go in front , light them through the long dark passage .
When they come to the place where the dead bird lay , the mole put his broad nose against the ceiling and push a hole through , so that the daylight could shine down .
In the middle of the path lay a dead swallow , his pretty wing press close to his side , his claw and head drawn under his feather ; the poor bird have evidently die of cold .
Thumbelina be very sorry , for she be very fond of all little bird ; they have sing and twitter so beautifully to her all through the summer .
But the mole kick him with his bandy leg and say : ` Now he ca n't sing any more !
It must be very miserable to be a little bird !
I 'm thankful that none of my little child be ; bird always starve in winter . '
` Yes , you speak like a sensible man , ' say the field-mouse .
` What have a bird , in spite of all his singing , in the winter-time ?
He must starve and freeze , and that must be very pleasant for him , I must say ! '
Thumbelina do not say anything ; but when the other two have pass on she bend down to the bird , brush aside the feather from his head , and kiss his closed eye gently .
` Perhaps it be he that sing to me so prettily in the summer , ' she think .
` How much pleasure he do give me , dear little bird ! '
The mole close up the hole again which let in the light , and then escort the lady home .
But Thumbelina could not sleep that night ; so she get out of bed , and plait a great big blanket of straw , and carry it off , and spread it over the dead bird , and pile upon it thistle-down as soft a cotton-wool , which she have find in the field-mouse 's room , so that the poor little thing should lie warmly bury .
` Farewell , pretty little bird ! '
she say .
` Farewell , and thank you for your beautiful song in the summer , when the tree be green , and the sun shine down warmly on u ! '
Then she lay her head against the bird 's heart .
But the bird be not dead : he have be frozen , but now that she have warm him , he be come to life again .
In autumn the swallow fly away to foreign land ; but there be some who be late in start , and then they get so cold that they drop down as if dead , and the snow come and cover them over .
Thumbelina tremble , she be so frightened ; for the bird be very large in comparison with herself -- only an inch high .
But she take courage , pile up the down more closely over the poor swallow , fetch her own coverlid and lay it over his head .
Next night she creep out again to him .
There he be alive , but very weak ; he could only open his eye for a moment and look at Thumbelina , who be stand in front of him with a piece of rotten wood in her hand , for she have no other lantern .
` Thank you , pretty little child ! '
say the swallow to her . '
I be so beautifully warm !
Soon I shall regain my strength , and then I shall be able to fly out again into the warm sunshine . '
` Oh ! '
she say , ` it be very cold outside ; it be snow and freeze !
stay in your warm bed ; I will take care of you ! '
Then she bring him water in a petal , which he drink , after which he relate to her how he have tear one of his wing on a bramble , so that he could not fly as fast a the other swallow , who have fly far away to warmer land .
So at last he have drop down exhaust , and then he could remember no more .
The whole winter he remain down there , and Thumbelina look after him and nurse him tenderly .
Neither the mole nor the field-mouse learnt anything of this , for they could not bear the poor swallow .
When the spring come , and the sun warm the earth again , the swallow say farewell to Thumbelina , who open the hole in the roof for him which the mole have make .
The sun shone brightly down upon her , and the swallow ask her if she would go with him ; she could sit upon his back .
Thumbelina want very much to fly far away into the green wood , but she know that the old field-mouse would be sad if she run away .
` No , I must n't come ! '
she say .
` Farewell , dear good little girl ! '
say the swallow , and fly off into the sunshine .
Thumbelina gaze after him with the tear stand in her eye , for she be very fond of the swallow .
` Tweet , tweet ! '
sing the bird , and fly into the green wood .
Thumbelina be very unhappy .
She be not allow to go out into the warm sunshine .
The corn which have be sow in the field over the field-mouse 's home grow up high into the air , and make a thick forest for the poor little girl , who be only an inch high .
` Now you be to be a bride , Thumbelina ! '
say the field-mouse , ` for our neighbour have propose for you !
What a piece of fortune for a poor child like you !
Now you must set to work at your linen for your dowry , for nothing must be lack if you be to become the wife of our neighbour , the mole ! '
Thumbelina have to spin all day long , and every even the mole visit her , and tell her that when the summer be over the sun would not shine so hot ; now it be burn the earth as hard a a stone .
Yes , when the summer have pass , they would keep the wedding .
But she be not at all pleased about it , for she do not like the stupid mole .
Every morning when the sun be rise , and every evening when it be set , she would steal out of the house-door , and when the breeze part the ear of corn so that she could see the blue sky through them , she think how bright and beautiful it must be outside , and long to see her dear swallow again .
But he never come ; no doubt he have fly away far into the great green wood .
By the autumn Thumbelina have finish the dowry .
` In four week you will be marry ! '
say the field-mouse ; ` do n't be obstinate , or I shall bite you with my sharp white teeth !
You will get a fine husband !
The King himself have not such a velvet coat .
His store-room and cellar be full , and you should be thankful for that . '
Well , the wedding-day arrived .
The mole have come to fetch Thumbelina to live with him deep down under the ground , never to come out into the warm sun again , for that be what he do n't like .
The poor little girl be very sad ; for now she must say good-bye to the beautiful sun .
` Farewell , bright sun ! '
she cry , stretch out her arm towards it , and take another step outside the house ; for now the corn have be reap , and only the dry stubble be leave standing .
` Farewell , farewell ! '
she say , and put her arm round a little red flower that grow there .
` Give my love to the dear swallow when you see him ! '
` Tweet , tweet ! '
sound in her ear all at once .
She look up .
There be the swallow fly past !
As soon a he saw Thumbelina , he be very glad .
She tell him how unwilling she be to marry the ugly mole , a then she have to live underground where the sun never shone , and she could not help burst into tear .
` The cold winter be come now , ' say the swallow . '
I must fly away to warmer land : will you come with me ?
You can sit on my back , and we will fly far away from the ugly mole and his dark house , over the mountain , to the warm country where the sun shin more brightly than here , where it be always summer , and there be always beautiful flower .
Do come with me , dear little Thumbelina , who save my life when I lay freeze in the dark tunnel ! '
` Yes , I will go with you , ' say Thumbelina , and get on the swallow 's back , with her foot on one of his outstretched wing .
Up he fly into the air , over wood and sea , over the great mountain where the snow be always lie .
And if she be cold she creep under his warm feather , only keep her little head out to admire all the beautiful thing in the world beneath .
At last they come to warm land ; there the sun be brighter , the sky seem twice as high , and in the hedge hang the fine green and purple grape ; in the wood grow orange and lemon : the air be scent with myrtle and mint , and on the road be pretty little child run about and play with great gorgeous butterfly .
But the swallow flew on farther , and it become more and more beautiful .
Under the most splendid green tree besides a blue lake stand a glitter white-marble castle .
Vines hang about the high pillar ; there be many swallow ' nest , and in one of these live the swallow who be carry Thumbelina .
` Here be my house ! '
say he .
` But it wo n't do for you to live with me ; I be not tidy enough to please you .
Find a home for yourself in one of the lovely flower that grow down there ; now I will set you down , and you can do whatever you like . '
` That will be splendid ! '
say she , clap her little hand .
There lay a great white marble column which have fall to the ground and break into three piece , but between these grow the most beautiful white flower .
The swallow fly down with Thumbelina , and set her upon one of the broad leaf .
But there , to her astonishment , she find a tiny little man sit in the middle of the flower , a white and transparent a if he be make of glass ; he have the pretty golden crown on his head , and the most beautiful wing on his shoulder ; he himself be no big than Thumbelina .
He be the spirit of the flower .
In each blossom there dwell a tiny man or woman ; but this one be the King over the others .
` How handsome he be ! '
whisper Thumbelina to the swallow .
The little Prince be very much frighten at the swallow , for in comparison with one so tiny a himself he seem a giant .
But when he saw Thumbelina , he be delighted , for she be the most beautiful girl he have ever see .
So he take his golden crown from off his head and put it on hers , ask her her name , and if she would be his wife , and then she would be Queen of all the flower .
Yes !
he be a different kind of husband to the son of the toad and the mole with the black-velvet coat .
So she say ` Yes ' to the noble Prince .
And out of each flower come a lady and gentleman , each so tiny and pretty that it be a pleasure to see them .
Each bring Thumbelina a present , but the best of all be a beautiful pair of wing which be fasten on to her back , and now she too could fly from flower to flower .
They all wish her joy , and the swallow sat above in his nest and sing the wedding march , and that he do as well a he could ; but he be sad , because he be very fond of Thumbelina and do not want to be separate from her .
` You shall not be call Thumbelina ! '
say the spirit of the flower to her ; ` that be an ugly name , and you be much too pretty for that .
We will call you May Blossom . '
` Farewell , farewell ! '
say the little swallow with a heavy heart , and fly away to farther land , far , far away , right back to Denmark .
There he have a little nest above a window , where his wife live , who can tell fairy-stories .
` Tweet , tweet ! '
he sing to her .
And that be the way we learn the whole story .
THE NIGHTINGALE In China , a I daresay you know , the Emperor be a Chinaman , and all his courtier be also Chinamen .
The story I be go to tell you happen many year ago , but it be worth while for you to listen to it , before it be forget .
The Emperor 's Palace be the most splendid in the world , all make of priceless porcelain , but so brittle and delicate that you have to take great care how you touch it .
In the garden be the most beautiful flower , and on the lovely of them be tie silver bell which tinkle , so that if you pass you could not help look at the flower .
Everything in the Emperor 's garden be admirably arrange with a view to effect ; and the garden be so large that even the gardener himself do not know where it end .
If you ever get beyond it , you come to a stately forest with great tree and deep lake in it .
The forest slop down to the sea , which be a clear blue .
Large ship could sail under the bough of the tree , and in these tree there live a Nightingale .
She sing so beautifully that even the poor fisherman who have so much to do stood and listen when he come at night to cast his net .
` How beautiful it be ! '
he say ; but he have to attend to his work , and forget about the bird .
But when she sing the next night and the fisherman come there again , he say the same thing , ` How beautiful it be ! '
From all the country round come traveller to the Emperor 's town , who be astonish at the Palace and the garden .
But when they hear the Nightingale they all say , ` This be the fine thing after all ! '
The traveller tell all about it when they go home , and learn scholar write many book upon the town , the Palace , and the garden .
But they do not forget the Nightingale ; she be praise the most , and all the poet compose splendid verse on the Nightingale in the forest by the deep sea .
The book be circulate throughout the world , and some of them reach the Emperor .
He sit in his golden chair , and read and read .
He nod his head every moment , for he like read the brilliant account of the town , the Palace , and the garden .
` But the Nightingale be good than all , ' he saw write .
` What be that ? '
say the Emperor . '
I do n't know anything about the Nightingale !
Is there such a bird in my empire , and so near a in my garden ?
I have never hear it !
Fancy reading for the first time about it in a book ! '
And he call his First Lord to him .
He be so proud that if anyone of low rank than his own ventured to speak to him or ask him anything , he would say nothing but ` P ! '
and that do not mean anything .
` Here be a most remarkable bird which be call a Nightingale ! '
say the Emperor .
` They say it be the most glorious thing in my kingdom .
Why have no one ever say anything to me about it ? ' '
I have never before hear it mention ! '
say the First Lord . '
I will look for it and find it ! '
But where be it to be find ?
The First Lord run up and down stair , through the hall and corridor ; but none of those he meet have ever hear of the Nightingale .
And the First Lord ran again to the Emperor , and tell him that it must be an invention on the part of those who have write the book .
` Your Imperial Majesty can not really believe all that be write !
There be some invention call the Black Art ! '
` But the book in which I read this , ' say the Emperor , ` be send me by His Great Majesty the Emperor of Japan ; so it can not be untrue , and I will hear the Nightingale !
She must be here this evening !
She have my gracious permission to appear , and if she do not , the whole Court shall be trample under foot after supper ! '
` Tsing pe ! '
say the First Lord ; and he run up and down stair , through the hall and corridor , and half the Court run with him , for they do not want to be trample under foot .
Everyone be ask after the wonderful Nightingale which all the world knew of , except those at Court .
At last they meet a poor little girl in the kitchen , who say , ` Oh !
I know the Nightingale well .
How she sing !
I have permission to carry the scrap over from the Court meal to my poor sick mother , and when I be go home at night , tire and weary , and rest for a little in the wood , then I hear the Nightingale singing !
It bring tear to my eye , and I feel a if my mother be kiss me ! '
` Little kitchenmaid ! '
say the First Lord , ' I will give you a place in the kitchen , and you shall have leave to see the Emperor at dinner , if you can lead u to the Nightingale , for she be invite to come to Court this evening . '
And so they all go into the wood where the Nightingale be wont to sing , and half the Court go too .
When they be on the way there they hear a cow mooing .
` Oh ! '
say the Courtiers , ` now we have find her !
What a wonderful power for such a small beast to have !
I be sure we have hear her before ! '
` No ; that be a cow mooing ! '
say the little kitchenmaid .
` We be still a long way off ! '
Then the frog begin to croak in the marsh .
` Splendid ! '
say the Chinese chaplain .
` Now we hear her ; it sound like a little church-bell ! '
` No , no ; those be frogs ! '
say the little kitchenmaid .
` But I think we shall soon hear her now ! '
Then the Nightingale begin to sing .
` There she be ! '
cry the little girl .
` Listen !
She be sit there ! '
And she point to a little dark-grey bird up in the branch .
` Is it possible ! '
say the First Lord . '
I should never have think it !
How ordinary she look !
She must surely have lose her feather because she see so many distinguish men round her ! '
` Little Nightingale , ' call out the little kitchenmaid , ` our Gracious Emperor want you to sing before him ! '
` With the great of pleasure ! '
say the Nightingale ; and she sing so gloriously that it be a pleasure to listen .
` It sound like glass bell ! '
say the First Lord .
` And look how her little throat work !
It be wonderful that we have never hear her before !
She will be a great success at Court . '
` Shall I sing once more for the Emperor ? '
ask the Nightingale , think that the Emperor be there .
` My esteemed little Nightingale , ' say the First Lord , ' I have the great pleasure to invite you to Court this evening , where His Gracious Imperial Highness will be enchant with your charming song ! '
` It sound best in the green wood , ' say the Nightingale ; but still , she come gladly when she hear that the Emperor wish it .
At the Palace everything be splendidly prepared .
The porcelain wall and floor glitter in the light of many thousand gold lamp ; the most gorgeous flower which tinkle out well be place in the corridor .
There be such a hurrying and draught that all the bell jingle so much that one could not hear oneself speak .
In the centre of the great hall where the Emperor sat be a golden perch , on which the Nightingale sat .
The whole Court be there , and the little kitchenmaid be allow to stand behind the door , now that she be a Court-cook .
Everyone be dress in his best , and everyone be look towards the little grey bird to whom the Emperor nod .
The Nightingale sang so gloriously that the tear come into the Emperor 's eye and run down his cheek .
Then the Nightingale sing even more beautifully ; it go straight to all heart .
The Emperor be so delighted that he say she should wear his gold slipper round her neck .
But the Nightingale thank him , and say she have have enough reward already . '
I have see tear in the Emperor 's eye -- that be a great reward .
An Emperor 's tear have such power ! '
Then she sing again with her gloriously sweet voice .
` That be the most charming coquetry I have ever see ! '
say all the lady round .
And they all take to hold water in their mouth that they might gurgle whenever anyone speak to them .
Then they think themselves nightingale .
Yes , the lackey and chambermaid announce that they be please ; which mean a great deal , for they be the most difficult people of all to satisfy .
In short , the Nightingale be a real success .
She have to stay at Court now ; she have her own cage , and permission to walk out twice in the day and once at night .
She be give twelve servant , who each hold a silken string which be fasten round her leg .
There be little pleasure in fly about like this .
The whole town be talk about the wonderful bird , and when two people meet each other one would say ` Nightin , ' and the other ` Gale , ' and then they would both sigh and understand one another .
Yes , and eleven grocer 's child be call after her , but not one of them could sing a note .
One day the Emperor receive a large parcel on which be write ` The Nightingale . '
` Here be another new book about our famous bird ! '
say the Emperor .
But it be not a book , but a little mechanical toy , which lay in a box -- an artificial nightingale which be like the real one , only that it be set all over with diamond , ruby , and sapphire .
When it be wind up , it could sing the piece the real bird sang , and move it tail up and down , and glitter with silver and gold .
Round it neck be a little collar on which be write , ` The Nightingale of the Emperor of Japan be nothing compare to that of the Emperor of China . '
` This be magnificent ! '
they all say , and the man who have bring the clockwork bird receive on the spot the title of ` Bringer of the Imperial First Nightingale . '
` Now they must sing together ; what a duet we shall have ! '
And so they sing together , but their voice do not blend , for the real Nightingale sang in her way and the clockwork bird sang waltz .
` It be not it fault ! '
say the bandmaster ; ` it keep very good time and be quite after my style ! '
Then the artificial bird have to sing alone .
It give just as much pleasure a the real one , and then it be so much pretty to look at ; it sparkle like bracelet and necklace .
Three-and-thirty time it sing the same piece without be tire .
People would like to have hear it again , but the Emperor think that the live Nightingale should sing now -- but where be she ?
No one have notice that she have fly out of the open window away to her green wood .
` What SHALL we do ! '
say the Emperor .
And all the Court scold , and say that the Nightingale be very ungrateful .
` But we have still the best bird ! '
they say and the artificial bird have to sing again , and that be the thirty-fourth time they have hear the same piece .
But they do not yet know it by heart ; it be much too difficult .
And the bandmaster praise the bird tremendously ; yes , he assure them it be well than a real nightingale , not only because of it beautiful plumage and diamond , but inside as well .
` For see , my Lords and Ladies and your Imperial Majesty , with the real Nightingale one can never tell what will come out , but all be know about the artificial bird !
You can explain it , you can open it and show people where the waltzes lie , how they go , and how one follow the other ! '
` That 's just what we think ! '
say everyone ; and the bandmaster receive permission to show the bird to the people the next Sunday .
They should hear it sing , command the Emperor .
And they hear it , and they be as pleased a if they have be intoxicate with tea , after the Chinese fashion , and they all say ` Oh ! '
and hold up their forefinger and nodded time .
But the poor fisherman who have hear the real Nightingale say : ` This one sing well enough , the tune glide out ; but there be something want -- I do n't know what ! '
The real Nightingale be banish from the kingdom .
The artificial bird be put on silken cushion by the Emperor 's bed , all the present which it receive , gold and precious stone , lay round it , and it be give the title of Imperial Night-singer , First from the left .
For the Emperor count that side a the more distinguished , be the side on which the heart be ; the Emperor 's heart be also on the left .
And the bandmaster write a work of twenty-five volume about the artificial bird .
It be so learned , long , and so full of the hard Chinese word that everyone say they have read it and understand it ; for once they have be very stupid about a book , and have be trample under foot in consequence .
So a whole year pass .
The Emperor , the Court , and all the Chinese knew every note of the artificial bird 's song by heart .
But they like it all the good for this ; they could even sing with it , and they do .
The street boy sing ` Tra-la-la-la-la , and the Emperor sing too sometimes .
It be indeed delightful .
But one evening , when the artificial bird be sing it best , and the Emperor lay in bed listening to it , something in the bird go crack .
Something snap !
Whir-r-r !
all the wheel run down and then the music cease .
The Emperor spring up , and have his physician summon , but what could HE do !
Then the clockmaker come , and , after a great deal of talk and examining , he put the bird somewhat in order , but he say that it must be very seldom use a the work be nearly wear out , and it be impossible to put in new one .
Here be a calamity !
Only once a year be the artificial bird allow to sing , and even that be almost too much for it .
But then the bandmaster make a little speech full of hard word , say that it be just as good a before .
And so , of course , it WAS just as good a before .
So five year pass , and then a great sorrow come to the nation .
The Chinese look upon their Emperor a everything , and now he be ill , and not likely to live it be say .
Already a new Emperor have be choose , and the people stand outside in the street and ask the First Lord how the old Emperor be .
` P ! '
say he , and shake his head .
Cold and pale lay the Emperor in his splendid great bed ; the whole Court believe him dead , and one after the other leave him to pay their respect to the new Emperor .
Everywhere in the hall and corridor cloth be lay down so that no footstep could be hear , and everything be still -- very , very still .
And nothing come to break the silence .
The Emperor long for something to come and relieve the monotony of this deathlike stillness .
If only someone would speak to him !
If only someone would sing to him .
Music would carry his thought away , and would break the spell lie on him .
The moon be stream in at the open window ; but that , too , be silent , quite silent .
` Music !
music ! '
cry the Emperor .
` You little bright golden bird , sing !
do sing !
I give you gold and jewel ; I have hang my gold slipper round your neck with my own hand -- sing !
do sing ! '
But the bird be silent .
There be no one to wind it up , and so it could not sing .
And all be silent , so terribly silent !
All at once there come in at the window the most glorious burst of song .
It be the little living Nightingale , who , sit outside on a bough , have hear the need of her Emperor and have come to sing to him of comfort and hope .
And a she sing the blood flow quick and quicker in the Emperor 's weak limb , and life begin to return .
` Thank you , thank you ! '
say the Emperor .
` You divine little bird !
I know you .
I chase you from my kingdom , and you have give me life again !
How can I reward you ? '
` You have do that already ! '
say the Nightingale . '
I bring tear to your eye the first time I sing .
I shall never forget that .
They be jewel that rejoice a singer 's heart .
But now sleep and get strong again ; I will sing you a lullaby . '
And the Emperor fell into a deep , calm sleep a she sing .
The sun be shin through the window when he awake , strong and well .
None of his servant have come back yet , for they think he be dead .
But the Nightingale sat and sang to him .
` You must always stay with me ! '
say the Emperor .
` You shall sing whenever you like , and I will break the artificial bird into a thousand piece . '
` Do n't do that ! '
say the Nightingale .
` He do his work as long a he could .
Keep him a you have do !
I can not build my nest in the Palace and live here ; but let me come whenever I like .
I will sit in the evening on the bough outside the window , and I will sing you something that will make you feel happy and grateful .
I will sing of joy , and of sorrow ; I will sing of the evil and the good which lie hide from you .
The little singing-bird fly all around , to the poor fisherman 's hut , to the farmer 's cottage , to all those who be far away from you and your Court .
I love your heart more than your crown , though that have about it a brightness a of something holy .
Now I will sing to you again ; but you must promise me one thing -- ' ` Anything ! '
say the Emperor , stand up in his Imperial robe , which he have himself put on , and fasten on his sword richly emboss with gold .
` One thing I beg of you !
Do n't tell anyone that you have a little bird who tell you everything .
It will be much well not to ! '
Then the Nightingale fly away .
The servant come in to look at their dead Emperor .
The Emperor say , ` Good-morning ! '
HERMOD AND HADVOR -LRB- 32 -RRB- -LRB- 32 -RRB- From the Icelandic .
Once upon a time there be a King and a Queen who have an only daughter , call Hadvor , who be fair and beautiful , and be an only child , be heir to the kingdom .
The King and Queen have also a foster son , name Hermod , who be just about the same age a Hadvor , and be good-looking , as well a clever at most thing .
Hermod and Hadvor often play together while they be child , and like each other so much that while they be still young they secretly plight their troth to each other .
As time go on the Queen fell sick , and suspect that it be her last illness , send for the King to come to her .
When he come she tell him that she have no long time to live , and therefore wish to ask one thing of him , which be , that if he marry another wife he should promise to take no other one than the Queen of Hetland the Good .
The King give the promise , and thereafter the Queen die .
Time go past , and the King , grow tire of live alone , fit out his ship and sail out to sea .
As he sail there come upon him so thick a mist that he altogether lose his bearing , but after long trouble he find land .
There he lay his ship to , and go on shore all alone .
After walk for some time he come to a forest , into which he go a little way and stop .
Then he hear sweet music from a harp , and go in the direction of the sound until he come to a clearing , and there he saw three woman , one of whom sit on a golden chair , and be beautifully and grandly dress ; she hold a harp in her hand , and be very sorrowful .
The second be also finely dress , but young in appearance , and also sit on a chair , but it be not so grand a the first one 's .
The third stood beside them , and be very pretty to look at ; she have a green cloak over her other clothes , and it be easy to see that she be maid to the other two .
After the King have look at them for a little he go forward and salute them .
The one that sit on the golden chair ask him who he be and where he be go ; and he tell her all the story -- how he be a king , and have lose his queen , and be now on his way to Hetland the Good , to ask the Queen of that country in marriage .
She answer that fortune have contrive this wonderfully , for pirate have plunder Hetland and kill the King , and she have flee from the land in terror , and have come hither after great trouble , and she be the very person he be look for , and the others be her daughter and maid .
The King immediately ask her hand ; she gladly receive his proposal and accept him at once .
Thereafter they all set out , and make their way to the ship ; and after that nothing be tell of their voyage until the King reach his own country .
There he make a great feast , and celebrate his marriage with this woman ; and after that thing be quiet for a time .
Hermod and Hadvor take but little notice of the Queen and her daughter , but , on the other hand , Hadvor and the Queen 's maid , whose name be Olof , be very friendly , and Olof come often to visit Hadvor in her castle .
Before long the King go out to war , and no sooner be he away than the Queen come to talk with Hermod , and say that she want him to marry her daughter .
Hermod tell her straight and plain that he would not do so , at which the Queen grow terribly angry , and say that in that case neither should he have Hadvor , for she would now lay this spell on him , that he should go to a desert island and there be a lion by day and a man by night .
He should also think always of Hadvor , which would cause him all the more sorrow , and from this spell he should never be free until Hadvor burn the lion 's skin , and that would not happen very soon .
As soon a the Queen have finish her speech Hermod reply that he also lay a spell on her , and that be , that as soon a he be free from her enchantment she should become a rat and her daughter a mouse , and fight with each other in the hall until he kill them with his sword .
After this Hermod disappear , and no one know what have become of him ; the Queen cause search to be make for him , but he could nowhere be find .
One time , when Olof be in the castle beside Hadvor , she ask the Princess if she know where Hermod have go to .
At this Hadvor become very sad , and say that she do not . '
I shall tell you then , ' say Olof , ` for I know all about it .
Hermod have disappear through the wicked device of the Queen , for she be a witch , and so be her daughter , though they have put on these beautiful form .
Because Hermod would not fall in with the Queen 's plan , and marry her daughter , she have lay a spell on him , to go on an island and be a lion by day and a man by night , and never be free from this until you burn the lion 's skin .
Besides , ' say Olof , ` she have look out a match for you ; she have a brother in the Underworld , a three-headed Giant , whom she mean to turn into a beautiful prince and get him marry to you .
This be no new thing for the Queen ; she take me away from my parent ' house and compel me to serve her ; but she have never do me any harm , for the green cloak I wear protects me against all mischief .
Hadvor now become still sad than before at the thought of the marriage destine for her , and entreat Olof to think of some plan to save her . '
I think , ' say Olof , ` that your wooer will come up through the floor of the castle to you , and so you must be prepare when you hear the noise of his come and the floor begin to open , and have at hand blaze pitch , and pour plenty of it into the opening .
That will prove too much for him . '
About this time the King come home from his expedition , and think it a great blow that no one know what have become of Hermod ; but the Queen console him a best she could , and after a time the King thought less about his disappearance .
Hadvor remain in her castle , and have make preparation to receive her wooer when he come .
One night , not long after , a loud noise and rumbling be hear under the castle .
Hadvor at once guess what it be , and tell her maid to be ready to help her .
The noise and thundering grow loud and louder , until the floor begin to open , whereupon Hadvor make them take the caldron of pitch and pour plenty of it into the opening .
With that the noise grow fainter and fainter , till at last they cease altogether .
Next morning the Queen rise early , and go out to the Palace gate , and there she find her brother the Giant lie dead .
She go up to him and say , ' I pronounce this spell , that you become a beautiful prince , and that Hadvor shall be unable to say anything against the charge that I shall bring against her . '
The body of the dead Giant now become that of a beautiful prince , and the Queen go in again . '
I do n't think , ' say she to the King , ` that your daughter be as good a she be say to be .
My brother come and ask her hand , and she have have him put to death .
I have just find his dead body lie at the Palace gate . '
The King go along with the Queen to see the body , and think it all very strange ; so beautiful a youth , he say , would have be a worthy match for Hadvor , and he would readily have agree to their marriage .
The Queen ask leave to decide what Hadvor 's punishment should be , which the King be very willing to allow , so a to escape from punish his own daughter .
The Queen 's decision be that the King should make a big grave-mound for her brother , and put Hadvor into it beside him .
Olof know all the plan of the Queen , and go to tell the Princess what have be do , whereupon Hadvor earnestly entreat her to tell her what to do .
` First and foremost , ' say Olof , ` you must get a wide cloak to wear over your other clothes , when you be put into the mound .
The Giant 's ghost will walk after you be both left together in there , and he will have two dog along with him .
He will ask you to cut piece out of his leg to give to the dog , but that you must not promise to do unless he tell you where Hermod have go to , and tell you how to find him .
He will then let you stand on his shoulder , so a to get out of the mound ; but he mean to cheat you all the same , and will catch you by the cloak to pull you back again ; but you must take care to have the cloak loose on your shoulder , so that he will only get hold of that . '
The mound be all ready now , and the Giant laid in it , and into it Hadvor also have to go without be allow to make any defence .
After they be both leave there everything happen just a Olof have say .
The prince become a Giant again , and ask Hadvor to cut the piece out of his leg for the dog ; but she refuse until he tell her that Hermod be in a desert island , which she could not reach unless she take the skin off the sol of his foot and make shoe out of that ; with these shoe she could travel both on land and sea .
This Hadvor now do , and the Giant then let her get up on his shoulder to get out of the mound .
As she spring out he catch hold of her cloak ; but she have take care to let it lie loose on her shoulder , and so escaped .
She now make her way down to the sea , to where she know there be the short distance over to the island in which Hermod be .
This strait she easily cross , for the shoe keep her up .
On reach the island she find a sandy beach all along by the sea , and high cliff above .
Nor could she see any way to get up these , and so , be both sad at heart and tire with the long journey , she lay down and fell asleep .
As she sleep she dream that a tall woman come to her and say , ' I know that you be Princess Hadvor , and be search for Hermod .
He be on this island ; but it will be hard for you to get to him if you have no one to help you , for you can not climb the cliff by your own strength .
I have therefore let down a rope , by which you will be able to climb up ; and a the island be so large that you might not find Hermod 's dwelling-place so easily , I lay down this clew beside you .
You need only hold the end of the thread , and the clew will run on before and show you the way .
I also lay this belt beside you , to put on when you awaken ; it will keep you from grow faint with hunger . '
The woman now disappear , and Hadvor wake , and saw that all her dream have be true .
The rope hang down from the cliff , and the clew and belt lay beside her .
The belt she put on , the rope enable her to climb up the cliff , and the clew lead her on till she come to the mouth of a cave , which be not very big .
She go into the cave , and saw there a low couch , under which she creep and lay down .
When even come she hear the noise of footstep outside , and become aware that the lion have come to the mouth of the cave , and shake itself there , after which she hear a man come towards the couch .
She be sure this be Hermod , because she hear him speak to himself about his own condition , and call to mind Hadvor and other thing in the old day .
Hadvor make no sign , but wait till he have fall asleep , and then creep out and burn the lion 's skin , which he have leave outside .
Then she go back into the cave and waken Hermod , and they have a most joyful meeting .
In the morning they talk over their plan , and be most at a loss to know how to get out of the island .
Hadvor tell Hermod her dream , and say she suspect there be some one in the island who would be able to help them .
Hermod say he know of a Witch there , who be very ready to help anyone , and that the only plan be to go to her .
So they go to the Witch 's cave , and find her there with her fifteen young son , and ask her to help them to get to the mainland .
` There be other thing easy than that , ' say she , ` for the Giant that be bury will be wait for you , and will attack you on the way , a he have turn himself into a big whale .
I shall lend you a boat , however , and if you meet the whale and think your life be in danger , then you can name me by name . '
