They thank her greatly for her help and advice , and set out from the island , but on the way they saw a huge fish come towards them , with great splashing and dashing of wave .
They be sure of what it be , and think they have a good reason a ever they would have to call on the Witch , and so they do .
The next minute they saw come after them another huge whale , follow by fifteen small one .
All of these swam past the boat and go on to meet the whale .
There be a fierce battle then , and the sea become so stormy that it be not very easy to keep the boat from be fill by the wave .
After this fight have go on for some time , they saw that the sea be dye with blood ; the big whale and the fifteen small one disappear , and they get to land safe and sound .
Now the story go back to the King 's hall , where strange thing have happen in the meantime .
The Queen and her daughter have disappear , but a rat and a mouse be always fight with each other there .
Ever so many people have try to drive them away , but no one could manage it .
Thus some time go on , while the King be almost beside himself with sorrow and care for the loss of his Queen , and because these monster destroy all mirth in the hall .
One evening , however , while they all sit dull and down-hearted , in come Hermod with a sword by his side , and salute the King , who receive him with the great joy , a if he have come back from the dead .
Before Hermod sit down , however , he go to where the rat and the mouse be fight , and cut them in two with his sword .
All be astonish then by see two witch lie dead on the floor of the hall .
Hermod now tell the whole story to the King , who be very glad to be rid of such vile creature .
Next he ask for the hand of Hadvor , which the King readily give him , and be now an old man , give the kingdom to him as well ; and so Hermod become King .
Olof marry a good-looking nobleman , and that be the end of the story .
THE STEADFAST TIN-SOLDIER There be once upon a time five-and twenty tin-soldiers -- all brother , a they be make out of the same old tin spoon .
Their uniform be red and blue , and they shoulder their gun and look straight in front of them .
The first word that they hear in this world , when the lid of the box in which they lay be take off , be : ` Hurrah , tin-soldiers ! '
This be exclaim by a little boy , clap his hand ; they have be give to him because it be his birthday , and now he begin set them out on the table .
Each soldier be exactly like the other in shape , except just one , who have be make last when the tin have run short ; but there he stand a firmly on his one leg a the others do on two , and he be the one that become famous .
There be many other plaything on the table on which they be be set out , but the nice of all be a pretty little castle make of cardboard , with window through which you could see into the room .
In front of the castle stand some little tree surround a tiny mirror which look like a lake .
Wax swan be float about and reflect themselves in it .
That be all very pretty ; but the most beautiful thing be a little lady , who stand in the open doorway .
She be cut out of paper , but she have on a dress of the fine muslin , with a scarf of narrow blue ribbon round her shoulder , fasten in the middle with a glittering rise make of gold paper , which be as large a her head .
The little lady be stretch out both her arm , for she be a Dancer , and be lift up one leg so high in the air that the Tin-soldier could n't find it anywhere , and think that she , too , have only one leg .
` That 's the wife for me ! '
he think ; ` but she be so grand , and live in a castle , whilst I have only a box with four-and-twenty others .
This be no place for her !
But I must make her acquaintance . '
Then he stretch himself out behind a snuff-box that lay on the table ; from thence he could watch the dainty little lady , who continue to stand on one leg without lose her balance .
When the night come all the other tin-soldiers go into their box , and the people of the house go to bed .
Then the toy begin to play at visiting , dancing , and fighting .
The tin-soldiers rattle in their box , for they want to be out too , but they could not raise the lid .
The nut-crackers play at leap-frog , and the slate-pencil ran about the slate ; there be such a noise that the canary wake up and begin to talk to them , in poetry too !
The only two who do not stir from their place be the Tin-soldier and the little Dancer .
She remain on tip-toe , with both arm outstretched ; he stand steadfastly on his one leg , never move his eye from her face .
The clock strike twelve , and crack !
off fly the lid of the snuff-box ; but there be no snuff inside , only a little black imp -- that be the beauty of it .
` Hullo , Tin-soldier ! '
say the imp .
` Do n't look at thing that be n't intend for the like of you ! '
But the Tin-soldier take no notice , and seem not to hear .
` Very well , wait till to-morrow ! '
say the imp .
When it be morning , and the child have get up , the Tin-soldier be put in the window ; and whether it be the wind or the little black imp , I do n't know , but all at once the window fly open and out fell the little Tin-soldier , head over heel , from the third-storey window !
That be a terrible fall , I can tell you !
He land on his head with his leg in the air , his gun be wedge between two paving-stones .
The nursery-maid and the little boy come down at once to look for him , but , though they be so near him that they almost tread on him , they do not notice him .
If the Tin-soldier have only call out ` Here I be ! '
they must have find him ; but he do not think it fit for him to cry out , because he have on his uniform .
Soon it begin to drizzle ; then the drop come faster , and there be a regular down-pour .
When it be over , two little street boy come along .
` Just look ! '
cried one .
` Here be a Tin-soldier !
He shall sail up and down in a boat ! '
So they make a little boat out of newspaper , put the Tin-soldier in it , and make him sail up and down the gutter ; both the boy run along beside him , clap their hand .
What great wave there be in the gutter , and what a swift current !
The paper-boat toss up and down , and in the middle of the stream it go so quick that the Tin-soldier tremble ; but he remain steadfast , show no emotion , look straight in front of him , shoulder his gun .
All at once the boat pass under a long tunnel that be as dark a his box have be .
` Where can I be come now ? '
he wonder .
` Oh , dear !
This be the black imp 's fault !
Ah , if only the little lady be sit beside me in the boat , it might be twice a dark for all I should care ! '
Suddenly there come along a great water-rat that live in the tunnel .
` Have you a passport ? '
ask the rat .
` Out with your passport ! '
But the Tin-soldier be silent , and grasp his gun more firmly .
The boat speed on , and the rat behind it .
Ugh !
how he show his teeth , a he cry to the chip of wood and straw : ` Hold him , hold him !
he have not pay the toll !
He have not show his passport ! '
But the current become swifter and strong .
The Tin-soldier could already see daylight where the tunnel end ; but in his ear there sound a roaring enough to frighten any brave man .
Only think !
at the end of the tunnel the gutter discharge itself into a great canal ; that would be just as dangerous for him a it would be for u to go down a waterfall .
Now he be so near to it that he could not hold on any long .
On go the boat , the poor Tin-soldier keep himself as stiff a he could : no one should say of him afterwards that he have flinch .
The boat whirl three , four time round , and become fill to the brim with water : it begin to sink !
The Tin-soldier be stand up to his neck in water , and deep and deep sink the boat , and soft and soft grow the paper ; now the water be over his head .
He be think of the pretty little Dancer , whose face he should never see again , and there sound in his ear , over and over again : ` Forward , forward , soldier bold !
Death 's before thee , grim and cold ! '
The paper come in two , and the soldier fell -- but at that moment he be swallow by a great fish .
Oh !
how dark it be inside , even dark than in the tunnel , and it be really very close quarter !
But there the steadfast little Tin-soldier lay full length , shoulder his gun .
Up and down swim the fish , then he make the most dreadful contortion , and become suddenly quite still .
Then it be a if a flash of lightning have pass through him ; the daylight stream in , and a voice exclaim , ` Why , here be the little Tin-soldier ! '
The fish have be catch , take to market , sell , and bring into the kitchen , where the cook have cut it open with a great knife .
She take up the soldier between her finger and thumb , and carry him into the room , where everyone want to see the hero who have be find inside a fish ; but the Tin-soldier be not at all proud .
They put him on the table , and -- no , but what strange thing do happen in this world !
-- the Tin-soldier be in the same room in which he have be before !
He saw the same child , and the same toy on the table ; and there be the same grand castle with the pretty little Dancer .
She be still stand on one leg with the other high in the air ; she too be steadfast .
That touch the Tin-soldier , he be nearly go to shed tin-tears ; but that would not have be fit for a soldier .
He look at her , but she say nothing .
All at once one of the little boy take up the Tin-soldier , and throw him into the stove , give no reason ; but doubtless the little black imp in the snuff-box be at the bottom of this too .
There the Tin-soldier lay , and felt a heat that be truly terrible ; but whether he be suffer from actual fire , or from the ardour of his passion , he do not know .
All his colour have disappear ; whether this have happen on his travel or whether it be the result of trouble , who can say ?
He look at the little lady , she look at him , and he felt that he be melt ; but he remain steadfast , with his gun at his shoulder .
Suddenly a door open , the draught catch up the little Dancer , and off she fly like a sylph to the Tin-soldier in the stove , burst into flame -- and that be the end of her !
Then the Tin-soldier melt down into a little lump , and when next morning the maid be take out the ash , she find him in the shape of a heart .
There be nothing left of the little Dancer but her gilt rise , burnt as black a a cinder .
